* * *



Track 1: What Could Kane Hailand Have Tattooed On His Forehead?


Kane Hailand drove through concrete highways with a senseless tattoo plastered across his forehead.  He thought only of how much change the land had seen- the metal signage refracting warnings of perpetual road construction, the matrix of tail-lights glowing red to light the scrutinized skyline, cars blaring horns like curses unto their fellow vehicles, billboards lit to promote everything from diamond jewelry and chewing gum to sexual safety.  There were so many lights- everything was so visible, observable, so permanent and public.  Then there was the billboard with Kane's face on it.

Lit high in the firmament above all other billboards, Kane Hailand's image observed the metropolis while wearing a winking eyepatch and a Jester's hat, sandwiched between the one he loved and the one she loved.  Sooner or later they make a monkey out of all of us- dress us up and make us dance.

Kane ignored the radio's rolling vocal lilts until he heard his own name sound from the dashboard in the emcee's introduction to a song Kane Hailand wrote during his stint in the greatest musical trio the world had ever known.  The song, From Darkness, was recorded on a handheld cassette player during a weeklong blackout.  The lyrics explore the birth of music as the piano and the singer slowly ascend from their lowest notes to culminate in the amazing screech of musical light at the high end of their respective instruments.  The song was treasured among Scoundrels fans for its live performances, in which the band and all their fans wore blindfolds.  When the singer hit her famous high note, a remarkable and orotund A6, every being in presence stepped out of the blackness of their blindfolds to behold Kane Hailand's godlike silhouette in a glorious beam of light- the sensation was as powerful as birth.

The Scoundrels were the most talented trio of individuals to ever commit life to a record, but they never matched the caliber of their first-ever piece- Train of Power.  Kane Hailand believes this is because perfection has no equal.  His younger self knew every secret in the universe with an architect's certainty, but he abandoned those secrets in the abysmal recesses of time- truth, he knew in youth, and then forgot.  Driving into the violent wind with no destination was the only way for Kane to run from his self.

Kane turned off the dial.  To anyone else, coasting smooth at 99 mph over the American highway while getting lost to Scoundrels tunes would have rung paradise, but to Kane Hailand it was global prison.  Lackluster-eyed Kane Hailand had been bent over and defeated.

Kane Hailand was God until he destroyed the world.  The Creator of the universe, Adonai, Yahweh, Jah, the One- Kane Hailand.  None of these names suit him as he is now, driving through someone else's world with a tattoo on his forehead.  What is God to do when eternity expires?

Kane prepared to challenge his will and take a brash leap into one of two freedoms- he'll either die or he won't.  The shame about music is that their gods die too young.

Twisting the rearview, Kane lifted his wool cap, the only remaining artifact from his political days, stitched with the snaggle-toothed guise of Geronimo, the 9-legged octopus who served as mascot for the Violet 9.  Kane examined the violet tattoo on his forehead, only readable when reversed through mirror.  His mind dove and drowned in memory.

* * *

Approximately eighteen months after his university loft mysteriously exploded (arson was never suspected), Kane Hailand and his roommate were taking a hiatus from recording their first album, I am the Jester, O yea, O yea, because Kane's roommate was on another drug binge.  Kane handed a sugar pill to his roommate.

Roommate:  What is this, cyanide?

Kane:  Yes.  I'm trying to kill you.

The roommate swallowed the pill.  Minutes later, the two began a competition to determine who could eat Chinese food faster.

Dressed primly in a blue military tunic, a treble clef epaulet on his right shoulder and a bass clef on his left, Kane's appearance was blinding.  Blue bells jangled from his brass cuffs, his blue hair was cropped to expose his ears, and the twin sides of his mustache mirrored each other as hands preparing to pray.  His crystalline collar controlled the light spectrum as the four ears of his blue-tinted Jester's hat flopped to their own accord.  A hand-painted blue eye-patch covered his left eye so that his masked eye would always be gazing into a blue infinity.  Sun King, his pet bluebird, nibbled tactfully at his beef lo mein.

The roommate astounded in a red three-piece suit, both breasts emblazoned with an initial- HA.  He had heavy bags under his eyes from night terrors and wrathful sermonizing.  A red top hat floated above his skull like dust in a moonbeam.  His red hair tangled over his shoulders and he wore an eye-mask made of red feathers plucked from the mythological phoenix.  Fire heated the souls of his red boots, the same fire that burns within a man in a ring who thrives off the adrenaline.

Kane manipulated his chopsticks with furious dexterity while the roommate plunged a fork into his carryout container.  If there was a piano beneath the roommate's fingers then his hands would produce cities of sound, but his stiff fingers were incapable of handling chopsticks when removed from the piano.

Kane and his roommate challenged each other, glaring as they devoured.  The roommate flashed his red eyes, snarling his patented devilish snarl, brow formed in an inverted question mark beneath his red-feathered mask.  He poured hot sauce into his custom-made red takeout container.  Kane grew up an orphan, yet he somehow found a roommate who was born a diva with custom-made takeout containers.  Through all their competitions, Kane never once witnessed his roommate allow a bite past his lips without hot sauce.  In between bites, the roommate downed liquor.  He claimed that he drank because liquor lubricates the throat better than water, thus allowing him to gain a competitive edge against Kane in their Chinese Food game of war- all addicts make excuses.

Their battle, as always, was deflected toward the immortal entrance of the roommate's girlfriend.

Gorgeous tresses dyed violet spilled over her slender shoulders, her once-sapphire eyes sunken from the cigarettes.  She saw the world through a violet scale with colored contact lens. Violet is the only color, she used to say.  She wore a tight-fitting violet coat made from violet petals, nothing underneath.  Kane watched his roommate's girlfriend pass his roommate breaths of violet smoke through her kiss.  She retrieved a violet bandana from one of the 9 pockets sewn to the inside of her flowery coat, knotting the garment over her boyfriend's red-feathered mask to suppress the red flames of his eyes.  To access her inside pockets, it was necessary that she loosen all 9 of her coat's buttons with the gentlest of care so as to ensure the protection of the violet-pedaled coat.  The buttons were made from the eye of the violet.  Coolly, she opened the flap of her coat to expose a naked breast.  Kane watched.  She wanted Kane to watch.  She used to be such a sweetheart- innocent, virginal.  He couldn't blame her for what she was about to do- the roommate got what he had coming.  They all did.

She cleared the empty takeout boxes from the table and laid the following arrangement from the contents of her 9 coat pockets- a sewing needle, a spool of violet thread, a mechanical pencil, a printer cartridge that she had emptied and refilled with home-made violet ink, and, as always, her violet monogrammed cigarette case, custom-made to fit 9 cigarettes, hand-rolled with the violet paper she had dipped in perfume to smell like violets.  The length of the cigarettes equaled the accumulated length of her 9 violet fingernails- she abhorred the metric system.  She peppered the tobacco with solvent violet 13, which Kane and his roommate had stolen from the university's chemistry annex.  The solvent, when lit, produced a violet-colored smoke.  These were the chemicals she put in her lungs.

She removed a violet-plated .9mm pistol from her coat.

Roommate:  You carry a gun now?

Girlfriend:  Sit back, honey.

She set the violet pistol on the table.  This pistol would one day render her the only performer ever to fire a gun in Carnegie Hall- the drunken pianist fell asleep while playing her accompaniment, and she woke him with a violet bullet in the leg of his mad red piano.

The girlfriend rolled the sleeve of the roommate's red suit to his elbow, using the violet thread to tie his arm to the chair.  She held the needle next to the tip of the mechanical pencil so that a half-inch of metal poked free into the air like a bayonet.  Holding the pencil and the needle in this position, she wound the thread counterclockwise around the two objects.  At this point, Kane recalls a lascivious violet wink from her beautiful eye.  He watched as she wrapped the thread, twisting her violet polished fingers above the mechanical pencil, neatly around the needle, spiraling to the silver point that would forever stain.  The girlfriend plugged her blindfolded boyfriend's ears with two polished fingers.  Through 9 intermittent violet lipstick kisses on the roommate's blind face, she puffed her violet smoke and spoke to Kane.

Girlfriend:   The thread soaks the ink (kiss).  You wind the thread as close (kiss) as (kiss) possible (kiss) to the tip of the needle (kiss).  That way (kiss), you don't have to stick it so far into the skin (kiss).  As much as I would like to let our boy here (kiss) ride the pain (kiss), he wouldn't be able to handle it.

She kissed her blindfolded boyfriend hard on the mouth as she groped inside his red suit pocket for a lighter.  For sterilization, she held the exposed eye of the needle under the red flame, and to this day that fire burns in Kane's memory as the eternal torch of retribution.

The girlfriend sucked her violet-polished finger and thumbed saliva across her boyfriend's open forearm in an animal act of cleaning.  She lifted her crafted mechanism and dipped the sterilized needle into the open ink cartridge.  When she withdrew the needle from the ink, she pointed it toward the ceiling so Kane could watch in silence as the ink bled down the thread.  And Kane watched it bleed- violet blood trickling through the thread as he trapped a large bite of beef lo mein between his chopsticks.

Kane Hailand snuck an advantage in his Chinese Food Game of War while he watched her prick a homemade needle into his roommate's arm.  Kane had no wish to come between them.  That's a lie.  The roommate snarled his devilish snarl and occasionally inquired to discover what it was that his girlfriend was doing to his tied up arm that caused such sexy pain.  She paused to snatch the red top hat from the roommate's head, allowing his tangled red hair to shine.  After a spectacle of inked stabbing so precisely intense that Kane imagined he could feel it, the girlfriend raised her hand-made mechanism from her boyfriend's tied-up arm.  She spoke.  Kane imagined whatever she said to be directed more toward him than to her blindfolded boyfriend.

Girlfriend:  I want you to see it.  But I have to wash it first.  Wash well.  It's very important to wash well.

That was Kane's favorite part.  Wash well.  Defile the body in an ordered chaos of controlled hysteria, but be sure to wash it well.  Wipe it clean, dust the remnants of madness and expose the finished craft to the world.  She lifted an inky cloth from her boyfriend's arm and she told Kane to have a look.  The roommate shouted hurriedly as he always shouted hurriedly because he believed speech to be a waste of time.

Blindfolded Roommate:  Why should Kane get to see it first?  Let me see.

Girlfriend:  I wanna see Jake's reaction.  I wanna see it in his face.

Roommate:  Stop calling him Jake.  He's Kane now.

The girlfriend rose from her chair and lifted Kane's eye-patch, kissing him gently on the eyelid.  In a trice, Kane's left eye went from peering into the blue infinity of his eye-patch to the soft and moist universe of her violet puckered lips.

Girlfriend (in Kane's ear):  I just shared more with you than he ever would with me.  Thank you.

She walked out the door for the first time, leaving behind a violet inked signature on Kane's roommate's forearm of the 9 figures she felt best embodied the experience they shared-SCOUNDREL.  It was the only thing she ever did for herself.  As for Kane's first taste of heaven in the home of her kiss- well, that was for all three of them.

* * *

In another, more recent memory, Kane Hailand surveyed the army of his mutilated reflections in the webbed pattern he punched into the mirror.  Her method of tattooing was too maniacally and perfectly controlled.  Rage should be barbaric.  Passion should be barbaric.  In the broken mirror stood a vagrant in an undershirt, sporting half a beard of shaving cream, bleeding at the fist.  He needed to leave.  Leaving was the only way.  If he didn't leave her, he would kill her.  It wouldn't be the gruesome domestic murder that the media would glorify for centuries as the epic disbanding of The Scoundrels through lustful slaughter- it would be the much more subtle, oft-seen melodrama in which he'd slowly suck the life out of her with their mutual projected indifference.  She didn't deserve it.  She was perfect until he destroyed her.

The souls of fortune who have been blessed with such phenomenal gifts as Kane Hailand's imagination are never hesitant to improvise.  Globules of shaving cream still hanging from his earlobes, Kane scraped a handheld razor against the unshaven side of his face, ridding himself of his trademark mustache for the first time since he sprouted the extraordinary facial hair as an adolescent scholar in the orphanage.  Without the mustache, he noticed just how much he looked like Hank Adaline, the genius pianist-turned-DJ.

Instead of continuing with the razor, Kane pulled a jagged fragment from the busted mirror and raised it to his head.  Just one momentary lapse and he'd be lying on the floor with a split Adam's apple- the thought was absolutely thrilling.  He dragged the glass shard in a descending streak over his eyebrow.  Blood snaked from the open wound, spreading like a delta over his eye.  In his preoccupied state, Kane failed to account for the fact that he has blood, that any tearing of flesh, let alone on the fragile forehead, will thunder blood to flow like rain down his face.  The forehead is a highly expressive, highly human physical asset, the only visible indication of man as an intelligent being.  Peruse any textbook and you'll find in the evolution of the human skull that man's forehead has become much fuller and more pronounced.  A forehead distinguishes man as man- no other animal has a forehead.  In man, however, you'll find an expressive field of flesh, a badged shield over the world of his mind, bordered by two lines of hair.  A forehead is a blessing from nature, crowning man as king.

All of Kane's towels were in the wash.  He relied on her to do his laundry, but she only ever opted to use the washing machine when she needed a boost of vibration.  Kane fetched a spare roll of toilet paper to absorb his blood.  Ordinarily (that is, if one could be in this position ordinarily), he wouldn't have bothered with the leaking gash in his forehead, but the blood was gushing in such a constant rush that, peering into the scramble of his reflections in the broken mirror, it was difficult to decipher where he had already cut, and he didn't want to botch the carving.

Kane wiped his brow and resumed treating his forehead like a jack-o-lantern.  He was once The Jester in the greatest musical trio of all time- alas, The Jester and The Scoundrels are no more.

It is most unfortunate that Kane failed to account for his use of the mirror to guide his carving- when viewed away from the mirror, his tattoo is meaninglessly backward.  He also botched the fourth (or fourth to last, depending on which way you look at the tattoo) character.  Don't be too critical of Kane's blunder- watch any child practice his handwriting, and it becomes immediately apparent that this character is one of the more difficult letters in the English alphabet.  After drenching the roll of toilet paper in blood, Kane lifted the rug from underneath his feet and dabbed it to his forehead.

He could smell the synthetic smoke from her violet ashtray.  Somewhere in his mind he was unrelentingly annoyed with her for keeping her ashtray in his bathroom.  The ceramic ashtray was an impeccable mold of her mouth as it stretched when she growled her most famous growl in the coda to The Hounds of Anger.  The violet molding was anatomically perfect, except that it held a pile of violet ash in place of a tongue- this was probably more fitting.  Though she didn't live with him, he somehow became entrapped in a living situation in which she kept an ashtray in his bathroom.  A box of tampons, a violet glass makeup case- she had invaded.  Of course, she couldn't smoke outside because she couldn't be seen.  This stubborn secrecy was not to hide their affair.  Hank Adaline knew about the affair.  At least Kane assumed Hank knew- they didn't talk about it.  What nobody knew, however, was that she carried on the affair with Kane when she was supposedly visiting the oncologist.  Her smoking was a chore, requiring constant attention like the child she never had.  Her smoky drawl empowered her to become the only woman Kane ever met who could growl.  This was Anika Handel, the greatest contralto in the history of sound, who smoked two packs a day.  The earth is a temple, the body a wasteland- everybody has their own methods of destruction.

Kane completed the insignia with a defiant slash of mirror, bowed into his forehead as if to prove to God or his self or whoever may be watching that he had done the deed.  As he moved to lift the lock from the door, the faint taste of death leaking into his mouth from the bleeding crest over his brow, he noted curiously that he hadn't felt any pain when carving the insignia into his forehead.  He had been too focused, too adrenalized to notice any pain.  Kane Hailand believed father pain must be present to validate birth.

Kane emptied the contents of the violet ashtray into his palm and smacked them to his forehead, letting the violet soot stain his open flesh to sting a holy primal pain.  Gritting his teeth to chew the bloody red rug, Kane clenched his fists and trembled in triumphant agony as the sweet liberation ignited his being with the omnipotent sensation of life.  This scar will endure long after death.  Pain, pain, beautiful pain- pain as lovely as Kane.

* * *

This is what Kane Hailand recalled when driving through his life.  He conjured the following scenario in his once-brilliant mind countless times over the week since he replaced his signature Jester's hat with a tattooed forehead.  She would take a cab.  If anyone other than the cabdriver asked where she was going, she would feign weakness and whisper in a masterful rasp that she was on her way to another session with the oncologist.  She would arrive at Kane's beachside resort for one of her afternoon visits.  She would unbutton her violet coat as she walked through the foyer so that when she did finally saunter into his studio, she would play the naked minx and tempt him in lustful desire.  Not finding him in the studio, she would wander curiously until she craved a cigarette.  This last part wouldn't take long- she would remind herself that she's dying anyway.  In the bathroom she would find a broken mirror and a sink full of blood.  He didn't even leave a note.  She used to be an angel- she never had a chance.

There are certain safety risks one assumes when soaring thirty-six thousand feet in the oxygen-depleted atmosphere just a week after one has violently severed the flow of blood through one's forehead.  Combine this with the astronomical risk of infection one faces when he inundates his sliced flesh with a fist full of carcinogenic ash.

Kane Hailand's memory was hazy.  Time, most assuredly, was fooling Kane Hailand.  He had only one human conversation in the week and a half since he tattooed himself in the busted mirror.  He imagines this is how his dialogue transpired, standing in the airport in his undershirt, his sneakers, and his wool cap from the Violet 9.

Ticketing Agent:  Welcome to Viking Transcontinental, where we never stop exploring.

Kane:  I'd like to go somewhere new.

Ticketing Agent:  South Sudan is the newest country, Sir, but we don't fly there.

Kane: I mean I'd like to go somewhere I've never been.

Ticketing Agent:  Have you reviewed the flight information, Sir?

Kane:  I don't know what airline this is.

Ticketing Agent:  Welcome to Viking Transcontinental, where we never stop exploring.

Kane:  Which flights have open seats?

Ticketing Agent (typing):  Within the next three hours I can get you to Hong Kong, Toronto, New Delhi, Paris, Cairo, Makhraj, Lima-

Kane:  Makhraj- where's that?

Ticketing Agent:  The Middle East.

Kane:  One ticket please.

Ticketing Agent:  Okay, one roundtrip ticket to Makhraj.

Kane:  Just a one-way.

Ticketing Agent:  Your passport, please.

Kane:  My passport.  Yes, of course.  My passport.  One moment.

Under watch of the airline employee, Kane Hailand frantically patted his blue-jean pockets.  Slipping past his passport, he removed a folded photograph.  The only existing shot from before Kane was abandoned at the orphanage depicted an infantile Kane holding the leg of another child who bore a similar facial structure.  Kane had always questioned why he should be holding the leg of the other child.

Ideas flashed through his head, too quick for the voice of conscience to piece them out, but powerful enough for Kane to recognize the general illusion of chaos, his heart not even beating but jumping without ever coming down so that the anticipation of regaining his heartbeat distracted him from breathing.  Again, he fished into his pocket for the passport.  In his flustered state, he temporarily lost access to his memory.  A man in such a state as Kane, in which access to one's own memory is prohibited, becomes unconcerned with minor stresses like social norms, foolishly unable to find a passport in the chasm of his pocket.  Kane handed his passport and his credit card to the ticketing agent.  His wallet, he surmised, will soon be left behind.

Ticketing Agent (raising his eyes from the passport):  Jake Hailand- my Lord- you're Kane Hailand.

Kane:  Some people know me by that name.

Ticketing Agent:  I didn't even recognize you without the eye patch and the Jester's hat.  And you shaved your mustache!  Oh my God, Kane, it's really you.  I know every word to Red Chaos and V.V.I.V.- She's detonated, looking gorgeous, what are you waiting for- you're a genius.

Kane:  Thank you, that's very flattering.

Ticketing Agent:  How's Anika- with her health and all?

Kane:  She's fine.  Look-

Ticketing Agent:  Please tell me you guys are getting back together.  You gotta get Hank back on the piano, man, his DJ stuff is garbage.

Kane:  I don't know the answer to your question.  Can I please just-

Ticketing Agent:  I am the Jester, O yea, O yea- jeez, you look like you've had a hell of a day.

Kane:  That's a keen observation.

Ticketing Agent:  Kane Hailand, The Jester, buying a one-way ticket to a place he's never heard of- wow.

There was a time when discussing his art with a total stranger amazed him, but standing in the airport in his undershirt, his sneakers, and his Violet 9 cap, with no luggage and no idea of where he was headed, Kane was plainly disinterested.  Struggling to stay alert, he drew stares from the people toting bags in the lengthy security lines.

Bright lights of the airport terminal.  Stinging pain in his forehead.  His wool cap.  Wool is good, thick and warm- absorbent.

His vision was foggy like breath on a mirror, causing the flight information on the digital departure board to appear illegible.  He imagined everyone who walked past would point at him and judge him with their eyes.  He felt as though he were standing nude while a perfect stranger pointed out the minutest of his flaws that he had never been aware of.  All he wanted to know was which way to his gate, which way to Makhraj, but he wouldn't dare attempt to speak to them when they were staring with such hostility.

A family of four stopped beside him to read the departure board.  They lined up like Russian dolls to view the flight information, all of them with olive skin and stern cheekbones, standing staunch and silent.  The mother, or the woman who Kane imagined to be the mother, was covered head to toe in a shadowy red silk niqab.  The loose fabric that draped over the woman's head swayed with the cool breath of the air conditioner, creating a pattern of morphing shadows in the red fabric.  Kane was startled, for here was a woman who had hidden every inch of skin under cloth, and yet Kane knew beyond certainty that she was a woman- what sort of essence exists within a woman that safeguards her unquestionable femininity?  It was in the eyes- the entrancing almost-red eyes that suggested complete purity or total menace, freedom or captivity, piercing two vivid holes into Kane's clouded vision.  He had seen those eyes before.  There was a time when those eyes were his illumination to being.   Kane claims that he often evokes the glorious pair of eyes in his imagination, and every time he sees them he becomes shocked anew by their power.  This, somehow, is the only thing that ever mattered.

Kane Hailand couldn't discern the family's language, but he believed he heard the word Makhraj, and so he waited for them to complete their conversation and then he followed the red niqab at a healthy distance, wishing to see those eyes again so he can gaze into them and challenge them for all eternity.

Kane doesn't remember much else.  He remembers the red niqab, dancing like a silk evening star in the distance.  Periodically, he would pat a hand under his wool cap to touch the greasy scabbed violet.  Wool is good, he kept thinking.

He claims to remember nothing of the flight except an endless field of clouds, floating constant like an ancient path to God's palace where Kane once roamed, every shape unique and ideal.  He remembers that evening sun, like an orange giant trying to tell him something if only he could penetrate its blinding light.  He dazed through an eleven-hour flight, eating nothing and thinking nothing except for the idea that at one time he could walk over the clouds as an immortal over sea.  He doesn't remember dates or logistics- he remembers smells and sensations, hunger and cold desperation.  He remembers that he didn't eat or drink a morsel all through the eleven hours of flight, but he doesn't remember when it was that he realized he left his wallet at the airport, that he never put it back into his pocket once he paid for his ticket.  He doesn't remember what caused him to panic.  He doesn't remember panicking at all.

When Kane wasn't watching the clouds as a being removed from all surroundings and past actions, he was cripplingly upset and amazed with the situation he entangled himself in.  He thought of Anika.  And Hank- always Hank.  Feelings of guilt, though he wasn't quite sure what he felt guilty about.  He really wasn't leaving anything behind, he told himself.  Besides, he didn't have a choice.  If he would have stayed, then he would have gotten revenge- revenge for all of it.  And now to wherever.  To Makhraj.  Seat reclined, eyes dry and half-closed, not awake and not asleep, Kane watched the clouds.

The next thing Kane remembers is walking out of Son Imadak International Airport into the ripe Makhraj sun.  He doesn't remember stumbling mechanically like a zombie from the plane to follow a flow of people for an interview with the customs officer- when you rely on Kane Hailand to use his memory, you'll always be left to guess.

As far as Kane recalls, one moment he was following a dancing red star in the pristine yet somehow grimy American airport, and in the very next moment he was confronted with a panorama of oriel windows and advertisements written in two languages.  One of the languages was English.  He didn't recognize the other, but he assumed it was indeed a language just as any coded symbol must be a language, and surely some language must be spoken in Makhraj.  Swarms of brown faces spoke in the unknown tongue.  Kane's younger self would have immediately recognized Arabic, the language of his childhood hero, but that was a different Kane than the one in Makhraj.  A young Kane Hailand once commented in a song called Light Shattered that the Arabic language is beautiful when written, yet its verbal tone is often harsh, as if misread in the disconnect between the language and the speaker- that younger, far more astute, Kane Hailand was always right, even when he was wrong, and he was blissful.  Most of all he was the scoundrel who challenged the devil to a battle of wits, and won.  Or did he- it was always difficult to tell who was winning between Hank and Kane.

Kane wandered through the people, breathing the smells and sights of a land unknown.  Though Kane Hailand had traveled the world as an international music icon, he had never before toured Makhraj.  Makhraj was unlike any place he had ever seen- a modern city built to mirror the shade of stone.  Sporadically, through the henhouse of gibberish, people would turn to him and greet him amicably in neighborly English, as if to reassert that he wasn't privy to their private native talk.  He was either an alien observing the human race or he was the only human observing an alien race- these thoughts from a man who once preached racial harmony, who lambasted societal constructs, especially those as foul as race.  Truth, he knew in youth, and then forgot.  He wished that for just one moment the force of gravity would dissipate, and everyone and everything that anybody ever worked for would float away into endless space.

Kane was struck by lightning as a university student.  He defied every medical study in human history when he developed a telekinetic gift to control particles of light.  One of the biggest spectacles at a Scoundrels show was to watch Kane Hailand the Jester work his miracles with light.  The lightning had another strange effect- it caused his shadow to vanish.

Kane hadn't seen his shadow since the lightning bolt, but there it was, dancing independently of his motion on the cobblestone roads in Makhraj.

The nimble rain at dusk brought out the smell of gasoline.  Buses and cars honked their horns and rammed against each other like bumper cars.  Penniless Kane walked west past the traffic, following the setting sun.  The last time he saw the sunset was in America, and here that same sun was setting once again- setting in Makhraj.  Kane says it's not often you get to see the sun set twice in one day.  You could try explaining to him that the two sunsets he saw occurred on different calendar days, but he won't hear of it.  This is typical of Kane Hailand.

Kane walked past a beggar who sat in contortedly atop the brick steps of a wax candle shop, gaunt cheeks sucking moisture from his raggedy gown.  Affected by the beggar, Kane tried to speak to the man, to establish a rapport that would perhaps evolve into the most unlikely and beautiful of friendships.  In response to Kane's questioning, the man could only shiver.  Overheated under streetlights in the night, Kane removed his Violet 9 wool cap and placed it snugly over the beggar's catatonic skull.  Kane considered that he was doing something generous for someone else.  After a day, perhaps a lifetime, in which he had acted entirely on his own behalf, Kane Hailand was proud, for he had granted alms to this man of the streets, a man who could hopefully appreciate the cap, blood-ink stains and all.

A young man approached.  Having watched Kane's encounter with the beggar, the young man noticed the severity of Kane's financial situation.  He draped an arm over Kane's shoulder, entreating the distraught American to clean up at a hotel and join the party at Club Emerald.  Kane politely declined.  He was roughing it, and the idea of a known destination was harrowing.  Besides, entering the public sphere would only increase his chances of being recognized as the Jester from The Scoundrels.  Any prospect of recognition struck the maddened Kane Hailand with sublime terror.  He followed an unquenchable urge to let the air flow free into his scarred wounds, to breathe his newfound spontaneity, to run from the sunlight that had long disappeared into the darkness of night.

It was in his encounter with the young gentleman that Kane registered the implications of having no money in a land in which he knew no one and he did not speak the language.  This realization led him to a second realization- namely, that he was hungry, and for hours he had been ignoring the crescendo of a tumultuous migraine.  His temples swelled and pulsed, and almost immediately his world became a curse in which light was the source of debilitating pain.  Escape the light.  Keep walking.  Everybody turned to stare at the American with the tattooed forehead, glaring at him and following him with red radar eyes.  He nearly stumbled into an impersonator of his self, a slim Jester wearing a hand-painted eye patch and a military tunic of the wrong color, dancing with a child who dressed as a chimp.  The citizens of Makhraj have never heard the name Elvis, yet they impersonate Kane Hailand in the streets.

Kane marched forth through alleyways of stone, through the square, past mosques and synagogues far older than Kane's homeland, past the mothers breastfeeding in the streets, the men in uniform, the soldiers bearing guns, through the grass, gardens, dirt roads and copses, as the pounding agony throbbed in Kane's head, pulsing rhythmically and musically, as everybody stared.  He even invented a little song that he sang with the beating pain in his head- Shelter, shelter, sought by all yet not by me / I do not wish to turn my back, I do not wish to leave.  Valleys and tan mountains under thin veils of darkness, no sign of life-just telephone wire.  Telephone wire- keep walking.  Walk until your legs crumble into ossified dust.  This was to be a very lonely experience.  This was to be whatever Kane Hailand was looking for.  Somewhere in his mind, he had done this before.

A man will often feel that the world's gone crazy and that he's the only sane one left.  Not Kane Hailand.  Kane knew that the world was as it always was, but he had lost his goddamned mind.

The valley nights were as cold as they were barren.  Though the valley boasts of a yearlong agricultural season, the temperature is highly temperamental.  Kane stomped atop the arid, dry micro-stones topped with tiny shrubs that hugged the ground, and for a while he imagined he was a gargantuan dinosaur clomping over prehistoric territory never walked by men.  The air grew colder as he wandered alone in his undershirt and sneakers.  Nobody was there.  Nobody was ever there.  Nobody look at poor Kane Hailand, he is so alone.  Yet somehow he was less lonely than when he was with her.  He lowered his head and charged forth like a bull into the cold, swallowing slow bullets of thick saliva, regretting the donation of his wool hat, navigating at night.  Whatever land Kane walked was not a land fit for sustaining life.  Wandering, wandering, wandering Kane- wandering into his next life in a series of lifetimes defined by his clothes- Kane Hailand in the Jester's garb, preceded by the political Rebel god of the Violet 9 leading secret meetings in his blue robe, who evolved from the poor orphaned Jake, yes, Jake who lived too long ago for Kane to remember what he wore.  He was now a new man, a loaded disappointment waiting to fire, wandering in his undershirt and sneakers, forehead tattooed violet.  The wanderer was taunted by his own degrading thoughts.  Kane Hailand is nobody's child- nobody's child would do as Kane has done.

The sun rose only to sink again with a sickly spring of his empty stomach and the pulsing migraine in his head.  Periods of rest were fickle and frequent.  Tired.  Weak.  Hungry.  He didn't know what day it was, what hour it was- where he was.  Weakness weighed his shoulders.  What little urine he produced was rust-colored like cola.  These are the ancient sands of Mother Land that man has walked for millennia to never leave his mark on this sacred spread.  Kane longed for the echoing grumbles to murmur from his stomach because it hurt less when it grumbled.  His mouth was hot and clammy, and it felt as though there was some force under his tongue that gave a vile taste and made his stomach churn sickness.  His migraine was his hunger, and he could focus on nothing else.

To Kane Hailand, the land breathed, and when it breathed it respired in the shape of letters that form the words to songs that have provided a voice for an entire generation- so why is Kane so disoriented?

No vegetation.  Kane says his sense of motion became more acute.  His vision strengthened.  He could detect every variance between the motion of animals and the motion of machines.  Strangely detached from his body.  Only in hunger did he notice his excess blubber.  He imagined his body could probably eat itself for several months.  This claim is absurd.  The longest documented case of the human body surviving without food is forty days.  To posit that one could survive off one's own fat for several months, especially if the hunger in question belongs to Kane Hailand, who is of a slim build, is preposterous.  Kane says despair is powerful.  He says despair can strip even the most humanized of regions to a jungle.  With no tools to hunt, he'll either eat or be eaten- these are the fundamental laws by which we live, the primordial code of our war for subsistence.  Kane had no energy for war.  Weary.  Dizzy. Sleepless.  Frail like a languid doll.  He imagines he spent days in this condition.

What would it be like to say goodbye to a lover?  Kane Hailand wouldn't know.  There was a time when he could feel passion.  His lyrics somehow inspired passion in others, but Kane Hailand was detached and dead inside.  Kane left Anika for the cancer to eat her.  He doesn't think he could have done much if he stayed.  There are medical studies that suggest that the patient has a higher chance of recovery with support from those around her- love can serve to boost morale, which is intimately linked with physical health.  Kane couldn't do that.  What they had was never love, anyway- it was probably spite more than anything else.  He couldn't keep her happy.  She was ruined.  He was too.  Her visits to his hotel were strictly sexual in every way except in the way that she looked at him- things go unspoken.  When Kane left, he took her excuse with him, and maybe now she'll go to her oncologist.

There is no shame when you are thirsty in despair, Kane says.  Your stomach is a constant reminder that you're lacking.  When you're lacking, it doesn't matter what you're lacking.  Kane imagined he was nearly empty.  There is nothing lonelier than an empty soul.  The migraine plummeted from his brain to his teeth like a militant army of pain turned against him.  And the thirst.  Thirst, Kane says, is the most consuming of pains, far more consuming than hunger.  He was dizzy, as if bound to an ever-rotating scaffold that somehow never completes its rotation.  Beaded cakes of rotting saliva lined his mouth like crusted filth, the cracks of his lips clawed with blood to mirror the spaces between his pained teeth, his mouth stale and foul-tasting.  Thirst doesn't allow sleep- it doesn't allow complete wakefulness either.  Thirst left Kane in a crippled daze, his mouth dry and sticky as if his tongue had been cemented in a powdered layer of concrete, wandering the sun-scorched wastelands.  Moving his tongue required an obstreperous effort.  Kane imagined he would kill an animal to drink its blood.  In an afterthought, he realized the sodium content of blood probably wouldn't make for a refreshing beverage.  Thirst doesn't allow forethought- the only thoughts thirst allows are thoughts of thirst.

While studying his shadow, Kane happened upon a leopard perched in a tree among the swirling river valley sands.  Golden in the wild grass, spotted in royal rings of black, chatoyant eyes mesmerizing and green, the leopard slobbered a yoyo of saliva in anticipation of its wandering prey in the grass below.  Kane never knew that leopards habit the Middle East.  Least of all did he expect to find a leopard in the river valley.  But even if this leopard were the only living leopard in the Makhraj wilderness, it would have assuredly found Kane Hailand.  Animals of all species gravitated toward Kane.  It was part of his gig, one of his musical superpowers.  Animals and Light.  He always traveled with an animal companion- Sun King the bluebird, Icarus the walrus, Phaeton the pig of light, and who could forget the infamous Glass Pelican?  Many venues disapproved, but The Scoundrels were adamant that Kane Hailand the Jester never took the stage without an animal sidekick.

Back in America, Kane's thoughts used to range from his dreams the night before to the universal implications of humanity in peril.  In America, petty issues bothered Kane.  In the wild, he thought about how to put food in his mouth.  Possessed by living hunger, Kane imagined he could hunt the leopard.  Pound for pound, the leopard is one of the most efficient hunters in the natural world, but why should Kane concern himself with such petty minutiae when his hunger had seized control?  The leopard remained still and silent, intently focused on some scene below that Kane couldn't make out through the waist-high grass.  Kane trekked forth, stalking slowly and silently, hiding behind a boulder in the grass fields.  Eat or be eaten.  Here in nature, pitted against this silent beast of the wild, a timeless portrait of man versus whatever he turned against himself.  Kane the animal, bow to his roar.  Weaponless, tactless, gaunt and delusional, Kane prepared to challenge the beast.  He briefly imagined what raw flesh would taste like- and they call the lion the king of the jungle.

The leopard pounced.

Instantly, the leopard had its passing prey by the neck.  A gazelle lay limp and bleeding in the predator's jaws.  Kane watched in astonishment as the leopard dragged the gazelle by the neck to its tree.  The leopard commenced its feast.

This was the most fortunate occurrence Kane could have hoped for.  Although he had no prior knowledge of a leopard's dietary habits, Kane imagined the leopard would not eat the whole gazelle.  Eventually, the leopard would have its fill, and once it had its fill, it would leave its post for Kane to gorge on leftovers.  All Kane had to do was stalk behind his boulder and be patient.  Kane watched the leopard tear through the flesh of its prey, marauding in a great buffet of cartilage.

Kane kept his distance because he didn't know if a leopard would consider human for dessert.  This was the first time he had ever feared an animal, as all animals had always been affectionate toward Kane, but he had lost so much of his former self that he couldn't gamble in assuming that he still retained the trust of all animals.  His vision faded into a blue headache.  Everything became more buoyant.  Yellow and gray sequences of light.  Leopards live in solitude.  They roam the land alone, cohabiting only for as long as it takes to mate.  Kane watched perfection in the motion of the leopard's jaws- the ferocious back-and-forth of its gorging head, its white quill whiskers, its blinking eyelids, which, when open, exposed a penetrating gaze as the gazelle lay still and utterly dead.  The leopard nibbled delightfully, peeling the hide from the bone to get to the meat.  Kane couldn't believe how simple the process looked.  It was not at all bloody or violent.  This was appetizing to Kane.

Like a man peering into opposing mirrors, Kane wondered if God has a God.  In the last song he wrote for the trio, Kane Hailand argued that God is a superior architect to man.  Man believes he was created in God's image because he wants to be like God, to create like God.  And man can create.  Kane most certainly can create- Kane Hailand was once God.  Through Kane's entire artistic career, the only truth he learned is that man cannot contend with God.  The only weapon man can wield against God is that of destruction.  In the rubble of destruction, however, something new is created.  Destruction can be a brilliant means to creation.  The song was called Alone in Myth.  Hank Adaline refused to write a piano accompaniment.  No matter how Kane presented the lyrics to the genius, Hank Adaline remained resolute in his decision to ditch the mad red piano for his new mad red turntables.  The greatest pianist in the universe became a forlorn DJ.  God does not live here anymore.

Drinking perfection in the motion of the leopard, Kane decided to smother the sun.  He told himself that if a sun could set twice in one day, it could just as easily set once and for all.  Somehow, he would gain the power to do the impossible.  Set the sun.  At the very least, he would try.  This was the Kane Hailand the world once knew.

Kane ducked behind the boulder in the grass, watching the primeval act and thinking what it could be like to be eaten alive.  He imagined it was the migraine that drained his capacity for movement, but he knows now that it was the lack of nourishment that so weakened him.   Thirst.  He describes thirst as the perpetual sensation of trying to burp, the consuming despair that there's a pit clogged in your closing throat.  His tongue was encased in an impenetrable armor of dryness, searching the cave of his mouth for saliva, suffering the recurring hallucinatory sips of water from which he would snap into consciousness, disappointed to learn that none of it was real.  As he enviously and voyeuristically watched the leopard's feast, Kane considered it strange that the leopard was unaware of his presence.

Appearing suddenly, like an apparition, a second, smaller leopard limped forth.  The feasting leopard raised its face in an instant snarl.  Kane says a leopard has two faces- one face is docile while the other is a fierce snarl.  The docile face is majestically playful, serene and contemplative.  The snarl is menacing, and it comes in a flash of fangs borne like ivory knives, only to be reformed back to its masked docility.  The snarl need only last an instant- its message is clear.

Just one fang hung like a stalactite in the roaring snarl of the limping intruder.  A younger Kane would have dedicated his entire artistic output to a small leopard with a lame leg and a single fang.  The small intruder approached Kane, hobbling forth.  The feasting leopard felt threatened, flashing its snarl, the two leopards hissing threats in muted roars as they began to parry in a circle.  Kane instinctively placed a protective hand over the photograph in his pocket.

The leopards made lunges at each other, dodging the opponent only to dance back into battle.  Snarling, hissing, roaring, pouncing, showing teeth.  Kane watched and forgot his thirsty crippling migraine.  Kills must have been scarce in the valley, as the one-fanged leopard, though visibly outmatched, refused to leave until it had its meal.  Eat or be eaten.  Leopard against leopard, heart against heart- what chance does man have at peace?  The larger leopard pounced on the miniature intruder, piercing its fangs into the intruder's throat, leaving the lame intruder to lie wounded beside the kill.  The victor did not cannibalize as Kane had hoped.

Kane considered carving his initials into the boulder he was crouching behind.  He would do it with his fingernails, or perhaps a stick.  If death was to find him there, the world should know the fate of their beloved Jester.  He decided against this- the land does not belong to man, as man belongs to land.

After having its fill of the gazelle, the killer leopard escaped into the wild grass.  Kane's hunger now a wailing siren in his head, he approached the kill.  The wounded intruder lay beside the kill, its chest inflating in perfect rhythm with the wind.  Watching the leopards' duel had excited Kane from his delirium, investing him with just enough life to regain an iota of sense, which told him that as long as the lame leopard was alive and near the kill, it was ill-advised to act.  A fleeting voice told Kane to put the leopard out of its misery- mangled and mutilated by a member of its own species, the one-fanged leopard will never know trust.

Kane continued wandering- his body empty, his head a rolling mass of pain, the scars on his forehead flaring like torches to lead his unknown path.  Sunrise, rise again.  Every time Kane saw the sun rise he wondered how many times it had risen that day.  He says thirst prevents you from conceptualizing things like day and night.  Kane Hailand will set the sun.

Kane couldn't remember his lyrics.  These are lyrics he performed nightly, lyrics that defined a generation, lyrics he polished with a sculptor's chisel, gauging their every nuance from the shape of their sound to their written appearance so that all words, syllables, letters, and pauses were perfectly aligned in rhythm.  These lyrics were Kane Hailand.  These lyrics were gone.

Thunderbolts roared.  Lightning lit the sky.

Somewhere along his journey, Kane imagined he heard the low rumble of a distant river.  A voice inside him imagined he wouldn't make it to the river.  His organs said yes, while what was left of his mind said to hell with it, too tired to argue, clawing through this slow-roasting thirst.  He saw a purblind image of his aqueous reflection in the water- pale sunken face, emaciated frame, and the mirrored tattoo which, when reflected in the river, appeared as he originally intended.  A zigzag bolt of lightning shocked the river.  Kane doesn't remember much else- just the singing lure of the river, the painted sunrise, and his final distinct vision, as vivid and as real to him as anything he had ever known- those brilliant, beautiful, unmistakable eyes that once blazed in fantastic fire through the silk window of the airport mother's red niqab, the eyes that have watched him and inspired him through all his life.  In this vision, however, the eyes were not set in the niqab- they didn't belong to a woman at all.  Kane saw the sacred pair of red eyes set in the stoic and providential face of a one-armed shirtless black man with a single leopard's fang affixed to a string round his neck.


* * *



Track 2: Leon by the Beard


Kane Hailand awoke in a dream.  He was in heaven, zooming up a ladder of light, safe in the calm of a sonorous whistle more beautiful than beauty can fathom.  The whistle sang in a tone that supersedes hearing, bending the air like a slithering cobra to weave its path to Kane's chakra, absorbing him in the type of soul possession humanity has dreamt of since it was brewed up and bundled in flesh- utopia.  It was as though he were an everlasting particle among the kingdom, and it was the supreme honor to serve in a kingdom such as this, flying up the ladder of light in perfect unity with the other particles like cherubs dancing at a thousand feet per second.  In this land of sound, Kane foresaw the prophecy that peace shall reign.  He experienced intensity unparalleled since The Scoundrels last played From Darkness in a vaudeville hall- but the birth in From Darkness was lit to the sounds of Hank's piano and Anika's stunning vocal, while the whistle that was now glorifying Kane never existed on the earth he once knew.  Still, this whistle carried a strangely earthen quality, as if the sound that possessed Kane was the music of the wind itself, spoken between the mountain and the land in timeless conversation.  Kane awoke.

Leon:  You lucky it is summer.  If it is winter, you are dead.

Kane squinted into the sun he so reviled.  The sun, the giver of soul, only reminded him of how dead he was.  His forehead burned under a wet cloth.  He had many questions, none of which he could formulate in his mind.  Blinking into a clear blue sky, he recognized the distant rumbling of the river.  He turned his head to see a robed man atop an ample stone.  The man's great beard was split vertically down the center, the two halves of beard looping under his arms to conjoin with the split braid in the back of his head- the general effect of his appearance was that his arms poked through two ropy coils of hair as a gymnast with his armpits in the rings.  Leon achieved this strange design through advanced application of knot theory.

A younger Kane Hailand possessed the eminent ability to recognize virtue in any disguise- this was the ability that allowed him to tap into the genius of Hank Adaline.  Inspecting Leon's split rings of beard, however, Kane couldn't recognize virtue.  Kane's only thought was that this strange alien who inhabited this patch of valley must be the ugliest man he had ever seen.  This is not to say that every man or woman is good-looking in comparison, but most people do their best with what faults they've been stunted with- eight billion people self-sculpting into their subjective impressions of the universal ideal.  Not Leon- don't you ever dare add Leon to this mix.  Leon, with his black-braided mane, most emphatically did not care to conform to anyone's standards of sexiness.  But a man cannot be told by his face- the only thing a face will tell is how the world will treat a man by such a face.

Leon:  Jake.  Jake Hailand.  You survived the lightning.

Leon lifted the wooden pail at his foot and moved toward Kane.  His footsteps were silent in buckskin slippers.  He poured a tasteless liquid into Kane's mouth.  A trident of water spouted from the pail, tunneling into Kane's throat, leaking down both cheeks, extinguishing his foul breath.  The sensation was but a humble ode to the salvation Kane expected would end the suffering of thirst, but then he transcended into the sneaking memory of the first drink Leon had given- warm water streaming from the sky.  Small details, such as how long he had been wherever he was or whatever his purpose in this perplexing palace may be, were trite mysteries to Kane Hailand.  The liquid, though tasteless, felt foreign, provoking his tongue to wag frantically and of its own accord like an alien in his mouth.

Leon:  Jake Hailand.

Kane (disoriented, gasping):  Deception!

The words never escaped the silence of Kane's diaphragm.  He tried to lift his head, but fell back into dreaming.  Again he awoke in heaven, under the caress of the otherworldly whistle and the rushing tide.  Leon fed Kane another sip.  Kane tongued the water in a swishing circle to scrape the layers of dirt-thirst from the walls of his mouth like a miner in pursuit of ore.

Leon:  You are awake.  Jake.

Kane:  How do you know that name?

Leon:  I check passport.  You travel with not much.  This is good.

Kane:  That name- Jake.  I don't use it anymore.

Leon:  What you wish we call you?

Kane:  Call me Kane- I don't really know who I am.

Leon:  Kane.  Leon.  Me too, I no use old name.

Kane:  You speak English.

Leon:  I can do more with the English than just speak.  In addition, I can write with the hand in the English, and I can have mistakes in the English-

Kane:  I see.

Leon:  You see.  I study the English late in life- already I was man.  No boy.  So I am looking at it always as outsider.  I find curious the way certain phrases is said.

Kane:  How did I get here?

Leon:  We find you by river.  Pass out.  No dead.  Close.

Leon lifted the wet cloth from Kane's forehead and dunked it into the wooden pail of water.  Kane relished in the chilled medicine of sweeping wind over the beads of moisture in his inked scabs.  Leon lifted another pail and set it before Kane.

Leon:  You is hungry.  Eat.

The gleeful Kane Hailand nearly swooned when he saw the golden circle of dates inside the pail.  He scooped a handful of dates into his mouth and reveled in the fruity burst of magical marvelous juice, jaws too weak to chew.  Leon gripped Kane's mouth.

Leon:  Eat slow.

Kane's body seemed to him an alien vestibule, and he thought it remarkable that this body had always been with him.  It was then that he realized he had been laying in the comfort of a hand-woven quilt.  Checking beneath the quilt, his legs appeared gigantic and his chest inflated automatically.

Leon lifted a hallowed reed and put it to his lips.  He laid his hands firmly yet delicately, like a surgeon, over select holes in the body of the reed.  He pursed a firm puff of air, and the reed converted his breath into the same whistle of euphonic captivation that once awoke Kane Hailand from the dead.

Kane:  What is that?

Leon:  This?  This is ney.

Kane:  It's the most beautiful thing I ever heard.

Leon:  Oh, yes.  Thank you.  It is nice.  You like music.

Kane:  I don't know if like is the word I would use- it's a complicated relationship.

Leon:  Yes.  I tell you still I am outsider to the English.  My choice to word maybe not is so good.

Kane felt his pockets for his infant portrait.

Kane:  Where's my picture?

Leon (holding the photo):  This?

Kane:  Gimme that.

Kane attempted to lunge for the picture.  He didn't get far.  Leon placed the photo atop Kane's blanketed chest.
Kane heard footsteps, but he was too ill to turn his head.  The jagged stone that he was using as a pillow contained several distinct edges and stony spikes which knobbed their presence into the back of his neck.  He was grateful for the hospitality, yet slightly annoyed with Leon for not having provided something fluffier than stone.  Maybe Kane wasn't grateful.  He wrestled with the ground as he rested.  His sneakers and his undershirt lay on a rock beside him, dry in the scornful sun.  Locations, dates, people, and events were all enigmatic to Kane.  Before he could ponder any further, two silhouettes obstructed his view of the infinite.

Leon:  Kane, meet Alma.

Alma was quaint in the sunlight, carrying a wooden pail full of fruit.  A blossoming pink wildflower had been tucked behind her ear, and Kane could make out the inevitable approach of winter-white in a faint streak through her chestnut hair.  She smiled, highlighting a penumbra of Frida Kahlo bristles above her lip that didn't serve to display feminine pride or even commentary on sexual subjection, but seemed rather to epitomize Alma's complete indifference to questions of societal standards, just as any being will be indifferent to questions beneath the pursuit of its ambition.  Her brow sloped in a strong and shapely angle, and her dark eyebrows created an exquisite contrast to her light-brown hair.  She had large eyes, blue as sapphires, with long lashes that swept like the brush of a broom.  She was unkempt, yet beautiful and natural- a Nordic nose and Egyptian eyes, Alma was a woman of the world.  Her smile was oddly youthful, small and fleeting.  It was obvious to Kane that she need not struggle to smile.  She wore the most uncomfortable sandals Kane had ever seen, which caused her ankles and toes to swell.  Her unconventional beauty had such a profound effect that it prompted even skeptical Kane Hailand to admit her immediately into his good favor.

A tall one-armed man stood behind Alma.  He was black and beautiful- barefoot, shirtless and hairless, a large dead bird slung over his bare black shoulder.  The sun beat down upon his back and reflected off his dark skin.  Kane considered that this man's bare shoulder was hot enough to cook the bird he carried.  The man held a bale of wood in his one hand.  There was an ivory fang fixed to a string around his neck and an unseen dagger holstered at his waist.  Most striking, however, was the fateful pair of eyes set in his skull, following Kane to challenge him for all eternity.  Hank's eyes, always Hank's red eyes- Hank's red eyes in his phoenix-feathered mask, in the niqab at the airport, in the black man's skull.

The man plopped the dead bird on the ground and walked over to a wooden wagon behind Leon.  He stuck his bald head under a wooden barrel.  With his one hand, he twisted a valve to let a red liquid flow into his mouth.

Alma (squinting, beautiful):  You look so much healthier with food inside you.

Alma's voice was striking in connection with all nature, as if all voices had descended from her one voice, the voice of all women- the voice of all.

Kane:  I really can't thank you enough.  You saved my life.

Alma:  Nonsense.  We give everyone at least a chance.  It's not much work for us to feed one more mouth, and it's certainly worth the investment if you earn your Anima.

Kane (sitting up with a rush to his head):  Anima?

Alma (nurturing Kane):  Get some rest while we prepare supper.  Be sure not to eat any more.  Your body isn't used to the food.  It's a miracle you survived the lightning.

Gathering his calm, Kane fell back into sleep, dreaming of Hank's eyes in the skull of the one-armed man.  Although Leon could be a frustrating conversationalist, it was thankful that Kane's hosts knew English.  The stone beneath Kane's head, he realized in a dream, was not a stone, but a strange sort of guitar that he had never once beheld in his experience recording with The Scoundrels.

Kane awoke to Alma's gentle touch.  The sky was dotted with stars to the brink of whiteness.  Alma's drooping sleeve loomed just above his face, and he inhaled her flowery scent with delight.  A fire crackled somewhere near Kane's head, reminding him of Hank Adaline.  He shuddered- but even the devil's fire was more tolerable than that maniacal sun.

Alma (staring into the sky):  It's beautiful, isn't it?  Untouched.  When I was a girl, I used to wish upon the stars.  I never knew what to wish for, so I just wished for more stars.  I stopped wishing when I came out here- in this land, wishes were already true.

Kane:  You're very lucky.

Alma:  We all are.  Most of us don't know it yet.  I have only one wish left, and I know one day it will be granted.

Kane shivered under his hand-made quilt, cold in the desert night, laying in fearful proximity to the fire.  No matter where she moved, Kane watched Alma out of the corner of his eye because there was something about her that demanded attention, the sort of unique quality that Kane once attributed to Anika in a song called The Bride Wore Violet.  Alma seemed to possess a willing openness.  This type of openness was one that Kane himself had never felt secure enough to try.  He was accustomed to hiding behind the twisted lyrical ruse of every song he ever wrote.

Alma:  You must be freezing.

Kane:  It proves I'm alive.

Alma:  I'm weaving you a sweater, but I ran out of wool.  We'll find a trader in a day or two.

The one-armed man approached, walking barefoot over the rocky earth.  Kane used to try to walk barefoot.  He did this because he envied Hank Adaline, that barefoot pianist, but every time Kane's feet hit the sand of his beachside resort, he felt a rocky fire burn under the soles of his feet.
Though the night was frivolous without a tree to warm, the one-armed man remained shirtless.  With Leon's aid, Kane stood weakly, wrapped in his quilt.  He faced the man's tantalizing red eyes.  The one-armed man struck Kane with an awkward sense of self-conscious intimidation- international superstars do not often feel this sense of intimidation in personal encounters.  Kane shivered under his hand-stitched blanket, suddenly more sensitive to the evening cold.

Kane:  I never caught your name.

The man didn't acknowledge Kane's introduction in the slightest.

Alma:  He doesn't speak English, Kane.

Kane poked his right hand through his quilted cloak, offering a shake.  He immediately noted his error- the man would not return the handshake with the right hand he didn't have.  Humiliated, Kane revoked his hand and patted the man's bare shoulder, feeling the heat of the man's naked skin, reverting to his useless language in a panic.

Kane (enunciating slowly):  I'm Kane.  It's nice to meet you.

The man flashed his red eyes and hocked a fat wad of burning spit onto Kane Hailand's tattooed forehead.  A fall of saliva streamed down the bridge of Kane's nose as the man turned away.  Leon approached with the wet cloth and washed Kane's forehead as he spoke.

Leon:  He will be friend to you if you find Anima only.  Be kind.  Respect.  I am sorry for spit, but really he is great man.  How you say- ah, jeen-i-oos?

Kane:  Genius?

Leon:  Yes, that is it.

Alma (giggling as she lopped the head off a plucked bird):  Cut it out, Leon.  Tell him the truth.

Leon:  I tell truth always, sweet Alma.

Alma:  He's faking it, Kane.  Leon speaks ten languages and he's a wizard in every one of them.  He's taught at the finest institutions in the Middle East.  Isn't that right?

Leon:  Of course, Alma is aware of my personal policies regarding aforementioned institutions.

Alma:  Tell Kane what you wrote your dissertation on.

Leon:  The application of the space-time continuum as it pertains to the relation between travel and the supernatural in the corpus of Shakespeare- it is entitled Vagabonds Allow Glimpses Into Noumenal Apparitions, which sounds pedantic until you notice the acronym.

Kane imagined how Leon's face may appear under his ridiculous display of beard- the frog-like lower lip, the piercing black eyes, the archipelago of small moles leading to his outer canthus- the realization of Leon's identity shook Kane like an uppercut.

Kane:  You're Baltasar Kanaan!

Leon:  I was.

Kane:  My song Light Shattered is about your essays on cosmology.  You changed my life.

Leon:  I'll bet two scavenges that you never noticed the acronym.

Kane:  What?

Leon:  Vagabonds Allow Glimpses Into Noumenal Apparitions.

Kane:  Vagabonds Allow Glimpse- Oh.  No, I didn't think to look for that.

Leon:  Your mind is a more efficient explorer when it's turned off.  When you're not thinking, you're capable of creation.

Kane forgot this somewhere in his youth, when he created a universe to call his own, when he spent what seemed like an eternity without ever having a conscious thought because everything he did was seamless and flawless, when he was God.  Baltasar Kanaan was the hero of Kane's adolescence.  When Kane Hailand was a gifted orphan in the shelter, he studied every word his idol ever wrote.  It was impossible that this bearded goof, living with a one-armed black man and a beautiful woman in the Middle Eastern wilderness, a musical extraordinaire who responds to the name Leon, was Baltasar Kanaan.

Kane:  How'd you do it?

Leon:  I assume your vague article it refers to my alleged suicide.

Kane:  There were pictures.

Leon:  They published pictures?  They're even viler than I imagined.

Kane:  How'd you fake a gunshot in the mouth?

Leon:  The truth is something you won't believe, and I refuse to lie.

Kane:  Then tell me the truth.

Leon:  I cloned myself. Then I killed the clone.  I released periodic publications of verbose and convoluted essays regarding the intersection of the most notable achievers in art and science- Shakespeare and Einstein- to occupy the world while I conducted clone work in secret.

Kane's rapture was dashed by Alma's motherly summon.

Alma:  Kane, come here.  Let me teach you how to prep a kill.

Kane turned to help Alma.  Astounded, he double-took to search for the face of Baltasar Kanaan beneath that silly beard.

Leon:  You're an American?  We hold these truths to be self-evident- it sounds good in theory, but you've never actually practiced it.

Kane slid his sneakers on and sat beside Alma and her headless, exuviated bird.  She fingered the hole that was once the bird's neck, swiveling her hand to produce the most unappetizing squeaks.  The bird reeked like the bowels of the sea.  Light-headed, he felt that he might pass out.  His body tingled.  He thought it strange to watch the beautiful and seemingly innocent Alma brutally mutilate the bird's carcass- he had seen beautiful women do brutal things before.

Alma:  What I'm doing with my finger is breaking the joints and freeing up space for the organs.  You're gonna gut this poor fellow.

Kane:  I am?

Alma:  You are.  Okay, now we're ready to draw the innards.  I'm going to cut the vent, and when I do, use this spoon to gut him.

Kane:  I'm not putting my hands in that thing.

Alma:  Relax, Kane.  Now, one swift motion- like this.

Alma scooped a violent spoon of air.  She cut the vent with a pair of sharpened sticks and passed a hand-carved spoon to Kane.  He reached slowly toward the fourteen-pound hulk of steaming naked bird.

Alma:  Quick.  Like this.

Kane:  Is it supposed to smell this bad?

Alma:  That's the odor of the sea.  This is a cormorant- they're fish-eaters.

Kane:  Why'd you burn it already?

Alma:  Delousing.

Disgusted, Kane mimicked Alma's motion, drawing only a portion of the cormorant's fetid innards.  He imagined he could feel the bird's anatomy through his wooden spoon, nearly vomiting from the stench.  Kane recalled when The Scoundrels were approached to write a jingle for Clownfinger's Sausage Factory- Hank Adaline responded by revealing his own sausage in a series of lewd photographs.  If only Hank could see the cormorant- burnt bloody, leaking entrails, and positively stinking- he'd probably douse the bird with hot sauce and dive in, cracking jokes and cursing all the while.  It took Kane several swipes before Alma was satisfied that the bird was gutted.

Alma:  That wasn't so bad, you big baby

Kane:  Did you just call me a big baby?

Alma:  In Ancient Greece, children were considered youths until the age of thirty.

Kane smiled, baffled at Alma's tough and intelligent beauty, still completely perplexed to find that Baltasar Kanaan had a pulse.

Alma:  Go get some rest while I put this on the fire.

The cormorant's fetor was even worse when it was cooking, and the stench kept Kane awake.  Overwhelmed, he lay with his head on the mysterious guitar.  Nobody else would ever think to attribute the word guitar to this wooden contraption, but to Kane Hailand it was a guitar.  After using the guitar as a pillow, he felt a strange connection with the instrument.  He watched the clouds until he heard Alma's motherly whisper.

Alma: It's time for the rite.

Alma, Kane, and Leon circled the fire.  Leon called to a tent several yards off the river.  The tent was constructed from a shaved tree branch and a large hand-woven tarpaulin, wiggling in the nightland as the one-armed man emerged from the flap, barefoot and shirtless, a drum in his one hand.  His drum, a hollowed wooden hourglass, was capped with an animal skin at each end, woven together by a series of chords strung bottom-top-bottom-top over the hourglass body like prison bars.  Approaching with a stern and confident gait, the leopard's fang swayed like a pendulum from his neck.  He stopped before the fire, bathing in its heat.

Leon (whispering to Kane):  Are you able to stand?

Kane stood opposite the one-armed man, amazed.  The man was smoking an herb that Kane had never smelled before in all of his experience with substances.  To Kane's left stood Leon, the ney to his lips.  Alma graced Kane's right, a U-shaped harp at her breast.  The fire crackled in the center of their circle, the river ran behind the tent, and all was silent.  The one-armed man bowed before the moon.  When he spoke, it was as if he was speaking on the moon's behalf.

The one-armed man spoke in a language unknown to Kane.  The voice, when isolated from its owner, was impatiently fragmented- it was not the otherworldly and authoritative voice Kane expected.  Alma assisted the man in switching the drum from his left shoulder to his armless shoulder, fastening a wooden contraption around his stump as a primitive prosthetic, and then tying the prosthetic to the drum at his side to ensure that the hourglass body stay tucked beside him.  To complete the process, he stooped to grab the rope that was dangling from the drum.  He bit the end of the rope and began a slow tapping rhythm.

The man tapped his one hand against the goatskin drumhead, gradually increasing his pace.  His wrist did not move a lateral inch- it just swiveled quickly to alternate beats between his thumb and four fingers.  Occasionally, he would toss his head back like a horse to yank the rope with his teeth.  Examining the drum, Kane saw that the rope in the man's mouth was tied around the prison-bar strings that crossed the body of the drum.  By pulling this rope, he was tightening the drum-strings, changing its pitch, shaping its sound, its language.  Rhythm isn't about letters or words, it's about syllables- Kane Hailand remembered this long-forgotten axiom when listening to the black man's drum.  Leon joined with his ethereal ney, whistling and flirting with the drum of the stars, engaging curiously as two reflections about to realize they are one.  Their song was simple, yet somehow more advanced than anything The Scoundrels had ever composed in their musical experiments.  Alma ran a dainty hand across the seven strings of her harp, sending a shiver down Kane's spine.  Music was all that spoke.  The lyre, the ney, the talking drum- Kane Hailand had never heard any of these instruments before, but when enveloped in their simplistic beauty, he experienced the nirvana that once impelled him to pursue music.

When apparently their song had finished, the three musicians placed their instruments on the ground beside them.  They commenced to eat the day's game and gatherings. Kane awoke from his trance.  No longer under the philter of their music, he became envious.  He recalled the first time he heard Hank Adaline play piano, fingers dancing with unmatched fury in the secret cell of the Violet 9, the two of them splendidly stoned out of their wits on an amalgam of hallucinogens.  It took Hank Adaline tripping into a psychedelic trance to muster the courage to expose his talent.  That was the first time Kane witnessed genius.  Tonight was the second.  Rot in the hell that you yourself created, Hank Adaline.

The one-armed man took a large breath and stuck his one hand into the fire, seemingly unaffected by the heat as he pulled the roasting stench of bird into the star-filled night to serve his people.

Alma:  So, Kane, we were wondering what it means.

Kane:  What?

Alma pointed to her forehead.

Kane:  Is it okay if we don't discuss it?

Leon:  We have a bet going.  I think the artist messed up the fourth letter.  Alma thinks it's not supposed to be a letter, but a symbol.

Leon pointed to the one-armed man, who was pulling meat from the cormorant by the fistful, serenely unaffected by the heat.

Leon:  He thinks you're crazy.  He thinks you have no chance.

Kane:  I guess the tattoo is kind of what brought me here.

Leon:  Everyone has a story.

Alma stopped Kane from lifting a pail of water to his lips.

Alma:  We haven't purified that water yet.

Alma removed several heated stones from the fire and dropped them into the pail to boil the water.

Kane:  Pardon me, but I'm a little amazed by your music.

Leon:  You like music?  He likes music, Alma.

Leon and Alma shared a look.  The one-armed man ate the stinking cormorant in silence, not looking at them, chewing delicately because every bite is an exercise.  He placed great stock in his teeth, as all one-armed percussionists must.  Kane deliberately avoided any glances in the man's direction.

Kane:  Does he really not know English, or are you fooling me again?

Alma:  We leave all pranks to Leon.  Heart of the People is way too solemn a man to play tricks.

Kane:  What's his name?

Leon:  Heart of the People.

Flames crackled in the night.  Heart of the People walked to the wagon and put his mouth under the wine-barrel.  Leon bit a bird leg and passed it to Kane.  The stench was unholy.

Kane:  Thanks, but I'm not hungry.

Alma:  In Ancient Sparta, men ate six times as much as their wives.

Leon:  You know, Kane, Heart of the People is originally from Sudan.  He says cormorant is a delicacy in many Northeast African tribes.  I understand your hesitance to try it, as I was hesitant myself, but my logic is that if human taste buds can develop such a delight for something that it becomes a delicacy in their corner of the world, it can't be so bad.

Kane bit into the cormorant, masticating slowly, tonguing the chewy meat, trying not to smell as he tasted, which proved impossible because the taste was the same as the smell- torturous.  At that point, he would have gladly traded a genocide for a bacon cheeseburger.  He required a tremendous effort to refrain from making faces like a child.  Starvation seemed the sweeter fate.  He passed the leg to Alma.

Leon:  The comic bliss of watching you try to eat that bird makes it worth rescuing you.

Kane:  Glad I can amuse you.

Leon:  I was not entirely truthful with you, Kane- cormorant has never been considered a delicacy anywhere in the world.  The bird has actually earned a reputation for being notoriously foul tasting.

Kane:  I got that.

Leon:  Heart of the People pulled that very trick on me many summers ago.

Kane:  So he has a sense of humor?

Leon:  Humor is innate.  Everyone is born with humor.  Unfortunately, humor can be abandoned.  When I was miserable, back in Bonabal, I always wanted to be a comedian.  I was never very funny, but I noticed that people tend to reap joy in the misery of others.  Our comedies are quite twisted when you think in this perspective- we laugh at the agonist's anguish, and I am the most criminal perpetrator.

In his philosophical Rebel days, Kane Hailand would have embarked on a long-winded diatribe about the role of humor as an aid to fill the void of insecurity.  As a truth-seeker, Kane spent evenings fantasizing about dialectic with the man who sat before him.  A younger Kane would never have seen Leon as a hospitable host, but as an adversary in metaphysical warfare.  The poetic Rebel Kane would have presented an arsenal of counterpoints for every idea anyone could list to him, just to prove that there are no certainties, that his subjective experience is constitutionally valid.  Then he'd turn around to prove that his constitutionality is uncertain.  The philosophically-inclined Kane would have scoured the world in search of the disguised man in front of him if he ever thought there was a possibility that Baltasar Kanaan was still alive and wandering, but the tattooed vagabond, the once-upon-a-time Kane Hailand, could barely stomach the consideration of his host's simple thought.

Leon:  You were navigating at night.

Kane:  Excuse me?

Leon:  When you forfeited your body to the buzzards in acceptance of a strange and beautiful end in the river- you were navigating at night.

Kane:  Well, yeah.  I was-

Leon:  Never navigate at night.

Alma:  You were mentioning before about what brought you out here, Kane.

Kane:  His name is really Heart of the People?

Alma:  He doesn't know we call him that.

Kane:  He's an amazing percussionist.
