Leon taught Kane to craft a dovetail joint to structure the wagon.  Kane slaved, his scarred fingertips burning in an unseen throb.  After hours of work, he became either accustomed or numb to the pain.  Alma awoke before sunrise, nauseous with the child in her womb.  She pulled splinters from her lover's fingers.

A spec of blazing sun appeared above the pink mountains.  That spec of sun ascended, growing into a radiant orange semicircle, and no matter how Kane adjusted his eyes, that sun seemed untouchable and beyond color.  The sun's low angle highlighted Kane Hailand's silhouette on the mountain, beaming strips of light in every direction, reflecting off the land.  Then, as if to remind Kane that the sun is the sun while Kane is but a mortal, the sun rose at a fantastic pace, growing into a holographic disc of light, dyeing the sky with a palette of pastel hues, colorless and blinding, too omnipotent to bear. Leon:  I am.

Kane:  I can go.

Leon:  Your fingers are too indelicate to scavenge.  Your hands are too large.  Besides- he and I have matters to discuss.  Stay here with your lover- wagon-boy.

Kane returned to his wagon-in-progress while Alma played her lyre beside him.  This was Kane's first experience building anything other than a song.  As a superbly intellectual orphan, he was never taught to work with his hands- and as an artist who had achieved international fame, any physical labor required of him was dumped on the stage crew.  For a moment, Kane couldn't find his shadow.  Then it appeared, dancing independently of his motion, tinted red from the sun.

Living her immortal life, she watched the land, servicing the men of all times, studying the evolution of physical love through the ages- how the men tended to her, how they spoke and related with her, how they made love.  Through these men she learned about humanity- she learned that humanity is a body, and each man serves a function akin to that of a blood cell.  Cells bond, divide, die, and regenerate until the being, humanity, ultimately dies.  Mountain Song told Alma that the girl is still alive and she will always be alive, servicing men as she has done for thousands of years.  She lives in a remote village in Iran, and before she services a client she is always sure to say Welcome back.  I have loved you before, as yours is the face of all men.  Though Kane couldn't understand Mountain Song's Arabic, he watched the shepherd paint expressions of delight on Alma's face, and this made Kane quite happy.

Alma (singing and strumming the lyre):  One good thing about music- when it hits you, you feel no pain.

Kane looked up from his woodwork in disbelief.  Alma's voice was soulful- it wasn't as powerful or as styled as Anika's, but it was just as fresh.

Kane (aghast):  That's Bob Marley.

Alma:  You thought I limited myself to classical art?

Kane:  I misjudged you.

Alma:  Unlike you, I was actually alive when Marley played.  My dad drove me two hours to see him play the Deeside Leisure Centre in Chester.  It was his final world tour.  Did you guys ever played the Deeside?

Kane:  We played the O2.

Alma:  Never heard of it.

Kane:  You must've been a little kid at that concert.

Alma:  I was.

Kane:  They let a kid into a Marley show?

Alma:  That's the beauty of his brilliance, Jake.  Even a child can understand it.

Kane:  That was Anika's only rule- no kids at the concert, only eighteen and older admitted.  She didn't want to corrupt them- she thought the youth was too precious.

Alma:  From what I gather of your music, she's right- you wrote a song about screwing the life out of somebody.

Kane paused to think.

Alma:  Let me show you something.

Alma walked toward Kane and manipulated his fingers in a painful stretch over the fretboard of his guitar.  It felt as though she was trying to pry his fingers apart, and each individual digit was isolated in pain.  Even after contorting his hand into a stubborn stretch, she was dissatisfied.  She moved his free hand toward the high end of the fretboard and positioned his fingers over the bottom three strings.

Alma:  Hold that there.

Kane couldn't have moved his fingers if he wanted to because they were stretched so far that they had stiffened.  Only Kane Hailand's large hands could hold this chord.  Alma picked up her lyre and placed her hands in position to play.  With a swift whirl, she strummed both her lyre and Kane's guitar in a fluid fashion.  The sound that rang drove through the soul of the world, carrying all unexplainable desire in its truth.  It was as though whatever notes the two of them played possessed a combination that unlocked the gates of paradise and all of its inhabitants rejoiced.  It made Kane sweat.  It made him shiver. Kane was speechless.  He had heard Hank talk of that very phenomenon- the perfect chord.  The Ancient Greeks claimed that this was the sound that dawned on a sonic scale when the Great Mother created the heavens.  Hank had discovered this chord by theorizing in his head, but he was never able to materialize the sound naturally.  He refused all assistance.  If he didn't do it himself, as it was done when the big bang blasted, he considered it false and insulting.  This frustration, Kane partly believed, caused Hank to abandon the piano- even the Chord of Creation can be made simple with assistance from machines.

Alma:  I never thanked you for what you did.

Kane:  I didn't do anything.

Alma:  You didn't have to take the fall for me.  I'm a big girl.

Kane:  Just some burnt fingers.  It was nothing.

Alma:  I think it was something worthy of a thank you.

Kane:  I'd endure far worse for you.

Alma knew how amazing it felt for Kane to exhale the pain from his past.  He was once a strong man, but he had been broken, and to help him heal into an even stronger man was the most gratifying experience she could ever comprehend.  Looking lustfully at Kane, she said with her eyes everything she desired in her body.  She pulled the knife out of Kane's calloused hand and pounced on top of him.

Kane (inches under Alma):  I can't.

Alma:  You can.

Kane:  I have to finish the wagon.

Alma rose from Kane.

Alma:  You never played hooky before?

Kane (nodding his head toward Mountain Song):  He's watching us.

Alma:  He's sleeping.  Watch this.

She waved her hand over Mountain Song's face.  He made no response.

Kane:  Can I ask you something?

Alma sat beside Kane and lowered his head to her breast, prepared for any question he may have.

Kane:  Leon always says he doesn't want to know about what he left behind, but what if I know that something really terrible has happened to his father-

Alma:  He doesn't want to know.

Kane:  I know how it feels to not know the fate of your own parents, and if I had the opportunity to learn something about my family then I'd do anything for it.

Alma:  You're a very brave man, Jake- braver than you know.  But Leon wants to ignore everything that's happened since he left society.  I think he's up to something, but he'd never admit it to me.

Kane:  What do you mean?

Alma:  I don't really know.  This isn't just an aimless wander, Kane.  Heart of the People is planning something very big, and I'm not quite sure what it might be.

Alma pulled a photograph from her blouse and showed it to Kane.

Alma:  You left this behind when you ran to catch the falling wagon.

Kane observed the photograph, wrinkled and sandy, nearly split down the middle between the two infants as if to pry Kane's grip from the other child's leg.

Alma:  You were a twin.

Kane tried to speak.  He had never before spoken the truth about his birth or that picture, and now that he wanted to, it wouldn't leave his lips.  Alma gazed into Kane's face, divining through the wormhole of his pupils.

Alma:  You don't have to say it.  I know.

Alma stood, stripped naked, and darted into the vast land.  Kane rose, stripped, and chased his frolicking lover.  As the lovers pranced naked into the wilderness, Mountain Song winked one eye open and giggled to himself.


By the time Heart of the People and Leon returned with a pail half-full of dead gerbils, Kane had completed the wagon.  Though the percussionist never said so, Alma told Kane that Heart of the People was impressed with Kane's work.  She said Heart of the People admired a man who took initiative, a man who understood repentance for mistakes.

The next day, the family was set to leave.  Mountain Song had given them a generous amount of vegetables so that they would have something to trade for soap at the bath.  Leon and Alma loaded the wagon while Heart of the People spoke to Mountain Song.  Though Kane couldn't understand a word exchanged between these two great men, he judged by the distance between their faces that their conversation was unmistakably dense.  The family thanked Mountain Song, and Alma left a doll she knitted for the children.  They parted ways.  The family's destination, long overdue, was the most glorious bath in the world.

Following his navigator, Kane pulled the wagon through the sun-drenched outdoors, hiding from the sun, surmising what the most glorious bath in the world could possibly look like.  His burnt fingertips roared in torment as he dragged his new wagon through the desert valley dirt, trailing far behind Heart of the People because the stench of the wolf's pelt on the chieftain's head was insufferable.

The family encountered an abnormally frequent display of wildlife- hundreds of animals ranging from insects to a slobbering pack of rank hyenas that instinctually flocked to Kane.  Sensing the land through his bare feet, Heart of the People beat the drum, the red blade winking in the sunlight at his waist.  Leon played the ney and Alma played her lyre, a black iris in her ear.  With the guitar strung round his neck, Kane aligned his walk to the rhythm of their music so that the body of his guitar caromed off his stomach with every beat.  He was fixated on the phrase Alma whispered to wake him that morning- if you have laughter, you have everything.  What could have inspired her to say this and how could she have summoned the gift of saying something so simple yet so true?  Kane bounced the phrase around his head, shaping it and feeling it for contour and sound.  As a songwriter, a phrase in his head used to terrorize Kane Hailand.  When a phrase appeared in his head he immediately panicked to remove it, as if the phrase were a parasite set to detonate in seconds.  He kept a pen and a pocket-notebook on his person at all times because if the pen didn't remove the parasitical phrase from his head within an instant it would fester and intumesce.  If you have laughter, you have everything.  Alma's phrase was so pleasant.  No matter how he played with this phrase in his cranium, he wanted to continue his play.

The family came to a tributary in their travels.  The water, brown and mucky, running ankle-deep and lined with algae, couldn't possibly have been the most glorious bath in the world.  Heart of the People filled the empty pails with water, filtering euglena and diatom from the murky water through a cloth that Alma stretched over the pail.  Though this water would indeed require an intensive purification process, it was imperative that they refill their empty pails because, as Leon explained, although this particular water would be reduced to mud when compared to the glorious waters that awaited them at the bath, a good traveler prepares for any unexpected hindrance.

Kane:  Can I tell you a story I've never told anybody?

Leon:  Certainly.

Kane:  I want Alma to hear.

Leon:  Alma.

Alma turned back from her great distance ahead.  She lifted her hand from the lyre and waved adorably under the sunlight.

Leon:  Wait there.  Kane has a story to share.

Kane and Leon caught up to Alma.

Alma:  What is it?

Kane:  I never thought I'd tell anyone this.

Kane paused.  Frustrated, he strummed a quick and aggravated chord on his guitar.  Kane removed the crumpled photo from his blue jean pocket.  Alma already knew what he was about to say.

Kane:  Hank Adaline's mom told me she's my mother as well.  She said Hank and I were twins.

Leon:  I thought you grew up in an orphanage.

Kane:  I did.  There's no record of my biological parents.

Leon:  Your parents gave away just one twin?

Kane:  I was left on the doorstep of the orphanage, wrapped in a blanket labeled Jacob- no last name.

Leon:  Would Hank's mother have any incentive to claim to be your mother if it weren't true?

Kane:  I think she needed a better son than Hank.

Alma:  Why?

Kane:  Hanks' mom hates him.

Alma (instinctively protecting her stomach with her hand):  She hates her own son?

Kane:  Hank can't identify with the kid in his baby pictures.  He says he feels nothing when he looks at a picture of himself as a child- he says it's like looking at a picture of a complete stranger.

Leon:  Do you and Hank have the same birthday?

Kane:  There's no record of my birthday.  I have no birth certificate.  I'm not sure that I was ever made a citizen of any country.

Leon:  You carry an American passport.

Kane:  It's a fake.  Our manager had it made so we could tour internationally.

Alma:  What's the birthdate on the passport?

Kane:  September 9th.  Coincidentally, Hank and Anika were both born on September 9th- so I just celebrate their birthday as my own.  It became a holiday among Scoundrels fans.

Leon:  Haven't you investigated this theory that you and Hank are twins?

Kane:  I don't really care.  I never had a mother and I don't need one.  If she didn't want me, then what kind of mother would she have been for me anyhow?

Alma:  But between you and Hank-

Kane:  It wouldn't matter if Hank and I were brothers- it wouldn't change anything.

Alma (holding Kane's hand):  Okay.

Kane:  His mom says we were born fighting.  She says we'll fight all our lives as all men will fight all their lives.  She says Hank will win- she says he's a menace and he doesn't deserve to win but he'll win because he's stronger than me.

Alma:  Do you think that's true?

Kane:  The part about the fighting- sure.  I've been fighting him from the moment I met him.  I'm still fighting him.  If somebody's going to win, it'll be Hank.

Leon:  You don't believe that.

Kane:  Hank Adaline is a hunter, a born attacker.  You should see him on that piano- he has the hands of the devil.  I'm not like that.  I was born simple.

Alma:  I can't find one simple quality in you, Kane Hailand.

Kane pulled the wagon through the muck, his footprints intersecting a strange trail of leopard prints.  All thoughts were consumed by rhythm, the body of the guitar beating against his chest to the tempo of his wagon-pulling.  When at last the family had crossed the river, Kane looked up to see a sight he hadn't beheld in any dream.

Heart of the People stopped the group before a tunnel of trees.  He took several steps into the tree tunnel and sat on a mossy rock aside a miniature stream, pines looming high over their heads.

Leon:  Kane, you are not prepared for what you are to see. I'll take the wagon from here.

Kane surrendered the wagon to Leon, walking forth and looking high into the trees above him.  Scattered sunlight poked through the leaves, diaphanous like a moth-eaten curtain.  The sunlight became stronger as he progressed through his path, until there were no leaves, just sun.  Kane lowered his head.  Ensue bucolic wonder- showtime, draw the curtain.

A mellifluous melody sang through the open chamber and diamonds of sunlight glimmered on the water's surface, chiming tintinnabulations like a glass orchestra.  Kane Hailand stood surrounded by a ring of cliffs coated with greenery, bursting with ethereal delight.  Colorful flowers rained from the trees, enlivening the land.  The people played in the water, naked, blithe and carefree, enmeshed in euphoria.  Opposite Kane, built far into the ring of rock, was a tumbling waterfall.  Alma stripped naked.  Heart of the People and Leon stripped as well.

Alma:  You don't mask your body with clothing, Jake.  Not here.

Shed all clothing and sprint naked.  All his life Kane had been told not to run naked, but Kane was born naked and who are these so-called authorities from his past to tell him, nay, demand of him that he can't be as he was born?  Escaping the chains of cloth persecution, Kane dropped his guitar, removed his sweater, his undershirt, his jeans, and his tattered sneakers.  He wobbled over rocks toward the water.  Heart of the People approached a naked trader for some soap.  The family lifted their instruments, clutching their Animas against their naked flesh.

Leon:  Welcome to the bath.  Heart of the People has requested that you join us in song.

Heart of the People beat the drum with expert rhythm.  Leon attended his ney and Alma's two hands graced the lyre like calculated arachnids.  The birds capped the harmony and the waterfall batted a rhythmic roll onto the water, opening the plants' stomata to breathe the song of the lagoon and enhance the growth of life.  The creatures in the water all turned to revel in the music as Kane brought his burnt fingers to the guitar, aghast in awe, for every moment was a dream.  Before he played each note he listened closely to the others, feeling their sound, eyes closed, forming the shape of their music in his head to discover what notes could perhaps serve as addenda.  Kane Hailand composed to the gap because music, sound, is about silence.  He had never truly listened to music in this fashion, not to his own music or to any other sound- to truly listen and become engulfed in melody so that all the universe is song.  This was a feeling he often provided for others yet had never experienced, and the high splendor of this sacred moment resonated in his soul.  He listened and picked the sounds with his guitar, not thinking but playing- exuding the music.  The family walked toward the water as they played- the drum, the ney, and lyre all guiding Kane's guitar.  His feet ached with every step, but he moved onward, anxious to feel the water's cold relief upon his heated skin.  Choral rock encased the great chamber of the pond, resting sternly in a ring, draped with roots and vines from age-old trees.  Kane stepped into the icy pool, a ring of rock before him and the tunnel of trees behind him.

Once-wandering Kane Hailand was now at one with sanctified nature.

The family stepped into the icy pool, leaving their instruments on the rocks at the edge of the water.  The bath was shaking in coldness.  To the waterfall, he must continue.  Water splashed swiftly into the growing pond, free falling from the sky, spraying misty debris and cooling the naked natural air.  Having eased into the cold, Kane submerged his body and swam, embracing the water as his new coat of freedom.  He kicked lightly, flapping his arms like the wings of an aquatic condor, propelling his body forth, transfixed with the water falling from the sky, unable to locate a source but content knowing that the water cascaded from the land above unto his humble head.  Splash lightly, gently, cool and pleasant- surreal.  Earthly pleasures cum divine- listen to the crackle of the water, pattering infinitely on the level surface above Kane Hailand's head as he communicated with colorful fish.  The waterfall is God's music, and not even Hank Adaline's piano could contend.  Mist, wetness, pleasure heretofore unknown- solace in solitude among the masses.  Kane shared this moment with all who were there, all who were here.  The Sirens had left long ago, yet their song was still embedded within the mossy crags and plummeting water.  The flowers, trees, rocks, and people joined in hand, cohabiting in merriment.

At last Kane reached the fall.  He held his singed hand under the falling water and watched closely as the droplets broke upon his palm like gentle explosions, small in space but epic in magnitude, healing his burns.  Water fell white and cold and made him feel alive.  He kicked off the wall and away from the fall, the mist landing lighter upon his tattooed face.  Two hands cradled his head, and he felt Alma's naked breasts smooth and slippery on the flesh of his back.  He felt her body wrap around his, enveloping him in love, the blooming product of their two souls brewing in her womb.  Embracing Kane, naked, wearing her badge of flesh in Eden, Alma spoke into his soul.

Alma:  Look up.

Kane abided.   The pale blue sky affronted by the horseshoe cliffs, the vines, the raining flowers, and the mermaid's song were all in beautiful harmony, but oh, although they were fantastic, superb and wondrous in sight and delight, they seemed to all exist for the central life, the all-purveyor, the catalyst- the Waterfall.  High above, painted a golden white hue of an angel's aureole by the high sun above, the world froze and the fall became an optical illusion seemingly frozen like a solid mass in the non-existence of time.  A flash amidst the sun, just over the quieted cliffs- a flash, a moment, brief, but strong and ever-enduring- God.  Kane saw God in the water.  He recognized God in an instant just as surely as one recognizes one's self.  Cradled in his lover's embrace, a smile stretching over his face, Kane spoke silently to his great Creator who stopped the world to speak to him.  Thank you, Kane said, for this sweet earth runs on your breath, and all is right.  Kane smiled at the water and the flowers hanging over the fall, brushed by serene sunlight.  Floating with the water and the fish and the people in the mountains, all was right.

Alma and Kane bathed each other.  Kane plucked a raining flower from the air and placed it behind Alma's ear.  She placed an identical flower in his ear.  He stood, wet and cool and clean.  A cool caress of wind kissed Kane's moistened flesh.  Water came down from the sky.  Kane basked in the amazing and rarified gift of rain.  Looking into the waters for the first time since he had stumbled into wilderness, Kane saw his reflection.  Wavy and contorted in the rain-rippled bath, he examined his countenance.  His tattoo, when reversed in reflection, appeared as he had originally intended it.  He still couldn't make out its meaning.  A horizontal line of cracked skin slashed across the tattoo where he habitually scrunched his brow.  His hair had grown considerably, looking almost as it looked before he ever cut his hair to form The Scoundrels and don the Jester's hat.  His beard, now full, was brilliant and tawny, robust and full of character- far more comfortable and natural than his trademark mustache from his days as a Jester for The Scoundrels.  He felt contentedness, a feeling he hadn't felt since Anika had taken his feelings away.  His hair and eyes, renewed in vitality, were no longer the hair and eyes of Kane Hailand, international phenomenon, Jester and God, controller of light- these were the hair and eyes of Jake, the luster-struck adolescent poet who had yet to ever happen upon the maddened piano genius.

The rain ceased, and the land emanated the sweet smell of petrichor.  Kane's reflection became full and clear and unified.  The family dried in the gentle wind and resumed their clothing and their instruments.  Kane grabbed the wagon-handle, and they wandered back through the tunnel of trees from whence they came- beneficent fortune had even been so kind as to prompt Heart of the People to leave his stinking wolf's head behind.

Kane:  On the internet.

Alma:  People actually use the internet?

Alma:  Kids have always chosen what music was popular.  The Beatles, Elvis, any big name you want to throw out there, they've never had many fans that were older than them.

Kane:  Why do you think?

Alma:  Kids are the only listeners who are open to change.  Without kids, music would never evolve.  The youth gives us change- they give us evolution.  They ensure that we're never settled in our stubborn ways.  That's why the youth is so precious.

Kane:  I used to consider my songs to be my children.

Alma:  Looking after so many kids can make you crazy.

Kane:  Hence the tattoo.

Kane:  I had a favorite kid.

Alma:  Which one?

Kane:  Light Shattered- the song I wrote about the Baltasar Kanaan's- Leon's- essays on cosmology.

They did this at Mountain Song's abode and again at the bath.

One method, which Leon didn't particularly care for, was to observe moss on trees- in the northern hemisphere, moss always grows thicker on the southern side of the tree.  The sun and stars, Leon said, were most dependable, except for when it wasn't sunny or when the stars were occluded.  Never use the moon to navigate- the moon will always fool you.  Pay attention to heat and light- due to the path of the sun, rocks and trees are lighter and slightly hotter on the sides that face southeast to southwest.  Heart of the People is so skilled in this aspect of navigation that he can sense heat with his skin.  Wind and shadows, those that aren't there, can be of inestimable value.

The child, about six years old by Alma's estimation, ravaged the prey with the wolves.  Balancing on all fours, stark naked, he tore the raw flesh from the prey using only his teeth, clenching his jaws, shaking his head with great vigor to tear the flesh, driblets of blood speckling his dirt-strewn face.  The family watched from the hills above as the boy growled at a wolf that wished to share the carcass.  A wolf was showing teeth with its slavering jaws, eyes set and determined to teach the boy a lesson in eat or be eaten, and this human child shows his teeth right back.  The boy dived face-first into the prey, gnawing at raw flesh.  The vagabonds watched in amazement.

Alma:  We have to save him.

Leon:  It's not our responsibility to save that boy.

Alma (a protective hand over her stomach, with conviction):  It most certainly is.

Leon:  What happens, Alma?  We save the child, and then what?

Alma:  We teach him to love.

The child pranced on all fours, wrestling and playing with the wolf pack.  At times the child stood on two legs, galloping awkwardly with a hunched back, hands cupped and stiff like claws.

Leon:  This is a boy who has been raised by wolves, Alma.

Alma:  He's still a human child.

Leon:  Do you expect this boy who knows nothing of his own species to learn to love us?  Do you expect him to find his Anima?  We would be his captors, Alma.

Alma:  I don't see it that way.

Leon:  Do you wish to give this boy him a name?

Alma:  Of course.

Leon:  Who are we to name this child?

Alma:  We named Heart of the People.

Leon:  He doesn't acknowledge that as his name!

Below, the boy ran his fingers through the coat of one of the wolves, picking insects from the wolf's fur.  After cleaning the wolf, he lay on the ground for several wolves to lick him.  One of the wolves licked a small open wound at the boy's hip, sanitizing the child as any caring mother would clean her son who had come home dirty from play.

Leon:  He certainly won't name himself- a feral child knows no language.

Alma:  How do you know he's a feral child?

Leon:  Look at him.  He acts as a wolf, fighting against them for his share of the kill.  This boy is no longer human.

Alma:  We could teach him to be like us.

Leon:  There's a critical period in human development in which children reach a point where they are no longer capable of developing certain civilized constructs, like language.

The boy pranced with the wolves- slavering, sniffing, clawing, and spitting.  When the wolves howled the child howled in an equally perfect tone, speaking with the wolves as it could never speak to Alma.  Two wolf cubs sucked milk from their mother's teats, and the fondness in the child's eye suggested to Kane that the boy might have been raised on that same milk.  Kane knew almost nothing about children other than that they thought in marvelous questions, they were known to cry in public, and they contorted their faces for amusement- but this child raised by wolves seemed a stranger to tears and funny faces.

Kane:  He looks happy.

Alma:  He can be happier with us.

Leon:  I have expressed my sentiments about taking this boy in, yet you remain obstinate.  I have a proposal for you, Alma.

Alma:  Okay.

Leon:  We test Kane's ability.  If the child gravitates toward Kane, as we have witnessed all animals gravitate toward Kane, then the child may be said to have the blood of the wolf, and therefore we cannot adopt him as our own.

Alma:  And if he stays put?

Leon:  Then you may try to coax him along with us- granted he seems to oblige.

Alma (squeezing Kane's hand):  Go ahead.

Kane walked forth.  The wolves dashed to meet him.  Alma prayed that the child would stay while the wolves jumped for Kane.   She wished to foster the boy, to make a home for him and nurture him to grow with her family.  Alma was enamored with every child she ever saw, but this particular boy was special.  Leon was right- the child wasn't quite human.  To Alma, the child was an angel.  Though the budding life inside her belly was promising enough to heal her health, the presence of a living child in her life- for her to raise and teach him love and love only so that he may live in harmony, was a prospective resurrection. This was to be the culmination of her life's work.  Children are supposed to see things the rest of us have lost the ability to see, they are supposed to play fantastic games that we've forgotten the rules to- children surf waves that we've forgotten we once surfed.  The light of God in the child's eye told Alma that this was to be fate.  And fate spoke- the child did not move with the wolves.

The immediacy of this boy becoming her child was overwhelming that for a moment Alma became so light-headed that she nearly swooned.  Excitedly, Alma followed Kane toward the child who had not moved with the wolves.  Shedding all sickness, Alma darted across the field for her boy.  The child, startled at the presence of this strange being, glowered threateningly at Alma.  She opened her arms in a gesture of love, to say I will be your mother and I will give you all I have.  The child, apparently eager to live in his new home, trotted toward Alma with awkward speed.  Nearly crying with joy, she anticipated the coming embrace with a mother's love, foreseeing a grand vision of the child jumping into her open arms.  The boy raced toward Alma with desire in his eyes.

He tackled her to the ground, clawing her stomach with ungroomed fingernails, snapping his jaws, biting her swollen stomach in vicious offense before fleeing into the wilderness as Alma wailed mercy.

What functions will he serve who survives man?  Hope squandered, mistrusting of solace, Alma was reminded of a quote she read in Aristotle- without law, man is the worst of animals.

Alma (beaten and bleeding):  It all goes so fast, doesn't it?


Two days later, Alma miscarried her pregnancy.


* * *



Track 6: The Nameless Stranger


Alma broke from a vicious dream into an even grimmer reality.  She opened her eyes to no effect.  Silver-styled patterns flowed through her vision in a way that made everything seem invisible.  The family had been staying in a cave by the sea for nearly a lunar cycle, and every wakeup since she lost the baby had been dimmer than the wakeup before, her vision fast fading along with her life, the silver-spotted patterns having morphed into blobs that bond like blood cells to form an inescapable field of silver impressions.  The silver-streaked flurry of Alma's vision darkened into a cavernous disco-ball of geodesic light, and beat by beat the silver spots have dimmed to a blind black.  Is blackness, she wondered dimly, eternal and infinite, or is it paper-thin and no larger than my eyeholes?  She was cripplingly exhausted.  God, she had discovered, will never grant her a child.

The sun had not yet risen and there was no scent of her lover.  She felt for Kane beside her, slapping her hand against the cold cave floor because no one was there.  Tears streamed slowly down her nose and her hair as she lay, a crushed lotus tucked behind her ear, her once-amorous eyes now glazed over like dewy blue marbles.  Her brain told her body to follow the vibration of Kane's sonorous guitar, but her body wouldn't comply.  She accepted her impending death because her duty to the rolling passage of the human species will be accomplished when Kane Hailand finds his Anima in the guitar.

Alma had confusedly lost track of day and night, and she was far too embarrassed to ask for assistance.  She convinced herself that Kane never slept.  This was incorrect.  In fact, Kane slept cozy in her arms through each night, the six guitar strings permanently indented in the nape of his neck- but no matter how closely Kane slept beside Alma, Kane always slept alone because Alma wasn't fully there.

While Alma had been slowly stepping into darkness, Kane was reclaiming his abilities with light.  Other performers tried to exercise their creativity by creating laser light shows with fantastic color, yet the laws that govern light confined those who use light as a tool.  Kane Hailand created the laws that govern light, and as their creator, he knew what lay beyond them.  Whenever a melody materialized in Kane's head, he felt a tingling glow in his fingertips, marking a faultless intuition that guided him to stab the perfect note.  Kane had no shadow in the cave.  While Leon and Heart of the People spent their days walking, eating, and trading with herdsmen, Kane spent his days playing music.  He worked tirelessly at his guitar in hopes that one day soon he will conquer the instrument and become the mystic that nurses Alma back to health- Alma hadn't yet told Kane that she resolved to die.

Kane Hailand watched Alma wake.  It was late afternoon and the sunlight crept into the cave.  Absorbing Alma's effortless grace, Kane morphed with his guitar to let it sing his every thought- the slight curve of her spine, vertebrae by vertebrae, streaking down her back from a billow of floral-scented chestnut hair to her ambrosial femininity hiding beneath the hand-stitched quilt, with a scent that can only be described as Alma, the slow draws of her sweet-breathing harmony, the ever-wrenching melancholia of a woman in sorrow, wishing to bring her back, to reignite her hope with a child inside her that will recreate her will to endure.  This type of thought used to irk Kane in the days of Anika Handel, but with Alma he was able to shed all burdens through the notes of his guitar so that all that remained were thoughts of love, thoughts of peace- Kane Hailand had never thought these thoughts.

Alma whispered his name through a thin rasp of her delicate beauty.  Kane offered no response because Kane was in the Combat Sphere, the centered vault of the Rebel's thought in which he can be bothered or distracted by nothing.  He'll play his guitar until the sun moves to set because when the sun sets it will be setting to Kane's music- Kane Hailand will set the sun.  He had carved grooves into the fretboard so that his hand could rest more comfortably when playing the Chord of Creation with Alma.  But Alma no longer expressed much interest in her lyre.

The song Kane was currently playing, Alone in Myth, was the last song that Kane Hailand The Jester ever wrote for The Scoundrels, about the cyclic destruction of man in his search to outdo the beauty endowed to him by God.  Hank Adaline refused to record Alone in Myth.  He never even wrote a piano accompaniment.  When Kane tattooed his forehead and fled into the wilderness, Alone in Myth was nothing more than a series of sketched notes in a notepad, a graphite-scratched representation of every unrealized beauty that Kane never knew- now it was a song, interpreted through the six strings of Kane's guitar.  Alone in Myth was a plea for someone to come along and heal all destruction, while Kane himself had just healed the broken fragments of Alone in Myth- Kane Hailand was living his Art.  This was yet another new Kane Hailand, the neophyte warrior of song.

The family first settled in the cave when Alma took sick, because the cave provided the entropic sense of shelter required for her recuperation.  Kane felt a certain sense in which there was nowhere to go and another sense in which it was okay that there was nowhere to go because the cave was lovely- every so often Kane would hear the delicate pluck of a moist drop falling from the hanging stalactites, and it always sounded wonderfully akin to Alma's lyre.  The cave's acoustic chamber of branchwork rock gave the music a physical body like a natural amphitheater on the shore.  Kane played his guitar, striving to revitalize his lover with every note.

Heart of the People had set up his tent in the cave.  He and Leon spent much of their time in this tent.  Kane secretly joked with Alma about the paradoxical implications that come with pitching a tent inside a cave, but to his leader and to Leon he didn't dare question their conduct.  As far as they knew, Kane Hailand's only preoccupation was his attack on the guitar.

Dutifully, Kane attacked his guitar, his stomach churning queasily to grind the meal of locusts from the night before.  Though scavenges and hunts had been weak, Kane learned to covet the slight hunger.  Food was copious when he was a bona fide rock star, and even when he lived in the orphanage he had never truly been hungry.  The organic struggle with his own blooming physicality made him feel alive, but Kane could not be bothered by his physicality in this moment because Kane was in the Combat Sphere, playing Alone In Myth, and all was music to Kane.  When alas he played the closing refrain, a somber trail of hopeful notes on the bottom two strings he couldn't name, he rose from the rocks to fetch water for Alma.

Lately Alma had been exceptionally weak upon wakeup.  Her sleep-sessions were becoming more frequent and more painful. She no longer dreamt in pictures, only in black sound.  At first this was terrifying, but she soon became accustomed as she would with any change.  Exerting all waking effort, Alma clapped a timid round of applause for Alone in Myth.

Kane (pouring water into Alma's mouth):  You know, The Scoundrels discouraged applause.

Alma (a sip, tightening her stomach to muster a reply):  Why?

Alma coughed.  It consumed her.  Kane nursed her calmly until she could breathe again.

Kane:  Clapping is such an arbitrary act.  So, instead of clapping, our fans would shout the name of whatever song they wanted to hear next.  Whatever title caught my fancy was the song we'd play.

Alma:  That's just as arbitrary.

Kane:  So it is- I never thought about it that way.

A stranger stumbled into the cave.  Clad in denim jeans and a chenille overcoat, hair close-cropped and face freshly-shaven, with a lit cigarette in his trembling hand, he was foaming at the mouth with one eye swollen shut, flailing his arms, sputtering nonsense.  Heart of the People and Leon emerged from the tent, noses piqued to investigate.  Kane moved to follow them.

Leon:  Stay with Alma.

Kane dropped the guitar and darted toward Alma, shielding her from the rabid lunatic in the cave.  Alma, blind to all, heard only terror in her family's voices, the gargles of the madman, teetering in an arrhythmic clamor of rocky footsteps- the cacophonous music of monsters with no faces.  Kane was mesmerized.  Here was a man who looked like no human Kane had seen since he fled his former life- a clean-shaven, olive-fleshed, greasy-haired kid who showed no visible indications of the dirt-smudged skin that plagues a nomad- and he entered their home to have a seizure.  Heart of the People and Leon paced toward the stranger, exercising as much caution as if they had spotted a sleeping shark.

Heart of the People shouted, but the stranger couldn't speak to answer.  He only doddered forth in his stupor, gurgling spit-dried nothingness, trying not to swallow his tongue.

Leon:  Who are you?

The stranger dropped his cigarette, nearly falling over.  It was necessary that Leon and Heart of the People continue to speak in both Arabic and English, as they were unsure which language, if either, the incapacitated stranger understood.

Heart of the People screamed in his Arabic.  Leon followed with translation.

Leon:  We are here to help.

The stranger continued convulsing in an epileptic apoplexy.  Leon became more desperate, shouting in a muddle of all ten of his languages, all of which seemed ineffective.

Kane (shouting):  For God's sake, help him!

Kane hugged Alma beneath him, crushing her with a protective instinct because there was a complete stranger making violent noises in her home, and she knew this but she couldn't see it happening.

The stranger collapsed to the cave floor.  A letter flew out from his coat.  Leon stooped to read the letter.  When evidently he had finished, he turned to his chieftain with a stupefied look of alarm.  Leon and Heart of the People proceeded in Arabic, conversing as the nameless stranger screamed his way through a violent seizure, not in language but in sound, mangled on the cave floor.

With his one arm, Heart of the People unsheathed the blade at his waist.

This was the first time Kane saw the oft-pondered object of his curiosity- a double-sided red-diamond-studded dagger of saw-toothed red steel containing an amber-sealed human eyeball in the butt of a handle made of pure ruby.  Kane's stomach lurched into a squirming mass of lead and he nearly vomited locusts on Alma.  The convulsing stranger tried to utter prayers but instead sprayed spittle in the cave.  Kane recalled the fiery punishment he once accepted for the presence of the glass vial.  With a conviction that he never knew until then, Kane was certain that he did the right thing in accepting the punishment.  He did it for Alma, because maybe he should love her and maybe she deserved to be loved, because there was a part of him that knew he must atone for all the selfish harm that he inflicted upon others.  But to think that Heart of the People- Kane struggled to produce the words in his head.  Something inside him didn't want to face whatever he sensed the ruby knife would bring.

Leon bowed his consent to Heart of the People and accepted the blade.  Remorsefully, unblinking, Leon drifted toward Kane and Alma, the blade resting on his palms.  Alma struggled to breathe under the terror of Kane's desperate clutches.  The cave smelled like death.  Leon approached, closer, as Alma shivered in threatening pain.  Leon laid the blade before Kane.

Leon:  Kill him.

Kane watched Leon's face for a smirk or a slight twinge in his brow or any other unknown subtlety that could possibly signal for twisted humor, but what he saw was the usual somber black-beaded eyes, the chain of islet moles leading from Leon's eye to his two loops of whacky beard, the defeated countenance of the man who once transformed Kane Hailand's worldview, ordering him to kill.

Kane (trying to fake a laugh):  What?  No.

Leon said nothing.

Kane:  I'm not gonna kill him.

Leon (sighing):  This isn't a request, Kane.

Kane (shielding Alma, whimpering beneath him):  You don't give me any credit.  You don't see how far I've come.  It's a test.  It's a stupid test and I'm beyond this.

Leon:  It's not a test.

Kane:  I remember everything you told me- violence is the weapon of the weak.

Leon:  Look at me, Kane.  This man has been bit by the Xantippe cobra.  The venom will have eaten him long before we can reach help.  He is numb now, but in two minutes he will suffer the worst agony known to nature, and it will follow him into death.  You have a responsibility toward your fellow man.

The stranger's seizure heightened in violence, sending spasms of fright from his nerve center and out into the cave, the perilous sound of a man at his end.

Leon:  Kane!

Kane lunged for the ruby blade and hurled it into the dark depths of the cave.  To test him like this, to order him to kill a stranger on the grounds that some unknown animal had bitten the man- Leon has demonstrated his extraordinary survival skills in the past, but could he really recognize a particular snakebite without even seeing the wound?  For Leon to think that he could toy with Kane's psyche as he had just done was a move that was both narcissistic and hard-hearted, a biting insult to all of the progress Kane felt he had made- so Kane responded fittingly, by tossing Heart of the People's red blade into the craggy depths of the cave.  He could accept Leon's practical pranks, the jokes at Kane's expense, even the scorched fingertips for the spilled wagon, because all previous suffering was in good faith and consistent with the philosophies of Heart of the People's teachings.  It was part of the game, and it didn't matter that he never signed up to play because until now he was enjoying himself and he was growing.  Now these people had become something vastly different from the personas that guided Kane these past few seasons.  They were supposed to be his tutors, the altruistic and principled souls who gave him something to believe in when he never believed in anything.  Leon, the man who uttered peace in reverence above all other holies, was now trying to fool Kane into relapsing in sin, to murder a perfect stranger of whom he knew nothing except that the man needed medical assistance because he was a victim of some evil ordeal- all of this while the stranger suffered helplessly on the floor.  Kane looked to Alma.  If this was a test- she couldn't be in on it- she wouldn't-

Leon said nothing.  He only sauntered after the red blade.  Fetching the knife, he began a path toward the infested stranger on the floor.  He stopped and brushed his free hand through his braided beard.  He closed his eyes and exhaled.  Pinching the tip of the knife between three fingers, Leon threw the red blade like a cartwheeling rocket into the stranger's windpipe, severing his spinal column, ceasing his seizure, and sending the man into immediate paralysis.  Blood sprayed like mist.  Heart of the People moved tranquilly forth.  The one-armed percussionist dislodged the blade from the stranger's windpipe.  Stoically, the man who Kane was supposed to venerate as promethean slit the nameless stranger's throat, jutted his one hand into the open incision, and clawed the lifeless head back until it was attached to its former body by only several thin-strung bloody tendons which Heart of the People snipped with a cool stroke of his red ruby blade.  The one-armed beat-man completed this process with a calm ease, making it plainly evident that this was not his first execution.  He foraged a wooden pike from somewhere outside the cave and placed the head on top.

Leon kneeled in a pool of blood, squatting in his moccasins to examine the headless body.  He approached Kane, the letter in hand, leaving a trail of bloody footprints.  Alma shrieked and whimpered in the constricting arms of her lover, imprisoned in her visionless blackness though she could smell her lover's fear, his quickened heat-breath on her forehead, his clammy sweat on her skin.

Alma (whispering to Kane):  What's happening?

Kane (whispering through cries):  They murdered a man.  They murdered, they murdered, they murdered, they murdered.  Leon murdered a stranger.

Leon dropped the letter before Kane.  Kane's hands trembled and his eyes teared.  Mechanically, he unfolded the paper- written on isosceles-triangular Scoundrels stationery, a pastel cartoon of each respective bandmate in each of the three angles, Hank the left, Kane the top, and Anika the right, The Scoundrels stenciled lightly over the center.  Written in cursive ink over images of the band, the contents of the letter were as follows.


To my sweet sister Marieta,

I am writing to you in English so that Mutter will not read this.  How is she?  I wish to Jesus that I had money I could send you, but money has been difficult to find.  Much has changed since I last wrote.  By the time you are reading this I will be far into my journey to Greece.  Yes, dear sis, I am coming to see you. Our family will be together for the first time since Vater died.   I had a dream the other night that he was alive and we were eating Mutti's moussaka.  I am afraid, Marieta.  I have always been afraid but now I am afraid and desperate too. The reason for my journey home is not so wonderful.  I must address Anika Handel's declining health.  I wonder how it is by you, but I imagine the Greeks are taking it harshly.  She always had a space in her violet heart for Greece.  And with this news of Kane Hailand disappearing gone, it seems as though our dreams are rotting slowly.  I hear people saying that Hank Adaline has recorded new music.  I wish with all my heart to hear his piano once again, but this poor country I am living in has banned the music.  I don't know what message Hank's new music may be saying, but I imagine it to be a riot. I once saw a movie of Hank playing the deejay (do I say this right?).  They showed it on the news, in a story that warned the people of Hank Adaline as a shaitan- a devil and a menace.  Watching his hands with the records is like watching a riot.  Part of me thinks maybe he is talking about justice, and that is why this unjust government has banned the music.  I don't understand the music.  I wish that you can write to me and tell me of the sound.  But it must be that I cannot hear from you until I find you at home.  I have heard also, through a source I must not name in this letter, that Hank is touring the world with his music and that he will be playing at the Parthenon on the eve of the new year. He left America because he says Americans no longer understand music.  His new shows are not like The Scoundrels shows, I hear.  It is not a theatre show with lights and animals.  I hear that Hank Adaline, yes, the Red Shadow, is just traveling from country to country to play music for the people.  I have collected enough money to buy a plane ticket to Athens, and so I journey to the airport in Makhraj.  Do not concern yourself with how I have gotten this money.  I will repay my debts, I assure you, as Vater always taught us.  But I must see this performance.  I must.  I feel that if I don't see this performance then my heart will cry forever.  And you and Mutter will come with me to share these hopes in times of sadness.  The show, of course, is free.  It costs nothing to go. He is just playing.  Not for money.  Just for people.   Perhaps I will stay with you in Greece for a while. I have been thinking about this a lot.   I know there is no money to be earned, but maybe it will be easier to find food with a man's help.  Maybe I am wrong.  But what is there that can be worse?  Do not repeat any of this to Mutter.  I know what she will say.  I pray that my love for you and Mutti will guide me to your door, and we can find hope in Hank's music at the Parthenon, where our ancestors have sought hope in the past.  And may God bless The Quaquaversal (how do I spell this?) with new health.

P.S.  These people really think Hank is the devil.


The letter was unsigned.

Leon (a sly snicker):  So that's what The Jester looks like.  Nice eyepatch.

Something unknown festered inside of Kane.  No matter how he tried to control whatever this feeling was inside of him, he could sense it growing to possess his being.

Leon:  This is a sign, Kane.  This man was sent here for you.

Everything Kane Hailand had come to believe in, everything he found in the wilderness that he never found in his societal life was turned upside-down and beaten in the form of Heart of the People's bloody knife and Leon's serene brow.  These men were able to weigh the scales of justice under the highest-pressure conditions, to take a man's life without guilt, but Kane failed to summon this ability within his self.  Kane's leaders finally trusted him with a task that demanded courage and strength, but Kane didn't have the courage to act.  He was betrayed by his own judgment, betrayed by the society that had tamed him, betrayed by the land that was now supposed to foster him.  He was worthless.  Kane slammed his guitar into the cave walls, just as Hank Adaline used to demolish the top of his grand red piano, so intense and in the moment that it was no longer apparent to Kane that he was spraying chocks of wood like a chipper, smashing the guitar into the wall, beating the cave in hopes that it will crumble because this is the apotheosis of passion, whack whack whack until all that remained in Kane's hands were a few broken strings hanging from a split guitar neck.  A perturbing twang resonated from the defiled instrument to fill the cave with violence.

Without ever having known what materials composed the guitar or how it was made or even how to play it completely, Kane smashed his guitar into sawdust and splinters, beating the absolute inadequacy out of the instrument.  Heart of the People flashed his red eyes with a vengeance, shooting his fire at the wood in Kane's hands.  Kane tossed the flaming wood to the ground.  The one-armed arsonist threw a fist of fire at Kane's blue sweater, sending Alma's woven labor of love up in flames.  Shaking free from the searing sweater, the burns heating in his chest, Kane stomped the flames, reducing his sweater into pungent ash.  Knowing he would never be able to combat Heart of the People, Kane slouched to the floor, defeated.  Leon picked splinters of guitar from his hair and his beard.  Smoke filled the cave.

Leon:  Kane-

Kane could feel the fury tensing in the sinews of his neck, blood screaming in his brain.

Kane:  You don't even know who this man is!  You don't know anything about him.  How did you know you could kill him?

Leon:  There's much about us that you still have yet to learn.

An odd series of cramps knotted themselves around Kane's insides.  He had always been second best to Hank.  Kane would never prosper as long as Hank existed. Even after he found people who actually granted him an opportunity, Kane still couldn't prosper because he always relied on Hank to prosper for him and he never learned how to prosper through his own merits.  Kane finally put a name to the feeling that was brewing inside him- it was spite.  Kane Hailand was always possessed by spite for everything that was better than he was- spite for Hank Adaline, for Heart of the People, for Leon, for the incalculable world and all of its unanswerable demands.  Still panting from his violent outburst, Kane stood to stare Leon in the face.

Kane:  Your dad is dead, Leon.  He killed his self, mid-sentence, on national television, and he did it because he couldn't handle the grief you left him with.  He did it like he thought you did it, with a shotgun in his throat.  Your dad's dead and it's your fault because you couldn't handle reality.

Kane slumped back against the wall and stared at the dead man. The nameless stranger was no longer an inspired idealist because he was dead and his head will soon decay on the pike outside the cave, distended jaw hung low and leaking blood, eyes just barely open, rolled high and unblinking, streaming fresh red blood from its detached throat.  The head looked more like one of Hank's whacky stage props for The Hounds of Anger than anything that could have ever possessed living hope.

Leon stood over Kane, still in shock.  Kane's anger didn't permit him to acknowledge Leon, though there was a tiny voice inside of him that begged for Leon to slap him and do something horrible that Kane fully deserved.  Kane tried to justify his actions to himself.  He told himself that nothing really mattered, when in actuality he was afraid of the truth that had been trying to sing to him since birth.  On some basic level that he didn't quite understand, Kane could hear these truths in song- but he ignored them, and he never felt more pathetic.

Without blinking, Leon looked at the dead body below him.

Leon:  He hasn't been in the wilderness long.

Kane (affected, forgetting his spite):  How do you know?

Leon:  He's close-shaven.  He wears sneakers, like you.

Kane:  He doesn't even have a name.

Leon:  Pardon?

Kane:  He doesn't have a name.  There's no name in the letter, no name in his clothing.  He has no identification.  You killed this man and you never even knew his name.

Leon:  Yes.  It's awful.

Kane:  We invent names all the time.  We name things, we name ourselves, we name other species- but he dies without a name.

Leon:  I'm sure he has a name, Kane.  It's just unknown to us.

Kane:  If we can't name ourselves, then it's the end.  We're done.

Leon:  Calm down.  You're getting crazy.  It's only a name, Kane.

Kane:  Who are you if you don't have a name?

Leon:  You can't name one note on your guitar, and yet you produce wonderful music.

Leon left Kane with the body.  Kane looked to Alma.  She was shivering, cold and alone.  He rushed toward her and adjusted her blanket, holding her close to keep her warm, whispering into her ear, caressing the teeth-marked scar on her emaciated belly, promising to rescue her from all of it, even if it costs him his life, because he finally realized that she's the only good thing that ever happened to him and he refused to ever lose her- it took him long enough to learn this but he learned it and he won't forget.  In his ephemeral delirium he really thought that he could carry her for days across the desert to a hospital, that she would recover and the two of them would live modestly in solitude with their many children, playing the strings of their instruments to seek everlasting harmony and live as lovers do.  He never considered that he lacked the proper survival skills, that he had absolutely no orientation or awareness of his surroundings, and that she was weakened so near to death.  Alma breathed in his ear, for he gave her the energy to be, and she used this energy to soothe him because it was her duty to stay alive as long as it would take to save him, to tell him all is right if only he can counter his own past.  But Kane could not be soothed.  Alma reached for her lyre.  She hadn't strummed the lyre in what seemed like a lifetime, and she couldn't find it in the darkness.  Kane, whom she knew through his touch and his scent, must be soothed.  So she sang.

Alma (singing):  One good thing about music- when it hits you, you feel no pain.

Kane's rage evaporated into a tearful sickness.  Somehow even the song of his lover incensed him with guilty fury.  Kane kissed Alma harder than was necessary on her cheek.  He carried her to the cave entrance, avoiding the crawling rivulets of blood.  He originally brought her to the entrance so that she could experience light.  Upon rethinking, he realized just how dumb this was because light had long left her.  Yet he continued with his actions, stroking his lover's hair in the grass, unsure of whom to trust.  His inner processor couldn't choose among the swirl of issues that swam in his head, so he thought nothing.

Leon and Heart of the People approached with the loaded wagon.

Leon:  We must go.

Kane:  Goodbye.

Leon dropped two sweaters on Kane's lap.

Leon:  You two change out of those bloody clothes.  Then help me carry Alma to the wagon.

Kane rose to argue Leon.

Leon:  You're not staying.

Kane:  It's fine.

Leon:  Kane, this is a sign.  Our exile has passed.

Kane:  What are you talking about?

Leon:  I must go back to civilization.  I must go back to Bonabal.

Kane:  There's absolutely nothing you could say that would make me go to Bonabal.

Leon:  You're not coming to Bonabal.

Kane:  Are you insane?

Leon:  I thought you'd like to be the one who escorts Alma.

Kane:  What are you talking about?

Alma (a verbal spasm):  Greece!

Kane turned toward Alma, walking slowly toward his ailing lover.  Her ear to the dusty ground, she heard his footsteps coming closer and she felt for his face.

Alma:  I'm dying, Jake.

Kane tried to look into her eyes, but that amazing unity he used to feel when he looked into those sapphire eyes was now gone, returning nothing but a blank face, a black hole of energy.  He breathed her wan complexion, eyes glazed and blue, unblinking and lachrymal in the occluded barrier of her cornea, her shivering lip, her once-flowing hair now stringy and whitening.  His mind knew the truth, but he couldn't form the words that would allow him to really understand, leaving him feeling like an empty vessel, unaffected by reality.

Kane:  We'll take you to a hospital.

Kane looked up at Leon.

Kane:  We'll take her to a hospital.

Leon:  She's dying, Kane.

Kane:  They can help her.  Modern medicine is amazing.  They've made so many advances since you left.  I promise you- they can help her.

Alma:  Jake.  Listen to me.

Alma traced a fingertip over the curvature of Kane's nose, absorbing his tears in her tight skin.

Alma:  I want to die in Greece.

Leon:  Will you take her?

Kane collapsed beside Alma.  His earth was getting colder.  Consumed by the approaching winter, he couldn't think.  Winter dampens the earth, and a dampened earth will dampen thought.  Kane was once able to recognize the beautiful natural phenomenon of winter, but his thoughts were too dampened to recognize this now.  He never believed Anika.  He never believed that she was dying.  She never went to the doctor.  She continued, if not increased her smoking when she said she got the diagnosis.  Kane was never sure that Anika Handel was dying in the way that she said she was dying, the way that Alma was actually dying.  No.  He had to confront it.  He abandoned Anika when she was dying.  Face it.  He abandoned her.  He abandoned her just like he abandoned Hank on the most meaningful night of their lives, their masterpiece- Train of Power.  He abandoned Hank and Anika as Hank and Anika had both abandoned him, because that's what they do, these Scoundrels, they fill each other full of hope and then abandon.  He had already abandoned someone he loved, and he couldn't endure it again.

Kane:  I have no choice.

Leon:  Change clothes, Kane.  We must move swiftly.

The broken family traveled southeast toward civilization.  Kane pulled Alma in the bed of the wagon.  Leon had offered to pull the wagon, but Kane declined out of principle, to be the protector of his lover and to feel like a man.  He said no more to Leon, avoiding so much as a glance in his tutor's direction because Leon made him feel little.  Pulling the wagon proved a much less demanding task for Kane when there was no guitar to carom off his chest as he walked.  The walk was an effective means of releasing the tension inside him.  He wanted so desperately for Alma to play her music, to distract him from his terrorizing thoughts of Hank at the Parthenon, but Alma displayed no signs of strength.  Being close to Alma tragically reminded him of how much closer they could be if only he could see her grow to become an old woman and a mother.  He would treat her as she deserved- he would love her, and Anika couldn't say a thing about it.  Alma's one goal was to have a child and she will have passed without having achieved it.  How can there be peace in a world such as this?  Something drastic was too happen, and it was to happen soon.  Reading his mind, Alma spoke from the wagon.

Alma (weakly):  It's dangerous for you to love me.

Kane:  I've run from danger all my life.  I'm ready for it now.

Alma:  You're learning.

Kane:  But I'm scared.  I'm scared I'll let you down like I've let everybody down.

Alma:  You don't need to know the answer to everybody's problems, Jake.  You just need to know the feelings that can help them through it.  You give me these feelings, and you wouldn't be able to give them if you didn't have them inside you.  You need to get in touch with yourself, Jake.  You need to know you.

Alma sighed in stomach pain because her four-sentence speech was debilitating.  Kane felt weak whenever Alma opened her mouth because even though she was facing her death, she was so much stronger than he was.

Heart of the People stopped ahead, his one hand pointing in the distance.  Kane followed the extended finger to a trail of leopard footprints spread in an awkward ring around a violet bush.  Kane ran to the bush and picked a handful of violets.  Running back toward the wagon, he was charged with a bolt of energy so strong that he froze in shock.  He hadn't felt this feeling since the lightning-bolt.  Staring at Kane with chatoyant green eyes was his companion, the underdog champion of the persecuted, perched in the grass, snarling its patent snarl- the one-fanged leopard.

Leon:  He has come.  This is my time.

Heart of the People clutched the fang at his neck.

Leon:  He wants revenge.  He wants to foil my plan for peace.

The one-fanged leopard limped forward, nuzzling its head into Kane's oversized hand.  Leon tensed.  Kane let the lapping tongue of the beast lick his fingers.  Massaging the one fang, everything made sense.  Hank Adaline was up to something.  The idea of Hank journeying through the landmarks of the world, playing his music gratis to endow the people with hope- it was a thinly-veiled ploy at best.  Not Hank.  Hank never gave a damn for people or for culture.  He was up to something, flashing his red eyes and his devilish snarl, plotting some perverted end with his mad red turntable.  The Parthenon is one of the holiest remnants of civilization- Hank Adaline is the most unholy man ever born, desecrating all that others hold sacred.  The icon of sin, the Red Shadow, the bearer of fire- he must be stopped.  Kane stroked the leopard's head.  It suddenly made sense.  Kane failed to kill the ailing man in the cave because he wasn't meant to kill the man in the cave.  Kane needed to witness the murder in order to learn that killing can be a necessary means to the most honorable ideals.  This was fate.  Heart of the People's red eyes were fate.  The stranger's letter was fate.  Alma's wish to die in Greece, where Hank was playing his show, was fate.  The one-fanged leopard was fate.  It was fate that he confronts Anika and put her behind him forever- it was fate that he kills Hank.

Kane:  I need to find a guitar.

Leon:  For what?

Kane:  I have a show at the Parthenon.


* * *



Track 7: Heart of the People


Leon smiled through his loop-braided beard.  He shouted to Heart of the People, who exalted.  The drummer's apparent joy only augmented Kane's confusion because Heart of the People never acknowledged Kane's existence through the seasons they lived together.

There was one particular lyric from The Scoundrels' oeuvre that cycled through Kane's mind as he pulled Alma in the wagon and the leopard limped behind him.  I won't die by fire.  The highwayman will kill me and I'll come back as an Indian- these were the opening lyrics to Slave Song, the second track off Red Chaos, Kane's musical portrait of Hank Adaline, the barefoot devil who wears red in the dark just to fool you.  Upon Kane's reentry into civilization, soon to bury his love, it became difficult to say whether Kane wrote these lyrics about Hank or himself.  Hank was the thief, Hank was the highwayman- or was it Kane?  All his life, Kane took and took and took and he never gave anything to anyone, and what was Kane if not a thief?

Kane Hailand first entered the wilderness alone, wearing only his undershirt, his sneakers, and a senseless tattoo.  Now he was reentering society in the company of a dying woman whom he had fallen in love with, a limping one-fanged leopard, a one-armed African tribesman, and his childhood hero.  This was too bizarre- there were too many hints.  He only ever entered the wilderness to escape the invisible chains that bounded him, but now he realized that the only true escape from The Scoundrels was to kill Hank.

Alma:  Why 9?

Kane:  What?

Alma:  Why did she think in 9's?  Why 9?

If Kane were to examine his lover more closely, he'd learn that Alma was developing the famous 9-pound smile he once wrote about in Vile Violet Inviolate Violence, the musical portrait of Anika Handel.  Alma was weary.  She closed her eyes because they were useless, and because the wind was rushing into her open eyes to make her cry.  Then, strangely, the sun must have touched her black vision, for it became pink.  Alma reaped confusion in her great world of pink because, even more mysteriously, the bumpy rhythm of the wagon she lay in was rolling in a faultless pattern of 9-beat cycles.

The trees rained eucalyptus, soft and pink upon their heads.  Leon always talks of peace, but what kind of peace can there be when someone as selfless, as genuine, and as worthy as Alma can lose her unborn child?  Leon threw a knife into a stranger's windpipe.  Leon does not know peace.  No man knows peace and no man will ever know peace because men as a species are too intelligent, too rational for peace.  There will always be those who lack, whether in material or spirit.  There will always be those who envy, those insecure men, those who steal- those who sin.  You may diminish their numbers, but as long as these Scoundrels exist among men, harmony will always be disrupted.  All human injustice is rooted in the Scoundrel- Hank Adaline, that devil, will see his end.

After blurting the news of Usman Kanaan's death, Kane felt incalculably distant from Leon.  Even when Leon spoke to Kane, it was as if the words were just phantoms of his true feelings.  Walking solemnly by Leon's side, Kane spoke.

Kane:  You have no documentation.  You can't cross any borders.  What's your plan?

Leon:  Heart of the People's plan is that I out myself as Baltasar Kanaan.  This, given my alleged suicide, will bring uproar.  We're going to shake the world, Kane Hailand.

Kane:  For all the freedom we thought we had in the wilderness, we had borders.  We were always confined by the limits of society.

Kane batted his eyes, amazed at what he just said.  An orb of light, his renewed musical superpower, flared inside his soul.  He hadn't uttered such a coherent thought since he tattooed his forehead.  Words had always come so easy to Kane Hailand- The Jester had a limitless lexicon that he could spin into rivers of light. The leopard purred, burrowing into Kane's hip.  Kane's shadow had vanished once again.  He craved his guitar.

The group walked on through the immense sands of the desert dunes, all of them hoping the black clouds above wouldn't storm because Alma had no prayer of surviving a storm.  When Mother Nature is kind, we take her for granted- only when she acts like a torrential bitch do we grant her the attention she deserves.

Kane (kicking a rock down the mountainside):  The acoustics at the Parthenon probably suck.

Leon:  To have garnered such universal admiration, Hank can't be as bad as you claim.

Kane:  He's worse.  He's fooling the world.  He'll tempt you in a manner so deceivingly candid you won't realize you've been tempted.

Kane fed a few ice chips to Alma, then to the leopard.  He popped a few chips into his own mouth.

Leon:  You have no choice.  It's written in fate.  You and Hank must make peace.

Kane choked on the ice chips.  He caught his breath and tried to mask his disbelief- did Leon really think Kane was going to Greece to reunite with Hank?  This was the man who threw a knife into a stranger's esophagus and then watched his leader place the severed head on a pike, and he still tries to sing that silly song of peace with a straight face?  Leon can never speak of peace without first confessing his insanity.  Kane said nothing- it was best not to reveal his dangerous truth.

The group walked on, shortcutting their return to Makhraj.  Rosy-pink pedals blanketed the ground and the sun glimmered pink over gold mountains, kissing off the sand.  Thin, prickly vines hung like willows from the trees, sweeping lightly against the mountains.  Gorgeous rocks, sculpted by the hands of time, paved the path to Kane's destiny of fraternal battle.  The bells of war were soon to be rung.

Not knowing the date, Kane didn't know whether the anticipation for Hank's New Year's performance would gnaw at him for a day or a month.  When he sees Hank at the Parthenon, he'll surely see Anika too.  The thought of meeting her was unapproachable.  Anika would never understand his feelings for Alma- she'd never understand why he had to kill Hank.  He considered what Hank Adaline's mother had prophesied- if there is to be a fight, Hank will win.  So be it.  Eat or be eaten.

Alas the troupe reached what appeared to be society.  They navigated at night, for Heart of the People's code was now defunct.  When the stars were at their brightest, the travelers passed through a field of marijuana.  Heart of the People put fire to the field, just to cause some fun before he was to dive headlong into society.  The effects proved revitalizing to Alma, who hadn't experienced such a sensory rush since the damaging fright of the stranger in the cave.  She craved more smoke.  The smoke filled her lungs and brought her closer to her God.  Kane held his breath while walking through the burning fields because drugs only reminded him of Hank.  He still hadn't spoken to Leon, and Leon respected Kane's decision to remain confused.

Pulling weakened Alma in the wagon, Kane thought only thoughts of war.  It would have damaged him enough if his mother and father were to have met for the one brief tryst of his conception just to birth him into lonely void- but for his parents to endure the stress of the pregnancy, the smiles and cries, the pains and joys, and the prenatal exuberance of melding their souls into a child, only to dump Kane while continuing to love his first-born twin- there was no justice.  There was no peace.  Kane's birth, his very existence, demanded war.  Hank was born first and Kane was born second, and no matter what paths their lives blazed, they could never really be equal.  Hank and Kane were born for war and it was time they stop putting it off.

Alma's thoughts were much different than those in Kane's head.  Lying in the wagon, every breath wrought a sharp pain in her chest.  She was too weak to lift an arm or shift her neck no matter how much pain her current position caused- Alma's pink world was darkening.  Night was spreading and death was imminent.  There had always been a flower tucked neatly behind her ear, but now her ear felt naked and she was too tired to voice a request.  Death was near, as near as Kane was to his Anima- but Kane had no guitar to bring him any closer to his Anima, while death wrestled no obstacles.  Alma didn't know how much longer she was capable of fighting, longing for the sweet sound of Kane's soul in the guitar, to sing to her and guide her into death.  She thought of the immortal prostitute from Mountain Song's story.  Mountain Song told Alma of how the girl lives today.  It has become difficult for her to service the men.  The problem doesn't lie with her age, because she doesn't age, and the problem doesn't lie in the scars and the markings she has gained through the unprompted persistence of living, just as the problem doesn't lie in the physical manifestations of the hundreds of childbirths she endured before she lost her uterus, and the problem doesn't lie in the fact that notions of beauty have drastically changed since she drank the immortality potion- the problem was that none of the men she serviced would ever grow old enough to share anything significant with her.  Through her many lifetimes, she has become too wise.  She has seen too much, and she will see far more than any man can ever know.  She is lonely.  She is as lonely as God.  Immortality, not death, is what we should fear.  Alma learned a great deal in this life, and she will carry it with her into whatever lies beyond.  And if nothing lies beyond then at least she will have lived a full life.  Kane claims to have lived multiple lifetimes- his greatest disappointment is that he can't access the person he was before Train of Power.  Kane needs to realize that this is okay, because that child named Jake made him the man that he is, the man he's still becoming, and if that child lived forever then it wouldn't do him any good.  Alma wanted to say this to Kane, but she was too weak to explain.  She needed to salvage her limited energy, and she sensed that Kane was close to discovering everything on his own.

They walked- through square buildings of stone, through dimly lit streets, soundless except for the wagon rolling over cobblestones.  They encountered several shadows in the night, but every suggestion of life fled upon sight of the leopard.

Leon:  The people are scared of the leopard.  Hide him.

Kane:  Where do you expect me to hide a leopard?

Leon:   Stay one hundred paces behind me while I tell them who I am.  Watch your pockets- especially around children.

Kane:  I don't have anything to steal.

Leon and Heart of the People walked ahead, the one-armed drummer moving barefoot over cobblestones.  Kane brushed Alma's hair with his fingers.

Kane:  How do you feel?

Alma (weary):  Are we close?

Kane:  We'll be there soon.  You stay strong.

Alma:  Jake-

Kane:  Shhh.  I know.

Alma:  It's all violet, Jake.

Kane startled.  He felt a surge of light in his large shaking hands, and he tried to contain the fabulous beams they may evoke.  Alma wanted more than anything to imagine Kane's face as she last saw it- grand and statuesque, his beard high to his cheekbones- but the only image her brain produced was blank violet.  It was happening- the energy of The Scoundrels, the light of the Jester, leaving nothing behind but a sick violet love.

Kane:  It's okay.  We'll be there soon.

Kane smiled a vicious smile.  He was regaining his abilities, and he would need to have his full strength if he was to kill Hank.  Once again, Kane Hailand was in love with a woman, and he was determined not to abuse it as he had done before.  Kane won't be at peace until Hank, that Devil, is long extinct.  This was for Alma, because Alma won't find peace until her lover finds it too.  Alma deserved justice.  She deserved peace in death, and she could never die peacefully until Hank Adaline dies.  The leopard jumped, paws resting on Kane's shoulders to lick his violet tattoo.

Peasant women carried buckets in both hands, singing to God, ignoring Leon.  Kane watched everybody shun Leon away.  Leon retreated to the wagon.

Leon:  They think I'm insane.

Kane:  You're a homeless man with a moronic beard telling people that you're Baltasar Kanaan, several decades after he committed suicide- yes, they think you're insane.

Leon:  That's a shame.  I always loved this beard.

Kane examined Leon's countenance- sweaty and grimy, mud in his fingernails, stinking of dust.  For a moment he considered outing himself as Kane Hailand, but who would believe that a longhaired, two-eyed piece of walking filth with a backwards tattoo on his forehead was The Jester?

Kane:  We need to change everything about the way you look.  You need to look just as you did when you were Baltasar Kanaan.

Leon:  We need money.  And we also need to hide that leopard- we'll get arrested.

A few passing cars stopped to stare.

Kane:  Maybe we should get arrested- tell them who we are.

Leon:  No one believes our identities.  If we get arrested, we're finished.  Get that leopard in the wagon!

The thought of spending the remainder of his days in a Middle Eastern prison was enough to make Kane reconsider.  He communicated with the leopard as he did with all of his animal companions, by spreading patterns of light through his fingertips to direct the animal where he wished it to go.
