The leopard climbed into the bed of the wagon, snuggling beneath Alma to serve as her pillow.  Cars passed and Alma blinked dust from her unseeing eyes.  Kane laid a blanket over Alma and the leopard.  Soldiers walked the streets in loose-fitting turbans.  After a pause, the broken family walked on, following fences lined with graffiti as stray dogs followed Kane.

Leon:  In this land, children handle guns as I played my ney.  Their symphony is the scream of a bullet.

They followed the street to a ragged bum on a stoop.  The bum wore a dirty wool cap with a patched image of Geronimo, the 9-legged octopus from the Violet 9.  The bum spoke.

Bum:

Heart of the People looked to Kane, puzzled.  A clan of ministers passed, eyeing the group warily.  The bum jangled an empty cup before the ministers, crying and begging because they acknowledged his humanity.  They passed without donating.  Leon lectured the bum in Arabic, indicting the bum for leeching off society.  If he couldn't find work, Leon argued, it was his responsibility to create work by offering a service of some kind- surely the man must have some talent that could be somehow beneficial.  The bum claimed ignorance.  Leon said that if the bum could direct them to a store that sells cosmetic products, he would see to it that the bum is rewarded.  The bum agreed.

Kane removed the ney and the talking drum from the bed of the wagon.  Leon affixed the wooden contraption to Heart of the People's stump, and they played.  Kane stroked Alma's face as he reveled in the music, still feeling guilty about his confession to Leon.  He thought of how Hank Adaline wasn't ever of this time- Hank was always coming from either the past or the future.  When he played his red piano it was either from a time before creation or a land beyond the grave of earth.  Kane Hailand was always fascinated with this phenomenon.  Frustrated, Kane shook all memory.  This was no time for nostalgia.  Hank must be annihilated.  Besides, Hank was a DJ now- the mad red piano was gone.  No one knows Hank Adaline like Kane knows Hank Adaline, and history will consider itself served a warm plate of justice when Kane Hailand murders his brother.

A soldier stopped in front of the musicians and lowered an M-16 to their faces.  They quit their instruments, staring down the barrel of the weapon.  After several beats of silence (Alma counted 9), Alma heard the vibrating plop of a coin in a cup.

The soldier spoke in Arabic.  The group laughed uproariously.  The soldier walked on.

Leon (through spurts of laughter):  He says we're an odd-looking bunch.

Kane unwillingly joined in laughter.  Even Alma had to laugh.  To the soldier, the bum appeared the most normal among them- a loopy-bearded Arab, a one-armed shirtless African, and a crazy American with a senseless tattoo on his forehead, standing next to a wagon with a dying woman in the back, all of them freshly dunked into the stink and the scabs of the wilderness.

The sun rose along with the people.  Kane still wanted to do the impossible- set the sun.  As the dew disappeared from the stones to warm the earth, the music attracted a sizable crowd.  Within an hour, Leon announced that they had surely earned enough money to buy supplies for his grooming.  The bum guided them to a nearby shop, sharing his story as he walked.  He was mourning his brother, a soldier killed by his own men in a terrible miscommunication.

When they reached the shop, Heart of the People played his drum as they waited for Leon to buy a hair-grooming kit.  Alma estimated a 9-minute wait.  Leon resurfaced, empty-handed.

Leon:  Things have become more expensive since ninety-two.

Hank Adaline would have never exited a shop empty-handed- even if he didn't desire a single item in the shop, he would have stolen just for practice.  It was time to kill the thief.  Light grew inside Kane, light that he planned to use to smother and kill Hank Adaline.  Hank was everything Kane hated about himself.  Hank was Kane's guilt, his sin and his lie- Hank Adaline must suffer and trickle blood to the death.  It was coded in their DNA- one of them must conquer.  Kane thought only of Hank's lifeless body in a pool of blood and alcohol.  The only way Alma could die in peace was if Kane Hailand killed his brother.  The only way anybody could ever die in peace was if Kane Hailand killed his brother.  Hank Adaline was always at war with himself and with Kane and with the world at large, because the genius was never quite from the same place as the rest of us. He was an outsider, and he made the world suffer for it.  The world needed peace and Hank needed war.  Murdering Hank was Kane's divine beckon.

The musicians resumed playing until mid-afternoon, when they had actually accumulated enough money for a grooming kit.  Leon bought the supplies and checked into a dilapidated, three-suite hostel.  Kane, Alma, and the leopard waited outside.

Baltasar Kanaan emerged from the hostel- hair cropped short, all shaven but the mustache, the famous and unexplained scar on his throat now visible.  This man, though slightly wrinkled and spotted by the sun, was unmistakably Baltasar Kanaan, the hero of Kane Hailand's youth, who inspired The Jester's trademark mustache.  Kane felt his own beard, yearning to sport his mustache again.

Leon requested that the bum lead them to the nearest municipal building.  In exchange, he promised to grant the bum a job in Bonabal.  People stopped and turned to stare and whisper as the group of travelers passed, remarking with astonishment how the man with the mustache bore an uncanny resemblance to Baltasar Kanaan.

The bum led the broken family to the Parliament of Makhraj.  Examining the glorious Parliament structure, gilded in gold and marble, a tower among the stone buildings that comprised the remainder of the city, it appeared as though all of the money in the city had been funneled into this beautiful building.  Having amassed a sizable following of people who shouted through the streets to learn if Leon was a relative of Baltasar Kanaan, Leon entered the building with unmistakable pride.

Leon:  My name is Baltasar Kanaan.  I have been away for a long time, but I am here now and I need you to lead me to someone who can arrange a flight to Bonabal immediately.


The broken family was placed in a holding cell for two weeks while the Makhraj Parliament issued countless phone calls, screenings, and even a blood test to confirm the identity of Baltasar Kanaan.  Kane, Alma, and the leopard were held separately from Leon, Heart of the People, and the bum.  They were fed frequently, and this seemed to boost Alma's health.  Given the astonishing nature of Leon's claim, they were held in a maximum-security penitentiary.  The guards assured Kane that if Leon proved to be an impostor, they would all be transferred to accommodations that were far less comfortable and far more permanent.  The only reason Leon's claim was being seriously considered was because the mustached man was able to recite whole passages from Baltasar Kanaan's VAGINA in eight languages without any hint of an accent.

Kane could hear Heart of the People and Leon converse from the opposite side the cellblock.  They conversed in varied tones- sometimes hopeful, sometimes flustered- without ever stopping to eat or sleep.  The bum sat in silence, picking his teeth with his thumbnail.  Several times throughout the first few days, Kane called to Leon.  At first he called just to hear Leon's voice, but his friendly calls soon turned into desperate apologies that Leon never heard because Leon was so fixated on his talks with Heart of the People.  So Kane tended to Alma, trying to keep her alive until he could kill his brother.

Hank Adaline was an icon of sin.  He represented everything that Kane ever wanted to be, everything Kane became, and everything that sent Kane into the Middle Eastern wilderness on a binge of self-loathing.  For two weeks, murderous thoughts festered in Kane's mind.  But something else was happening in that remarkable mind of Kane's- he was writing music.  Though he had no guitar, the music was permanently penned in patterns of light in the Jester's head.  He tried to write violent music as the soundtrack to Hank Adaline's death, but Kane Hailand's mind kept riffing on the Chord of Creation.

After two weeks in the Middle Eastern penitentiary, the DNA test cleared and Leon endured a series of interrogations.  The Makhraj Parliament was elated to have an ally who could perhaps influence Bonabal's questionable foreign policy.  Makhraj provided the jet that Leon requested, under the mutual agreement that Baltasar Kanaan's existence was to be hidden from the public until further agreements with the Bonabali government had been established- Bonabal had not yet decided how they wanted their media to portray such a bizarre ordeal.  The Makhraj Parliament was especially hesitant to let a live leopard aboard one of their aircrafts, but Leon voiced his insistence on Kane's behalf.  Finally, the Parliament agreed to fly the leopard on the condition that it was kept in a cage, which they ordered and installed in the plane within the hour.


The group boarded the plane along with two diplomats who were appointed with the responsibility of briefing Leon with the two decades' worth of news he had missed.  Two armed pilots boarded the aircraft and relayed their respects to Leon, proud to commandeer this historical flight.  The jet only had six seats, one of which had been removed to accommodate the leopard's cage.  Kane vowed to sit on the floor with Alma, freeing the seats for Leon, Heart of the People, the bum, and the diplomats.

Leon informed Kane that tonight was New Year's Eve.  The plane was to land in Bonabal, where everyone but Kane and Alma would disembark.  Kane and Alma were to be flown to Athens, and if they traveled with haste they could make it to the Parthenon before midnight.  Considerately, Leon had ordered a guitar for Kane.  Kane uttered his thanks, still uncertain of where he stood relative to Leon's good graces.  The new guitar was quite different from the instrument that Heart of the People handcrafted in the desert.  It was unique and it carried a beautiful sound- an electric musical killing machine, the body of which was a mirror, decorated with six strings that were much looser and more ductile than those of the guitar that Kane shredded against the wall of the cave.  Alma lay in Kane's lap as he experimented with his new weapon, playing slide-style, moving a soda bottle over the fretboard atop her belly, kissing her in between notes.  She did her best to express her appreciation with a smile, and these odd smiles gave Kane the greatest joys he ever knew.  It had been decades since Alma had flown in a plane, let alone a gulf-stream government jet that flies like a comet at .85 Mach, and the experience of flying while blinded was overwhelming.  With no sight, she had become reliant on her hearing as her most trusted link to the outside world, but the rising pressure in her ears formed a barricade from the world as she knew it.  Alma didn't speak for the duration of the flight.  Her words, she knew, were limited, and she was saving them for when she would be alone with Kane.  She listened closely through her migraine to hear Kane discover his Anima in the guitar, and this gave her the energy to endure against her oncoming death.  The last time Kane Hailand flew several miles above the earth in a twin-engine aircraft was much different than this.

Heart of the People and the bum clipped their toenails, struggling to manipulate the nail-clipping contraptions.  The one-armed beatman spent most of the flight staring out the window, drumming his one hand on the armrest, fascinated with his first aerial experience.

Leon lent his grooming kit to Kane, who cut his hair and trimmed his trademark mustache in the cockpit bathroom.  He still didn't quite look like the Jester.  Perhaps it was the fact that he was missing his eyepatch, his Jester's hat, and his military tunic- or perhaps it was the fact that there was a senseless tattoo slashed into his forehead.  You decide.

Kane exited the bathroom and resumed playing guitar for Alma.  His playing was more fluid on the mirrored guitar than it had ever been in the wilderness.  He gained confidence with every note, devising his musical ambush on Hank Adaline.  Light beamed from his fingertips and guided his fingers across the fretboard as he played Satan's Blues for Alma.  He didn't know why he chose Satan's Blues to play- the song came from Red Chaos, and it detailed Hank's enslavement by his temptation for drugs, sex, and liquor, containing those famous opening lyrics- drag my knuckles 'cross the land to drink blood from my sinful hand.  Maybe Kane just wanted to play one more Hank song before he put the fire out for good.

Leon read the multitude of documents piled waist-high next to his seat.  Kane couldn't help but laugh as he watched the diplomats attempt to instruct Leon on how to use a laptop.  Leon looked up from his stack of papers and chuckled aloud.

Leon:  I'm reading about this Bill Clinton thing.

Kane:  What Bill Clinton thing?

Leon:  The intern- Lewinsky.

Kane:  You may be the last person alive to ever consider Monica Lewinsky to be news.

Leon:  I always used to say, the sexiest thing about Hillary Clinton is Bill.

Leon quit laughing.  He paused, turning to Kane with a stern expression.

Leon:  I know why you're going to the Parthenon.  I know you plan to eliminate Hank.

Kane leaned his guitar against the wall beside him.  He said nothing.  He just stared at Leon, mirroring mustaches (though Kane's was coffee-colored and Leon's was black as crude oil).

Leon:  I know how important Hank's offenses are to you.  I don't know them as you know them, but I understand how you feel.  I've thought about my father as a man.  I've tried to understand things from his perspective.  In order to reach peace, you have to think about the situation from Hank's view.  In my head, I have made peace with my father.  If he were still alive, I'm sure that he'd be the first person to greet me when I exit this plane.

Kane:  I shouldn't have said anything.  I'm sorry, I-

Leon:  Unnecessary, Kane.

Kane lifted Alma's head from his lap and rested her gently on the mirrored guitar, careful not to peer into his own confused face.  Leon looked back to his papers.  Kane stood.

Kane:  You don't get it.  There's no escape from Hank.

Leon (looking up from his papers):  Who are you to talk about escape?  You have a tattoo on your forehead- you'll never escape from anything.  You must live with what you've done.  This is your responsibility.  Face your actions.  Face yourself.  Allow your mistakes to guide you to a better future.

Kane:  What if the man you killed was a musician- what if he would've been a great addition to the band?

Leon:  We have a reason for everything we've ever done.  I've listened to you tell the same stories of your past- you talk about Hank and you talk about Anika and you don't talk about anything else.  You still don't realize that you spent your life crafting a misery for yourself by turning the music into something it wasn't supposed to be.  You used music to wage war against your brother.  You used music as a weapon.

Kane:  He's not my brother!

Heart of the People flashed his red eyes.  The leopard walloped against the cage.  The diplomats eyed Kane as he became swollen with anger.  Leon assured them that Kane was no threat.  The bum clipped his toenails.  Alma wanted to soothe Kane, but the pressure was thickening in her voice and her head.

Kane:  You were my hero before I ever met you.  You were always my hero.  I worshipped you.  Then you saved my life, and I told you how much I admire your work, how it changed my life and gave me meaning.  And you laughed and told me that the whole thing was a stupid pun about a vagina.

The plane rocked through turbulent skies.  The pilot poked his head from the cockpit and uttered Arabic to Leon.  Leon nodded and buckled his seatbelt.

Leon:  He wishes you to sit down.

Kane remained standing.

Leon:  I'm going to explain what you've seen, Kane.

Kane:  See, that's just it.  Kane.  That's not even my name.  I'm Jake.  Ask Alma, she knows.

Leon:  Yes.

Kane:  What do you mean, yes?

Leon:  I mean that you should let me speak.  It's time for change.  I don't want any mysteries between us.

Kane:  Then why have you been fooling me this whole time?  All you've done is fool me from the second I met you.  Alma's the only one who's been genuine.

Leon:  Don't think of it as fooling you.

Kane:  But that's what it is.  I thought you were the noblest men I ever met, but you're not.  You're a deceiver.

Leon:  Stick to what you know, Kane Hailand.  Because what you don't know is what I can teach you.  There's no peace in the wild, Kane.

Kane:  You're always talking about peace.  Look what you did in the cave just a few weeks ago.  This is bullshit.

Leon:  We didn't go to the land for peace.  But here, in society, we can have peace.

Kane:  What are you talking about?

Leon: Humans can coexist with other species, and we should, but we're not meant to live among them.  We have evolved to cohabit with humans only, with each other, in societies.  These reports show that, for the first time in history, more people are living in cities than in the country.

Kane:  Are you stoned?  Have you lost your mind?  You've been living off the land since ninety-two.

Leon:  Yes, but you don't know our intentions in so doing.  Heart of the People and I have removed ourselves from society for so long because we wanted to better understand humanity.

The pilot poked his head back in the cabin and spoke to Leon.

Leon:  Would you like a beverage, Kane?

Kane looked at Leon, dumbfounded and enraged.  Leon politely dismissed the pilot.

Kane:  In order to better understand humanity, you escaped it- in what world does that make sense?

Leon:  Do you remember Moishe, the farmer, the one with three wives and three daughters?

Kane:  Vaguely.

Leon:  Do you remember how I told you that he's incapable of talking about the land?  Like a fish doesn't notice the water it lives in, the farmer doesn't notice land- because it is so much a part of him.

Kane:  Okay, so?

Leon:  This is how it is with society.  We need a reform.  We need peace.  But we've become so absorbed in the society we live in that it's been impossible for us to view it objectively.  We've been ill-equipped to implement peace.  It was necessary for Heart of the People and me to remove ourselves from the process of society so that we can better understand it- to reform, to bring peace.  This is a beautiful world, Kane, but we've seen great nations fight like children.  When you escape it all, everything becomes so much clearer.

Kane:  Heart of the People is from tribal Sudan- he's never been a part of a modern society.

Leon:  Which is precisely why he and I make such a great duo- he possesses elements of naturalism and the more elementary facets of human nature, while my background is highly entangled in one of the most intricately corrupt so-called modern cultures.  Heart of the People and I have been each other's greatest teachers.  It's time we return.  It's time we bring peace.  Every one of us as individuals must remember that we are blessed to be alive.

Kane:  How can you stand there and talk to me about peace when you guys just put somebody's head on a stick?

Leon:  As death has led us into nature, so has death signaled our return to men.  It was an omen that our work in nature is done.  We're done with death.

Kane:  You didn't have to kill him.  You could've just taken his presence as a sign, if a sign was what you were looking for.

Leon:  The man had been bit and lethally poisoned.  I couldn't let him suffer any further.  I'm not saying it was the moral thing to do.  But out there, in the wilderness, there are no morals.  There are only morals among men, because only men are capable of morality.  It is this sense of morality that will allow us to see peace.

Kane sat, placing Alma's frail body between his legs, trying to make sense of it all.

Leon:  As I've watched you learn the guitar, I've thought a lot about violence.  You're a violent player, Kane, and there's so much pain in your soul.  I used to tell you violence is the weapon of the weak- that's only partially true.  Violence belongs in the wild, where it's every creature for itself.  In the wild, violence is necessary for survival.  Eat or be eaten.  It doesn't have to be this way with men.  We are resourceful enough to coexist.

Kane (gesturing toward Heart of the People):  He's a trained killer.  How can he bring peace?

Leon:  He knows the horrors of war.  He knows the tortures of killing.  How can you expect a man to know something if he doesn't know its opposite?  Only through his knowledge of war can he truly know peace.  We need Heart of the People because he knows our true nature.  Nobody can know who he really is until an outsider tells it to him straight, and he accepts the elements of truth.

Kane:  What about her?

Leon:  Alma knows no more than you do, which is not much.  If you'll let me speak-

Kane:  You planned all of this and didn't tell Alma a thing?

Leon:  Our planning relied on Alma's ignorance.  She didn't need to know what she was working toward.

Kane held Alma closer, checking her neck for a pulse.  Eerily, the slow beats of her blood seemed to skip after every 9th beat.  Though she was too weak to speak, Kane knew she could hear everything they were saying, and so he asked the questions he thought she would ask.

Kane:  Why didn't you tell her?  She would've gone along with your cause.  She's the most peaceful woman I ever met.

Leon:  We didn't need her intentions, Kane. We needed her untarnished care.  We needed to keep her as inspiration.

Kane:  You needed to use her.

Leon:  You to be talking.  Look in the mirror.  Look at how you and Hank have treated Anika.  It's all you talk about.  We've been brewing our plan of peace for decades.  Mountain Song- he was an agent.  I read the prayers he collected.  He filtered all prayers that contained updated societal news, and he gave the rest to me so that Heart of the People and I could attune ourselves with the passions of the people, all while maintaining distance from society.

Kane:  What about the farmer- with the wives?  Was he in on it?

Leon (chuckling):  No, no.  Heart of the People just loved smoking Moishe's plants.

Kane took several moments to absorb this information, picking absently at the mirrored guitar.

Leon:  I will never be completely trusted after faking my suicide.  I recognize that people will always fear that I'll abandon them again.  This is why Heart of the People is so essential.  Heart of the People will bring peace.

Kane (sweating, smacking his forehead):  Do you realize how much information you're loading on me right now?

Leon:  I wish to tell you more of Heart of the People's background.

Kane (rubbing his tattooed forehead):  I don't know if I can handle this.

Leon unsheathed the red blade from Heart of the People's holster.  Occupied with amazement by his view of the clouds from above, the one-armed man didn't even turn his head.  Leon handed the red knife to Kane.  Kane examined the blade like an infant beholding space for the first time in miraculous wonder.  The dagger, studded with red diamonds, contained an amber-sealed eyeball in its grip.

Leon:  That is the eye of Lumusi the Decapitator.  Known for decapitating her victims with a blood-red blade, she taught that if you wish to kill a child then you slit the child's throat because slitting throats is a child's game.  If you wish to kill a man, however, you must pull through with the machete and take the man's head.  Lumusi was Heart of the People's overlord, one of the most notorious killers in the Sahara.

Kane dragged his glowing finger across the edge of the knife.

Leon:  Heart of the People's parents were loyal servants to Lumusi.  When they presented the Decapitator with the boy who had the magical ability to spark fire from his palms, Lumusi bred the boy to be her understudy.  She taught him how to administer disease, how to attack any dissenters with vitriolic acid.  She taught him how to drain spinal fluid.  She taught him how to shoot down innocent men in front of a mud wall.  She taught him the meaning of power.  All other assassins blindfolded their victims, but the nameless warrior looked them in the eye when he took their lives.

Kane nearly dropped his guitar on top of Alma.  He looked at Heart of the People, disgusted, and held Alma close to his chest.

Leon:  Heart of the People is from a place where your concerns, Kane, are not only petty, but unknown.  Imagine- you look a perfect stranger in the face and kill him in an instant because if you don't kill him in that second, he'll kill you first.  Eat or be eaten.

The leopard snarled its one-fanged snarl in the cage.

Leon:  Heart of the People's history is the exact opposite of what he is to accomplish in the future.  He has been inspired to create a positive change, and his inspiration is renewed with the eye of The Decapitator in his pocket.

Kane handed the blade back to Leon, who thrust it into the holster at the one-armed man's waist.  Only then did Heart of the People notice that the blade had ever been removed, and he clutched his leopard's fang necklace as if to remind himself of the peace he was to create.

Kane:  There has to be more to this.

Leon:  There always is.  One day, Lumusi sent our fiery warrior to a small Jaali village to fetch the blood of a child as a reminder to distribute a cut of every crop to The Decapitator.

Alma gasped.  Kane's heart thudded into his rib cage, thinking for sure his lover had passed on, but her heart remained constant, beating in 9's.  He kissed her gently.  The warm touch of her moist lips sent a tingle from his spine to his toes and he held her so close but it would never be close enough, and he breathed her scent like a drug, peering into her thoughts.

Kane:  Keep going.  She needs to hear this story.

Leon:  Heart of the People led a squad of mercenaries to the village.  They wreaked their usual havoc- spraying gunfire to signal their arrival.  The fiery warrior demanded every member of the tribe brought forth for examination.  When he felt confident that the entire tribe was indeed before him, he surveyed the children to determine which child would best suit Lumusi's needs.  Heart of the People was only fifteen years old.  He was still a child himself.  But he looked every child in the eye.  If his eyes flashed, it was a signal to his men that the selected child was about to be an orphan.  Just as they began their war dance, he heard noises from one of the clay huts.

Heart of the People, for the first time, turned to Leon.  Though he couldn't understand Leon's English, he knew exactly what story Leon was telling because Leon used the same tone of voice to tell this story in every language he ever told it.  The percussionist looked to Kane and Alma, assessing their worthiness, and nodded his approval to Leon.

Leon:  The warrior followed the sound into a straw hut, where a man sat alone on a bamboo rug, beating his palm against a talking drum.

Alma shivered in Kane's arms.  He wrapped the blanket around her.

Leon:  What affect that drum had on Heart of the People, I will not try to voice to you, for I would only shame the eloquence with which he speaks of divination.  But that drum changed him.  He walked back to his killing squad and burned them all alive.  Then he marched to Lumusi, plucked out her eye, and vowed never to murder again.  He stole her famous red blade along with her eye, and he has only unsheathed that blade twice since it's been in his possession.  You witnessed one of these occasions in the cave.

Kane:  And the other?

Leon:  I ask you to recall the story I told you the first night we ever met, the story in which the Sudanese government invaded our huts, and we stoned the lone soldier to death.  It was the night that Heart of the People's musical tribe disbanded.

Kane:  Of course.

Leon:  You see, I was the one who cast the first stone.  But Heart of the People cast the fatal stone, finishing the job that I began.  He and all his followers had stoned a man to death.  He had broken his vow to never kill again.  He made another vow, and this vow has been held.  He vowed to carry the sins of his people across the land, as any true leader will do.

Kane:  What do you mean?

Leon:  He still has the arm.

Kane:  Excuse me?

Leon:  Would you like to see it?

Kane had trouble producing words.

Kane:  He cut off his own arm- are you-

Leon:  It was the arm that cast the stone of death- that arm was the mark of his sin and the sins of all his people.  I followed him as he walked that desert night, watching from a distance as he severed his arm with the red blade.

Kane:  Wha-

Leon:  In preparation for my venture into the wilderness, I had learned how to tend to wounds.  I was able to save his life.  You and Alma were prohibited from loading and unloading the wagon because we couldn't allow you to discover the arm.  Heart of the People carries the sins of his people so that they may be absolved, so that they may learn peace.  Though our stay in the wilderness was an experiment, it was very much real.  Heart of the People is a man who has endured the grittiest of war- and because of this, he shall bring peace.

Heart of the People flashed his red eyes.  Kane was struck with a reverence that was almost holy, sharing love with Alma on the plane.

Kane (leaning back, clutching the mirrored guitar):  Peace has been attempted many times through the history of civilization- not once has it had lasting success.

Leon:  Though government commands the war, no government official has ever truly witnessed the horror that his decision brings to the people.  I have dreams in which I guide elected officials through the poorest communities.

Kane:  As a naive person, I can tell you with one hundred percent certainty that you have the most naive plan I've ever heard.  Not only will they deny you as a tour guide through poor neighborhoods, they'll turn on you.  When anti-government propaganda pops up at the same time you come back from the dead, they're going to recognize that it's not a coincidence.  They'll oust you, Leon.

Leon:  That's where you're wrong, my friend.  I'll be ousted from the second I walk off this plane- I'll never be trusted again.  The government is smart, they are aware of our mutual dissonance.  I won't have uncensored access to the media or the people.  They're going to turn me into a symbol of war.

Kane:  Are you going to society to bring peace or to be a war symbol?

Leon:  I predict that the government will tell the public that my suicide was, in actuality, a kidnapping hoax performed by the Natspatsuvians- this excuse would be a convenient justification for war.  They'll call to their people to seek revenge against Natspatsu.  My existence is sure to be akin to that of a prisoner.  The public will be given the impression that I am a high-ranking official who has been wronged by a false enemy, while in reality I will be a powerless puppet.

Kane:  So what can you do?

Leon:  I can outsmart them.  The longer I remain their puppet, the longer Heart of the People can perform his work unnoticed.  If I can ensure that they continue believing me to be their slave, Heart of the People will be working right under their noses to get access to the people.  Together we'll put this crazy world in order, Kane.  We're going to change the way we live with each other.

Kane considered for a moment, rubbing his hands over Alma's face to warm her shivering cheeks.  Leon's ideals of peace and fortune were so childish to Kane- they were pipe dreams, impossible in the immitigable orb of earth.  For Leon to believe with such conviction that he can ever establish peace was preposterous.  Leon understood the basic tenant that true peace cannot be achieved with bloodshed- if peace were attained through means of war, then it really wouldn't be peace at all, but coercion.  What Leon didn't realize was that men could never agree to peace.  The government and the people will never bond in brotherhood because both the people and the government are trying to control each other, just as all men and all organizations have a will to exercise control.  Leon didn't understand that peace among men was as inaccessible as Eden.  An urge struck Kane in a way that it hadn't struck him since the lightning- it was an urge to debate, and not just debate, but to constrict Leon's freedom with his words in the way that he had always spoken to Hank Adaline.

Kane:  So you want a revolution?

Leon:  No.

Kane:  But that's what will happen.  If the people resist the government, the government will release the military on its people.

Leon:  They already have.

Kane:  Already have what?

Leon:  According to these documents, the military is killing the people they were hired to protect.

Kane:  So what's your move?

Leon:  Unfortunately, our government lives in fear.  When any government lives in fear, it begins to ignore its responsibility to the people, which is supposed to be its sole responsibility.  A government must never consider itself to be a self-contained entity.  A soldier is the noblest profession of all, yet we forget that the responsibility of the soldier is to protect the interest of the people, not the government.  This is my logic, but the plan isn't mine.  The plan belongs to Heart of the People.

Heart of the People clutched the fang at his neck, solemn and firm-jawed, staring silently into the clouds.

Kane:  If the military turns on the government, then the government will find new soldiers- a hungry man will do anything for food.

Leon:  Yes, but I have money too, and I have taught Heart of the People to funnel this money to Mountain Song, who will reward soldiers for abstaining from the military.

Kane:  However much money you have- it's not enough to compete with a national government.

Leon:  It's enough to start.  I hope to gain wealthy sympathizers- like you, Kane.  You have money.

Kane thought for a moment, paying serious attention to Leon's words for the first time since he watched his mentor throw a knife into the nameless stranger's trachea.

Leon:  You never see a smiling face on any currency.  Why does money have to be so solemn?  Why can't money smile?

Leon paused and stroked his shaven chin.

Leon:  Think about this, Kane- many of Bonabal's soldiers are illiterate.  They've never even read the Koran.  They give their lives to defend a text they've never read.  We can funnel money to the people.  The good can win.

Light coursed through the Jester's veins as his fingers relaxed over the fretboard and he geared for war against Hank Adaline.

Leon:  In Plato, the officials are the lowest-paid members of society.  A government should run on merit, not capital.  Men have made great progress.  We've amassed enough resources for all of us to share contentedly.  Of course, those with greater merit will earn more resources than those who contribute less to society, but the disparities will be far less than they are right now.  Every man will be provided sufficient provisions.  A pooling of such resources can never be arranged in the wild- only a society can arrange a situation where every mouth is fed.

Alma whispered something, but it was too soft for Kane to hear.  Feeling the slight muscle movements in her sunken skin, it was evident that she had been listening to every word of their conversation.  Her cheeks tightened whenever she heard something exciting or something she agreed with.  Kane tried to lead her to speak, but he didn't know where to begin.  He put his hand in hers, and she brushed her index finger gently over his palm.  Kane had never been more grateful to be alive than when touched by a woman who loved him.  To think that this moment could be the last time she ever brushed her finger in his palm caused the tears to well in the eyes of the born-again poet.  Then he noticed that she was tracing the pattern of a cross.

Kane:  Religion- as long as religion exists, people will fight for it.  And you won't be able to stop them.

Leon:  I grew up in Islamic Bonabal- you forget how much religion factored into my upbringing.  Religion can do wonderful things for an individual, but it destroys societies.  I never adopted it because I always believed that religion exists due to fear.  So many religions rely on texts that are thousands of years old, but humanity has made sweeping advances since then.  These texts came into existence because people, in their newfound civilizations, needed a source for morality as well as a guide to explain the phenomena of the natural world.  Since then, science has explained much of these phenomena, and the teaching of morality has become the duty of the parent.  Religion has drastically waned in influence over much of the western world because the rules that were effective in the past are no longer applicable.  It may take several generations, but I believe the East will soon follow.  The demise of religion is the next step in human evolution.

Kane:  Do you realize how idealistic you sound?  It's impossible.

Leon:  If I don't chase my ideals, I might as well wither.

Kane:  Yes, but your ideals aren't your own- your ideals are on behalf of all men.

Leon:  I agree- my ideals depend on others to come to fruition.  So do yours, Kane.  You wish to kill Hank, and you can't do that without Hank.  No one can do anything purely alone.  As individuals, we're always dependent on others for success.  I've seen the same trend in technology.  The entire globe is becoming one society.  The smaller the world becomes, the better we're able to piece together the puzzle of humanity.  These are no revolutionary ideas, Kane, but the act of accelerating them is revolutionary.  I believe one day there will be one world government and one world language- a world without borders, for better or worse.  The lines that have been drawn between nations aren't just blurred, but faded and illusory.  Our differences only point to our similarities.  Race, religion, and geography will no longer matter.  The more we know, the more we mature.  We share one pulse, one story, and one struggle.  Together, we can know peace.

Kane:  This is insane.

Leon:  I don't plan to live long enough to see the fruits of my work, but I do plan to catalyze the movement.  It's not the strength of the individual that matters, but the strength of all mankind.  We're stronger now than we ever have been in our history.  Heart of the People can make this happen.

Kane:  But how?

Leon just placed an open hand over his heart.

Kane sat, contemplating, having completely forgotten his conceptions of Leon as a murderer.  There was a riddle somewhere in Leon's abstract musings, and Kane was trying to piece it together.  He wondered how much of Leon's plans, if any, Alma understood.  She breathed fitfully and painfully with her head in his lap.  The pilot poked his head through the cabin door and spoke to Leon.

Leon:  It seems we are to land soon.  We'll be disembarking in Bonabal, but the pilots have been instructed to fly you two and your leopard to Athens.  You'll be driven directly to the Parthenon.

Alma shot upright in a frisson, causing the rest of them to panic.  She lay her head back down in Kane's lap with a smile on her face.  If Alma never knew about Anika and her obsession with violet and 9, she would have been thoroughly confused. The pressure lessened in her head and she reveled in the lighted comfort of her lover's lap.  During her spasm, there was a 9th of a second in which everything became grey and dim, but when she lay her head back down in Kane's lap, her blank world of sight returned to its inexplicable violet hue.  She felt the aircraft rocket downward in descent.

Leon:  Though I would love for you to join my cause, I understand you have a task to complete at the Parthenon.

Suddenly reminded of his oath to kill his brother, Kane shuddered at the thought of how soon his fate was to unravel.

Leon:  Would you like to know the secret to cloning, Kane?  It's quite simple, really.  You isolate the regenerative qualities in the human anatomy- the ability of the body to heal.  Scars, as you have so poignantly demonstrated by that tattoo on your forehead, shape one's character.  Even so, there's a natural propensity for the body to heal so that it becomes full and unified once again.  These are the qualities we must isolate- not just in the human body, but also in the spirit of humanity, so that we can heal from the wounds that we've inflicted upon ourselves.  Cloning is a dangerous affair, but this idea is sacred.

The plane tipped on an angle to turn its course and face the runway below.  Heart of the People gripped his armrest with his one hand, shrieking with gleeful uncertainty as the leopard growled inside its cage.  The two diplomats had spent the entire flight estranged by Baltasar Kanaan, and they didn't know enough English to speculate into what elements of his mysterious past could be triggering his strange behavior.  They only knew enough to realize that his behavior was undoubtedly strange.

Leon:  How do you think I managed to kill my clone?

Kane:  With a shotgun.

Leon:  Stop being a smart-ass, I'm serious about this.

Leon sat up.

Leon:  You see, it was never an exact clone.  Sure, it had my exact genetic makeup, but I snipped the nerves along the spinal column to restrict the clone from movement.  Do you know why I did this?

Kane:  To make it easier to fire into his mouth?

Leon:  I restricted the clone from movement because, if he was able to move, he might've killed me first.

Kane nodded, unsure of where Leon was going with this unfit parting message, yet somehow sure that he was going somewhere because Leon seemed far less loony now than when the jet was mid-flight.

Leon:  I trust you'll guard my secret about clone work.  Clones are dangerous.  Certain things should never be duplicated.  Just because we have capability, doesn't mean that we should us it- we have been blessed with the almighty power of judgment.

Kane:  I understand your point, Leon, but if we were to attain peace, which is a fantasy in itself, then life would become monotonous.

Leon:  What are you saying, Kane?

Kane:  I grew up as part of a fightless generation.  We had wars, sure, but nobody cared for them.  Our hearts weren't in it.  The real wars were in our homes, in our heads.  What we did in The Scoundrels was to give people something to fight for.

Leon:  Why did you need a fight?

Kane:  Because life's boring without a fight, Leon.  Peace, liberty, justice- these are all just words, names, political moves!

Leon:  That is a pathetic outlook, Kane Hailand.

Kane:  Maybe.  But at least it's not a fantasy.

Leon:  We have a responsibility- to the flora and the fauna, to ourselves and to each other.  Heart of the People is an effective leader because he recognizes his own shortcomings, and he sees the strength in others.  He believes in his people, and he's not a despot.

Kane:  Really- because I remember him lighting my hands on fire in the goddamn desert.

Kane glared at Leon, now a philosophical adversary as any being of intelligence was a philosophical adversary to The Jester.  The plane hit the runway and the leopard jumped inside its cage.  Alma's head bounced.  Kane did his best to provide her a cushion in his hands.

Leon:  We are to part soon.  If nothing else, I want to tell you that, well, I was at the point of giving up.  We were so lonely and it looked as if nothing would ever change.  But then you came along, and we were no longer lonely.  You made us a family.  You gave me hope, Kane, and I'm only trying to return the favor.

Kane:  What if the same thing happens- Heart of the People has broken his vows before.

Leon:  We made a mistake.  We thought we could find peace away from society.  But now we know that we can bring peace to society.  You should make peace too, Kane.  You and Hank share so many stories, and still you don't know peace.  The past is the past and it always will be, but you can't let it control your future.  The world is dangerous, undoubtedly.  I enter the danger with but one promise- I will not provoke violence, but I will outsmart it.  The evolution of war contradicts that of civilization- as we've become more civilized, our wars have become more barbaric.  There used to be rules in war, but now we have guerrilla warfare.   War is uncivilized- it has no place in civilization.

The two pilots exited the cabin and opened the plane door for Leon and Heart of the People.  Kane rose to say his goodbyes.  He and Leon embraced, because for all the mania he endured under Leon's guidance, it was one of the most amazing experiences of his life.  Arms wrapped around his former idol, Kane whispered in his ear.

Kane:  Do you really want peace?

Leon:  I do.

Kane:  I think you just want to try to do the impossible.

Leon:  You wouldn't know.  You've never tried it.

Leon pulled away and looked Kane in the eye.

Leon:  A performer can look a man in the eye and say something he doesn't believe.  Quit being a performer, Kane, and be the man of passion.  You want me to tell you with my words how you and Hank can change and grow together, but I would rather slice my tongue.

Leon bent to kiss Alma on both cheeks.

Leon (whispering to Alma):  You've provided us with endless inspiration.  When we establish peace, you will be remembered as the great mother of all mankind.

Before exiting, Leon turned to Kane one last time.  Kane peered back at the man whom he modeled his trademark mustache after.

Leon:  Light and fire- you're not so different.

Leon exited the plane with the bum and the two diplomats in hasty pursuit.  Heart of the People followed Leon, but hesitated as he passed Kane.  He extended his one hand for a shake.  Kane, startled at the change in the man's demeanor, half-expected the percussionist to speak English.

Heart of the People flashed his red eyes and Kane felt divine light in his palm.  Shaking the hand that once scorched his fingertips, the very hand he always wished to shake since he botched his opportunity at the campsite that first night, Kane felt a greater sense of purpose and a greater universal love.  Heart of the People withdrew his grip and kissed Alma.  Before exiting, he removed his leopard-fang necklace and handed it to Kane.  The leopard snarled in the cage.  Heart of the People wrapped a turban around his head and applied glue to a fake beard.  Disguised, he followed Leon into destiny.

Kane lifted Alma into one of the vacant seats.  Sitting behind her, stroking her hair, he whispered into her soul.

Kane:  We'll be there soon.  Don't you worry.

Alma:  Play for me.

Kane lifted his guitar.  He played.  Though Leon failed to convince Kane that peace was attainable, he did convince Kane to admire the work that Leon and Heart of the People had planned in the wilderness.  Leon, if the government didn't kill him, was sure to be entering a situation in which personal comfort will be nearly impossible.  He sacrificed his own happiness for a cause greater than himself, and Kane had to admire this because he never gauged that capability in his own character.

Alone with his lover and his leopard, the only thing that mattered was ending Hank Adaline.  The nomadic era of Kane's life had ended just as every era in his life had ended- with a new sense of purpose and an abundance of uncertainty.  If he died in battle against Hank, he'd never learn whether Heart of the People wrought success in his pursuit of peace.  He'd never bury Alma.  Bathing in the flowery scent of her hair, Kane Hailand was newly empowered.  Kane basked in the galvanizing aroma, symbiotically enmeshing with his guitar as the plane took flight.  Kane Hailand oozed light from every pore in his body.  Yes, God is a charging bull- a majestic being that thinks in modes of light incomprehensible to humans.  So go ahead, Heart of the People, go ahead and find your peace- only just wait a short while until we rinse the bloodstains from Kane Hailand's forehead.

Alma lay in Kane's lap as he played.  She gushed to herself in her violet cell of existence.  Though Kane hadn't found his Anima quite yet, she knew with unbridled certainty that he was just a step away from walking off the cliffs of mortality into the paradisiacal abyss of the Anima.  She had dedicated the last moments of her life to sculpting his identity, and his voice was permeating through her consciousness, clear and violet, chugging in a 9-beat rhythm.  The violet, the 9's, they finally made sense to Alma.  If it weren't for the warning shot of Anika before her, she would have been utterly confounded.  But for her to enter the same fate that Anika had entered, with the violet and the 9's, it all made sense.  The constant color, the endless rhythm of sound, these weren't phenomena that were occurring in the natural world around her- they were illusions, the illusive effect that Kane Hailand bestowed unwittingly upon the one he loved.  Kane, the Jester, the master of light, was tapping into Alma's energy to make his music sing.  He used all of her energy, robbing her of all vivacity, leaving her with only the discarded parts of him that he was too scared to face in himself.  Train of Power, Kane had said, was written in 9-beat patterns.  He was afraid of his success in Train of Power, and so he couldn't face 9-beat patterns in himself.  He left these to Anika, and then to Alma.  Alma couldn't yet explain the violet, but there was something about the color that petrified Kane.

Kane's violet effect, although brilliant, was dangerous.  This was the effect that Anika never understood, the effect that drove her insane because she never loved him back.  But Alma did love him, more than she loved herself, and it made her happy to feed him her energy because she was happy to reciprocate his heavenly love.  She gathered all of her strength to refrain from singing along with his guitar.  She knew that if she sang, she would die.  Her energy was limited, and it must be reserved for Kane.  He was so close to his Anima, but there was still so much he didn't understand about his purpose in the world.  Instead of moving forward to become Jake, as he was born to be, Kane was using his potential to step back into the guise of the Jester and kill Hank.  Kane Hailand the Jester used music as war.  Though the Jester had love in his heart, this love produced a violet effect that was terrifying.  Kane must put down the instrument, put down the weapon, and leave music and war behind him forever- he must learn to love himself before he can love his brother.  Alma must reserve her efforts for this speech.  Then her Jake will be saved, and she can die in peace.  She laid her head in his lap, his guitar positioned to rest gently on her chest, and they flew miles above the earth in a violet storm of rolling 9's.


When the plane landed, the driver had not yet arrived.  The flight crew explained the phenomenon of Greek Time, the notorious notion that Greeks never abide by specific meeting times.  Kane and Alma waited about 9 minutes until the limo arrived.

When the car pulled up, Kane carried Alma through the side-hatch, down the staircase, and into an open limousine.  After laying her comfortably on the oblong leather seat, Kane went back for the leopard and the mirrored guitar, leading his feline friend using patterns of light, as every flight crewman sequestered in panic.  The driver rolled down the window.

Johnny-John:
Your friend Leon has sent me, Kane-
No tattoo has ever looked better.
No business of mine whether you've gone insane-
Just keep that leopard away from my leather.

Kane:  Johnny-John?  What are you doing here?

Johnny-John was the Scoundrels' rhyming driver.  He was at their command 24/7, shuffling all three bandmates to anywhere they wished to go- except for Anika's disguised taxi visits to Kane's beachside resort.

Johnny-John:
When my master needs a driver,
I'll glide graceful as a swan.
Kane Hailand, I'll deliver
At once to the Parthenon.

The leopard snarled, inciting Johnny-John to roll up the window.

Kane (softly, in Alma's ear):  We made it.  Welcome to Greece.

Alma made the trek to Greece- her motherland, the land of her ancestors, the land of the great mother Gaia.  Though she couldn't see the land, she could feel it.  It was blissful and serene.  Her pilgrimage was complete.  And now she will die here.  Her ear felt naked without a flower tucked behind it, but she was born naked and she'll die naked too.  She couldn't waste her few remaining breaths on requesting such trifles of Kane because all remaining breaths must be spent educating her lover.  Heartbeat fading 9 beats at a time, she put her finger to her lover's lips, and spoke.

Alma:   I always thought I was supposed to create a child.  I thought that if I made a child, then my Anima would be satisfied.  But I haven't made a child.  I've made a man.  I didn't need to create anything new to make the world a better place, Jake- I made it better by learning to love what was right in front of me.

Alma paused to cough.  Kane tensed, fearing her death.  He wrapped his arms to warm her.  He didn't dare speak.  He listened, truly, with the efforts of his soul, and breathed the faint sounds of her spirit.

Alma:  If you're ever unhappy it's because you've forgotten what we've taught you.  I've seen the true you.  I've seen your soul, and you are beautiful, Jake, you are wonderful and beautiful and you've always tried to hide this in every song you ever wrote, but if you don't hide anymore then you won't be afraid of anything.  You won't be afraid of yourself.

Kane let his tears fall into Alma's hair, staining them with lover's salt.  He placed his hand in hers, her hand in his, trying to pass his warmth to her because she was getting colder.

Alma:  You've achieved a following with your music.  You've had an accomplished career, and you can use this power for good.  But when you're in my position and you're crossing over into death, you won't be thinking of any of that.  You'll be thinking of me.  Just as you're holding my hand to guide me out of life, I'll be holding yours, waiting to guide you into death.  I have raised you to believe.

Kane froze.  How could she have done that?  How could she have just channeled into his greatest secret, his Train of Power?  She nearly quoted the final stanza verbatim- Behold!  She sees, offering her peace.  Fly beyond the light together, she will be your guide.  Suddenly it made sense.  Tapping into the fuel that once created Train of Power- his greatest masterpiece and his greatest sin- something made sense.  The Scoundrels' problems never resulted from the fact that they never equaled the perfection of their first-ever performance- Kane couldn't put the rest together in his head, too overwhelmed to broach the brilliance of Train of Power.  Alma lay still in his lap.  He wished she would say more, but she had nothing else to say.

Kane:  I have something for you.

Kane reached into his ratty blue-jeans and removed a pristinely preserved violet from his pocket.  He tucked the flower behind her ear.  It felt so natural and so perfect in her ear that she succumbed to a violet rush of being, making sounds and noises in an almighty release.

Alma (a near-smile, eyes closed and calm):  You make me feel young again, Jake.

She smelled of violets freshly plucked by the sprites of Eden.  Her hand in his, all was right.

Alma:  Take me outside.  I'm ready.

Kane ordered Johnny-John to pull over.  He opened the door and carried Alma outside to breathe the Grecian nighttime air, holding her hand all the while so that he may guide her out of life.  He rested her on the ground, a hint of smile across her face, and he felt the life slowly fade from her hands, holding her, singing sweet lullabies to rock her gentle soul.

What song he did Kane sing to his lover?  Well, that's something that will have to remain between Kane and Alma.  The important thing for you to know is that Alma finally rejoiced in her lover's vocal song, and every breath was pure elation, until she was not quite awake and not quite asleep, but positively dreaming.

Kane knocked on Johnny-John's window and requested that the driver wait while Kane buried the body.  Johnny offered to help, but Kane refused, as this was a deed that must be done by him alone.  He sifted his hands through the tough Grecian dirt, breathing hot breath to warm the sands.  Thus Kane Hailand dug Alma's grave, the only grave he ever dug.  He did not use a shovel or a hoe or any other machine- he used the raw physicality that his god gifted him.  When alas he had finished, exhausted, rewarded, and ensconced in yet another layer of filth from the earth, he placed the body in the shallow hole and scooped the dirt back over her.

He felt that he should write her name in the dirt, to commemorate her resting place- not for any living person to see, but just for her.  What would she want to be called- Alma, Gaia, Eve?  With a clawed hand, he snagged a stick from the ground, gripping the wood as he gripped every writing utensil- four fingers against a thumb.  This peculiar grip ensured that his hand-written ink always smudged against the side of his hands, sometimes slashing into his wrists and his palms if he became excited enough.  He put the stick to the sand, but it didn't seem right.  He couldn't produce words that would do justice to who Alma was and what she meant to him.  He reached back into his blue jeans and removed his only remaining violet.  Fixing the flower in the sand, patting the earth around the stem, he kissed the violet goodbye.


* * *



Track 8: The Genius Laments


Kane reclined in back of the limo, crusted in dust, petting his leopard- stunned.  He had buried his lover with his bare hands.  Now these same hands were to strangle Hank Adaline.  Though Kane had conquered much of the anguish that resulted from his past, the only way to completely annihilate his past was to obliterate it, to outdo it, to outdo Hank.

Johnny-John unrolled his window and dropped a paper parcel into the backseat.  He rolled the window up again.  Kane leaned forth and examined the package, reading a note tucked beneath the twine-

You have been granted the almighty power of judgment- L.

Kane tore the package.  Light pulsed inside him as he held the cloth in his hand.  Somehow Leon had located his infamous Jester's hat and ankle-length military tunic- The Jester's original, unscathed, epaulets and all.  Kane dug further into the parcel, discovering a selection of hand-painted eye-patches at the bottom.  Instinctively, Kane placed the Jester's hat upon his head.  His hair had grown since he last donned the hat, not just in length but also in volume, and the floppy-eared hat fit tighter than it used to.  Kane always favored a loose-fitting hat, one that would bounce and refract light in the most spontaneous of paths.  He considered ditching the hat, but he thought of how Hank would react if the mad DJ ever glimpsed Kane Hailand's tattooed forehead.  Kane thought of Alma as he dressed.  He thought of her burial, recalling the doleful crescendos of dirt upon her empty body.

Dressed in full Jester's garb, Kane struggled to choose the most appropriate hand-painted eye-patch.  Most of the patches depicted animal stage companions from an era of his life that was no longer relevant.  He rechecked the package for any more notes from Leon.  Feeling the bottom of the box, Kane felt a piece he hadn't noticed before.  Rubbing a smooth piece of glass between his fingers, he pulled a mirrored eye-patch from the now-empty package.

Staring out the window with his one uncovered eye, Kane watched the land go by.  The land was composed of the very dirt that he shoveled over his lover's remains.  He wanted to touch her, to kiss her, to run his fingers through her hair and hear her lyre.  But she was gone- he was alone.  The streets of Greece were lined with lemon trees and violet flowers.  Somehow Kane sensed that Alma was with him.

The roads, though dark, were green and mountainous.  Greece was the birthplace of democracy, but the land has seen just about every form of government since.  This means that every form of government has failed here.  Despite the unmatched magnitude of political turbulence to pass through, Greece has still retained a sense of beauty that suggests what civilization once was, and what it can again achieve.  Kane felt the hands of time tugging mercilessly at his ankle-length military tunic to drag him toward his destiny at the Parthenon.  His nerves ticked like insects.  Hank and Kane, Easton and Jake- no matter which way you put it, Hank came first.  Kane was here to kill his brother, to violate another beyond the brink of oblivion, fearless of whatever consequences may obtrude.  This, Kane knew, was principle- the only path to pride.  Kane unfolded the photograph from his pocket- it was Hank and Kane, assuredly, and Kane was grabbing Hank's leg, holding him back.  There could be no rational doubt.  But what was Kane holding Hank back from?

Kane Hailand had never murdered before.  That's not true.  There was Train of Power- but how could he ever equal that perfection?

Kane stroked the leopard, feeding him ice from the limousine bar.  He compared the leopard to his past animal companions- Sun King the bluebird, Icarus the walrus, Phaeton the pig of light, the infamous Glass Pelican- they were always weak.  Kane recalled the last time The Scoundrels played the Coliseum- the infamous Glass Pelican spontaneously combusted during intermission.  Kane was pressured into playing the second set with a stray cat that the roadies found beneath the Coliseum floor.  Hank Adaline thought this was hilarious (probably because Hank himself was the one who incinerated the animal).  It was the most humiliating show of Kane's career.  There will be no humiliation with the leopard.  The leopard was an untamed beast of the wild.  The leopard was Kane's first legitimate threat.

Stroking his trademark mustache, Kane recalled the days when just a stroke of his mustache would send a crowd of millions into uproar.  Alma would never have loved him then- he was a Scoundrel, impossible to love.  He peered out the limousine window through his one uncovered eye.  His other eye gazed into the mirrored infinity of his eye-patch to remind him that anything is possible.  He thought of Alma.  She died peacefully, and that was all Kane desired in coming to Greece.  But if Alma died peacefully while Hank was still alive and sinning, why did Kane have to kill Hank?  Rhythmic light beamed inside him, screaming at him to kill his brother.  He couldn't remember the rationale behind the murder, but for some reason he felt that the murder must occur.  Alma said her life had been complete, and it was complete because she learned to love what was right in front of her.  She told Kane to stop being afraid of his self, but how could Kane be afraid of himself?  He was certainly wary of himself because he didn't quite know himself, but he didn't fear himself because fear is a true feeling and you can't feel true feelings for what you don't completely know- or so Kane always believed.  The leopard snarled its one-fanged snarl.  Kane ordered the beast to the far side of the limo.  He sat alone in thought, wearing the fang around his neck.

The car stopped.  Johnny-John opened Kane's door.

Johnny-John:
Here alas, my dear fellow,
And there's no time to stir.
Bid Sir Adaline my swift hello.
It was swell to see you, Sir.

Kane hugged Johnny-John and walked with the leopard through the black Grecian night.  The parking lot was littered with Scoundrels fans.  The fans were passionate, as always, dressed in spirit, screaming, ardent to the point of feverishness, tuned in for the raucous, walking over strangers' cars and streaming smoke in the sky.  They were high- if not on drugs then on something else they got from music that they couldn't quite draw from life.  Kane predicted more fans would have dressed like the Jester, but there were very few Jesters in the crowd.  Most of the men dressed as Hank, while the women dressed as Anika.  Kane bit his lip when he realized that he'd have to face Anika after he murders her husband.

Dressed as the Jester with his mirrored guitar, the one-fanged leopard at his side, Kane thought it best to escape the populace and avoid attention.  He removed his mirrored eye-patch, squinting past the acres of people to find the ancient temple.  He had seen the Parthenon in photographs, but this place didn't match the image.  This place might as well have been another planet- aliens and all.  Kane followed the crowd to a turnstile.  Heads turned as they felt the leopard glide by their legs.  On any other occasion, the Acropolis would have been closed to the public at this hour, but the site managers opened their offices when they heard that Hank Adaline planned to appear.

The leopard was earning too much attention.  Kane could sense the alarm in the crowd.  He felt the energy of light beaming inside him and he could barely contain his angst.  His brain lit and his eyes grew.  He was about to panic.  He led the leopard back through the street-lit parking lot.  Fans turned their heads as The Jester walked past with his leopard, not a one of them suspecting this crazed fool to be Kane Hailand.  The fans held balloons, flashlights, and signs to support The Soundrels (Soundrels was their nickname, because sound was what they made), and they danced awkwardly over the rocky rubble.  They wore necklaces made of candy.  They dressed themselves in varicolored light, perhaps in homage to the once-great Kane Hailand.

Squeezing through bodies in the crowded parking lot, Kane escaped the mob.  He created light near a dumpster, spotting a broken mirror and an open bottle of adhesive in the mess at the foot of the dumpster.  Thinking quickly, he set his mirrored guitar to the ground and glued fragments of mirror over the leopard's spots.  Reflecting every color in the spectrum, the leopard snarled under the light of Kane Hailand.  Kane stroked the leopard between the ears and named the beast.

Kane:  That's a good boy, Apollo.

Kane led Apollo up a gravelly hill of rocks and trees, unaware of where he was going but following the chatter of the crowd.  Trekking through the darkness, Kane spotted a monument of half-size columns.  This, he knew, was not the Parthenon, but the crowd seemed to be wandering through these columns, and so Kane followed the mob.  The marble steps were slippery, and Apollo's soft paws struggled with every step.  Grunting and roaring, the leopard's fuss drew attention.  Nearby crowd-members turned their heads to address the commotion.  Upon sight of a Jester beaming light from his fingertips to guide a one-fanged leopard, the people could no longer be mistaken- Kane Hailand was alive.  History will be written tonight.

Quickly, Kane led Apollo around the back of the Pandroseion (the ancient temple that neighbors the Parthenon), through the stone rubble, to the south side of the Parthenon.  From this vantage point, Kane could just barely see the eastern front of the temple, where the mad red turntable and the mad red piano had already been set up.

Built to worship Athena, the goddess of war, the Parthenon overlooked all of Athens.  This was the old city of Athens amid the modern era it created, an unrolling of human thought from birth until now.  Kane recognized a red statue of Cerberus, Satan's three-headed guard-dog, at the helm of the Parthenon.  This was the same statue that Hank kept at the gates of his mansion.  People used to migrate to the Parthenon to worship and touch the light of their gods.  Now Hank Adaline was going to bring the devil's fire.

Stray dogs wandered through the rubble, threatened by the leopard.  Kane estimated that there were millions of people here, most of them without a ticket because they couldn't afford it- Scoundrels' fans were notorious for sneaking into venues.  They played the odds with the security team because they figured that out of the millions of fans, what was the likelihood that they'd be the ones caught by the Turkish Wrath Tough Squad?  Named after the song Turkish Bath, the Turkish Wrath were a group of 9 volunteers who followed the Scoundrels and acted as security for their shows.  They were never compensated, as Hank Adaline opposed the idea of a security team.  Volumes have been written about their methods of punishment when fans got out of line.

Most of the fans in the crowd couldn't even see the red instruments on the pedestal before the piedmont, overlooking all of Athens.  They wouldn't see Hank when he came out to play, but then again it wasn't about seeing Hank, and it never was.  Half of the crowd was here to see the Red Shadow finger-dance over Mozart's grave.  The other half came to see the hottest DJ in the world put fire to his turntables.

On his way up the steps, Kane overheard a story from an uncanny Anika impersonator.  At first he was struck by how much the fan looked like The Quaquaversal Anika.  Upon sight of the fan, he was struck with guilt, as Anika always struck him with guilt, and for a moment he forgot everything he shared with Alma.  But when the fan opened her mouth to speak, and Kane heard that squeaky mouse-like voice, it was clear that whoever he was looking at was not the greatest contralto in the history of sound.  The impersonator told Kane that Hank had been traveling the European continent, playing historical landmarks.  She said that the pope banned the Red Shadow from the Vatican.  Hank promised that tonight's event would just be leisurely playing, that it wouldn't be a show, but Kane knew that there will be a show because Hank Adaline is a walking show.  Kane Hailand put all his effort into being a showman, but Hank never put effort into anything- it was always natural for him.

Hank's piano was set stage right, the turntable stage left.  9 torches flickered from the front of the stage, and although the marble temple was beige in the daylight, it now appeared as red as Hank's instruments.  A red crane, used for restoring the historical monument by day, sat beside the monument, reaching into the night as if called upon to suspend the moon, though the crane was somewhat useless because all attempts at restoring history have failed and they'll always fail because time passes forward, and the past, though educational, must be relinquished.  This idea was the fuel behind The Scoundrels' lyricism, and it just recurred to Kane, who was only now realizing the value of his time spent in the wilderness.

Kane read an educational inscription on a nearby signpost-

The duration of the birthday of Athena, the goddess of war, is defined by the chariot of Helios, god of the sun, and Selene, goddess of the moon, at the corners of the piedmont.

The Greek gods were exactly as the Greeks were.  According to lore, humans commingled with gods- humans fucked gods.  When you build your own myth, as the Greeks did, you become gods.  Alma must have already known this.  Kane lost his concentration as the crowd roared like a storm.

Hank Adaline appeared in a cloud of smoke, strolling barefoot toward the red piano with that patented snarl, flashing his eyes, a supermodel on each arm.  The crowd became a seismic rumble, shaking the earth with their feet, raising their fists, hollering in every language (which amounted to no language at all), displaying all emotions in the human spectrum with potent zeal, demanding as much attention as the earth can demand of the celestial sphere.  The fans of The Scoundrels and the fans of Hank's solo work paid no attention to roped-off boundaries, and there was no longer anything the Turkish Wrath Tough Squad could do to stop them.  A riot will ensue.  The police will be here soon.  Hank Adaline, that devil, will make news once again as the destroyer.

Upon sight of his brother, his greatest sin and mortal enemy, Kane Hailand's mind dove and drowned into the memory of the deception.

* * *

In a violet-painted loft located in the secret depths of Uncle Dross University, the Violet 9 circled around Hank and Kane.  The loft, known among the 9 as The Theatre, was horizontally bisected at ground level.  Any outsider would have dismissed the room for a dank storage closet, but to Hank and Kane and their Violet 9, The Theatre was a grand and regal chamber.  In Hank's mind, the room was a four-walled cell built for intimidation, served best if it were painted as red as the underworld.  Kane Hailand thought the room to be a temple- it was His house that He had built, and it shall be blue as the heavens.  Violet was the only compromise Hank and Kane ever made.

The university had given the loft to Kane (or, as they knew him, Jake) as the room-and-board portion of his scholarship.  Then Jake met Easton Israele, sneaking into a master's political theory course that neither of them was enrolled in.  They quickly realized that they shared a passion for Art and Rebellion.  Though their passions were identical, their favored methods were fundamental opposites.  Jake believed in the ultimate meaning of Baltasar Kanaan, while Easton didn't believe in anything but his piano.  Then Balatsar Kanaan killed himself with a shotgun blast to the back of the throat.  There was a hurricane in southeastern America that day, and Jake was absolutely devastated.  He walked into the hurricane, climbed onto the roof, and jumped into a dumpster full of scrap metal.  He never blinked when the lightning struck.  Instead, he thought.  His thoughts were as lucid as those of a prophet endowed with the wisdom of the Lord.  In life, Baltasar Kanaan was approaching something luminary, but his potential was never realized.  Someone needed to carry the light, and Jake couldn't do it alone.  He proposed to Easton Israele that they combine philosophies and teach a class of their own.  They would hold the class in Jake's loft.  They would host open mic sessions for whoever wished to speak, and together they would find freedom.  Jake moved his belongings to Easton's place, clearing all but the cockroaches from the university loft.  To honor their commitment, Easton and Jake adopted the monikers Hank Adaline and Kane Hailand.  Those who came to the open mic with intentions to speak were easily dissuaded from doing so- anybody with any semblance of respect would never dare speak at the open mic because to speak would be to disrupt the amazing fratricidal fury that possessed these two kids.  The debates between Easton and Jake weren't just debates.  They were shows, and their shows became more popular as they heightened their passions to the status of the Rebel.  It became too much.  Easton couldn't handle the crowd.  Together, Easton and Jake barred those who didn't properly express their commitment from ever attending again.  9 months passed.  Of the original 99 spectators, only 9 remained.  They wore violet to blend in with the walls as they watched.  These 9 were to be the soldiers of peace and justice.  They had spent every moment of the past 9 months studying their tutors' maxims.  They had proven that they believed in every word of Kane Hailand's Creation Manifesto.  They were ready.

The 9-month initiation proved hard on its leaders.  Around month five, Hank and Kane began using drugs and booze to cope.  It had been four days since they had last ingested drugs.  Hank and Kane spent these days composing a musical ode to the Violet 9.  Kane's 252-line composition was a poetic outline of their plan to distribute power, happiness, and peace among the people- aptly titled Train of Power, written in red and blue ink in a violet leaflet.  Tonight was Rebel's Eve, the night of the takeover.  Tonight they will endow their people with a sense of justice as they take the streets.  But first, a surprise- Hank and Kane's Train of Power.  Kane ensured that everything was in its exact place.  Train of Power will transpire as he planned it.  There was just one problem- the singer had yet to show up.

Kane distributed 9 copies of the Violet Book to the Violet 9.  He puffed impatiently at a cigarette, which he smoked to wean him off the drugs- Hank had quit cold turkey.  Sun King, Kane's pet bluebird, was perched atop his shoulder.

It didn't matter that the singer was late.  Hank and Kane relished this moment, centered among the Violet 9 for the last time, all of them wearing violet from head to toe.  Their attention was fixed on Hank and Kane's imminent dialogue.  Pacing in a circle, the brothers glared at each other.

Kane:  What is the first phase of Art?

The Violet 9 (spoken together):  The first phase of Art is the Analyst.  The Analyst inquires what is this?

Hank (flashing his red eyes):  And the second phase?

The Violet 9:  The second phase of Art is the Intellect.  The Intellect inquires what should this be?

Kane:  State the third and final phase of Art.

The Violet 9:  The third and final phase of Art is the Rebel.  The Rebel inquires what could this be?

In His Theatre, surrounded by the Violet 9, Kane was God- the Creator of the Universe, Adonai, Yahweh, the One, Kane Hailand.  But for every inspiration he preached, Hank, that Devil, was there to disparage the youth and maniacally doctor their psychology.  Together, they built greatness.  Hank and Kane paced in a circle, glorifying the silence.

Hank:  Most of you didn't do shit to get where you are today.  You don't know what it's like to be like someone like Kane Hailand, to come from nothing.  They told you that your upbringing was privileged.  This is a lie.  You were never privileged.  You were disadvantaged- because you believed in money.

Kane:  That's where we came in- to ingrain in you a sounder moral code.  Every bite you put in your mouth is a bite you've stolen from your brother.   Every dollar in your pocket is a dollar you've stolen from your brother.  You eat your fellow men as they eat you. Not anymore.  The old order of things has passed.  We are paying our debt to this world for all it has given.  9 months ago, you were told to inconvenience yourself for the sake of others.  But you have learned since then- you have learned that there is no such thing as others.  We are brothers, and true brotherhood penetrates the skin to the soul.

Hank and Kane paced in a diametric circle, speaking more to each other than to the Violet 9.

Hank:  Justice- what's a republic if the public doesn't know of it?  The time has come.  Destiny is a fire that you'll accept when we release you onto the pavement.  Attack the moment.  Let it course through your blood.  You wear your colors proudly, for the people.

Kane:  Achieve, and then we shall become a fuller self than we ever thought attainable.  Tonight we endure.  Tonight we see perfection.  Tonight we give life!

9 scratches on the door, the singer's signal- it was time.

Kane:  You have your Violet Books.  When Hank gives his signal on the piano, you open your books together, and read along.

Hank and Kane exited.  Hank poked his head back into the Theatre, his only aim being to confuse the Violet 9.
