Hank:  Consider the possibility that what you're about to do is the biggest mistake in a pathetic chain of lousy mistakes you call life.  Consider the possibility that humanity is inherently sinful.  What are you working for?

Hank exited for good.  He introduced Kane to the choirgirl who was to act as their singer.  Her hair was curled in floating chestnut tresses.  She wore a white dress that purified her stunning blue eyes.  Something in her soul was calling to Kane, breathing in fantastic light inside his being.  It was as if all the energy from the lightning bolt came back with unchecked voltage to ignite him with a sense of purpose.  Staring at the singer, Kane was stupefied electric.

Hank:  This is my girl, Lucy.

Anika:  So, you're Jake?

Kane (entranced by her melodic voice):  Uh huh.

Anika:  What's your last name, Jake?

Hank:  We have new names, baby.  That man there is Kane Hailand.  You can call me Hank Adaline.

Anika:  That sounds stupid.

Hank:  Well, it's not stupid.  It's brilliant.  We have one for you too.

Anika:  I don't want it.

Hank:  You're Anika Handel.

Anika:  That's not even a name.

Hank:  It's your name.

Anika:  Whatever- as long as it's just for today.  Say Jake, that's a nice-looking bird you've got.  What's its name?

Kane (Sun King whistling on his shoulder):  I-

Hank (to Kane):  Let's go get dressed.

Anika:  What's wrong with what we have on?

Hank:  We have costumes.

Anika:  I'm not wearing a costume.

Hank:  We are.

Anika:  You guys take this way too seriously.

Hank:  Let's go, Kane.

Kane shook his daze from the enchantress.

Kane:  Cigarette?

Anika:  I'd love one, thank you.

Hank:  Since when do you smoke?

Anika:  Since when do you care, Easton?

Hank:  A voice like yours and you'll kill it with smoke.

Anika:  Go get dressed and let me have my smoke.

Hank:  Give her the lyrics to read over.

Kane handed a copy of the Violet Book to Anika.

Anika:  What's it called?

Kane (finally able to speak):  It's called Train of Power.

Anika:  Where do you guys come up with this stuff?

Kane's ability to speak had long expired.  Hank and Kane entered an alcove to change clothes.

252 (add the digits) lines, 9 syllables per line, spoken in couplets from opposing narrators- Train of Power was undoubtedly Kane's most advanced composition to date.  But Kane couldn't think about the performance that was about to take place.  All Kane could think about was what he was about to do to Hank.  Hank had been playing head-games with the Violet 9 all along, but he didn't realize that Kane, his supposed friend and partner was pulling the same trick on him.  Hank had an amazing gift with fire, but it led him to believe that he really was the devil.  He thought himself contemptible, a scoundrel of the lowest order- he thought he was capable of murder, free of guilt.  Kane was about to defile every notion Hank had of himself, and he was going to do it with Hank's own fire.  He was going to break the pianist's heart.

Hank:  I emailed my mom a picture of you and me.  She called me up crying so hard.  I couldn't hear what she was saying.

Kane shuddered.  Just last month, Hank's mother had drunkenly called Kane to say that he and Hank were twins, that she abandoned him as a baby.  Kane initially dismissed this for a joke, but she had left dozens of drunken voicemails over the past month.  He never said a word about it to Hank.

Hank nervously tapped his fingers on his lap, knowing exactly what sound would sing if a piano was below his hands.

Hank: I don't know how to ask you this, but did you fuck my mom?

Kane (coldly):  I never met your mom.

Hank removed his shoes and socks and pulled his red suit-pants up.

Hank:  I have to tell you, I'm really happy being sober.  I wouldn't tell this to anybody else- especially Lucy- but I'm feeling less guilty.  I've done and I've said some horrible stuff, but I'm sober now and things are looking better.  Everything's been so much more pleasant between Lucy and me- she's still a little mad at me, sure, but I really think I can make it better.  For a while there, those drugs had me thinking I was gonna leave her.

Kane (reluctant):  You're lucky.  Any other girl would've left you by now.

When Hank and Anika first met, the universe jumped.  When he took her hand in his for the first time, all experience and the capacity of mankind took a fiery breath in the comfort of their touching hands.  Since then, Anika had been blindly convinced that no tempest could shake her Hank, because he winked like a photograph and he charmed like the devil.  But then Hank changed when he got involved with the Violet 9.  He would leave every night and he wouldn't tell her where he was going.  He changed, and he changed her.  This is what Hank recalled as he placed the red top-hat over his tangled red wig.  He knew he had changed her for good.

Kane (fixing his hand-painted eyepatch):  The more practical clothes are, the dumber they look.

Hank (tucking a red blade in his waist):  What's so practical about an eye-patch and a Jester's hat?

The pair laughed, probably for the only time since they began their open mic nights in the loft.  Hank and Kane were always trying to outdo the other, but now that Kane was finally about to deceive Hank with irreversible boldness, he was able to shed his conscience and share a laugh with the devil.  It was like a game of chess, and the opponent didn't yet realize he was in check.  Hank and Kane emerged from the alcove, fully clad in Scoundrels garb for the first time.

Dressed primly in his stolen military tunic, a treble clef epaulet on his right shoulder, a bass clef on his left, Kane Hailand's appearance was blinding.  Bells jangled from his brass cuffs, his hair was cropped to expose his ears, and the twin sides of his Baltasar Kanaan-inspired mustache were mirrored as hands preparing to pray.  His crystalline collar controlled the light spectrum as the four ears of his multi-shaded blue Jester's hat flopped to their own accord, a hand-painted eye-patch over his left eye to always be gazing into the blue infinity.  Sun King, his bluebird, perched atop his shoulder.

Hank Adaline astounded in a red three-piece suit, both breasts emblazoned with an initial- HA.  He had heavy bags under his eyes from night terrors and wrathful sermonizing.  A red top-hat floated above his skull like dust in a moonbeam.  His red wig tangled over his shoulders, a mask of red feathers spread over his beaming red eyes, fire heating the souls of his red boots, the same fire that burns within a man in a ring who thrives off the adrenaline.  A red blade was tucked neatly in his waist.

Anika:  You guys look ridiculous.

Hank:  Ridiculously awesome.

Kane:  Polly wanna cigarette?

Kane removed the cigarette from his lips and gave the bird a puff.

Anika:  Easton, is that a knife in your belt?

Hank:  Will you just relax, baby?

Anika:  You didn't tell me I'd have to sing all of this.  I've never sang anything this long before.

Hank:  Well you have to sing all of it.  Kane calculated every damn syllable.

Anika leafed through the Violet Book.  Though the ink was red and blue, it appeared inexplicably violet to Anika.

Anika:  I can't read your handwriting.  Is that a 9 or a question mark?

Kane (perusing the verse in his mind):  It's a question mark.

Anika (to Hank):  Why are you wearing purple?

Hank:  I'm wearing red- what the hell are you talking about?

Anika:  Can we just get this over with?

Kane:  Sure.  Let's head outside.

Hank:  Outside?

Kane:  Your piano's outside.  I set up a mic.  They'll hear us through the speakers.

Even when he was about to do it, Kane wasn't quite sure why he ever felt it necessary to deceive Hank.  At first, he planned to bring Hank back to reality, to sober him up and start a band.  But Hank was sober now.  Hank was sober and happy and he had the most beautiful girlfriend Kane had ever seen.  But Kane did it anyway.  He deceived Hank, because, well, just to prove that even a genius could be fooled.  It was time for something new.  The poet needed a larger outlet than the Violet 9, and Hank wasn't ready to move on.  The trio performed Train of Power- their magnum opus, their premature peak, their one perfect masterpiece.  When it came time for the finale, in which Hank was to summon a great burst of fire from the mad red piano, the heat from his fireball detonated the pipe bomb that Kane Hailand rigged in the plumbing, and every member of the Violet 9 perished in flames.

The impact of the bomb sent Hank Adaline flying from the red piano.  When he landed, the blade at his waist plunged deep into his thigh, forever damning him with a lopsided limp.

* * *

The moon was red as blood, emitting a spectral aureole onto the swirling audience.  Escorted by his supermodel companions, Hank Adaline sat at the grand red piano, wearing an eye-mask made of feathers plucked from the mythological phoenix and a red suit cut at the sleeve to expose a violet-inked tattoo of the 9 letters Anika Handel once carved to epitomize their relationship- SCOUNDREL.  His ridiculous outfit, along with everything else in the world, will no longer matter when he puts his fingers to the red piano- 999 pounds of pure sound upheld by red porcelain demons, all eighty-eight keys painted red, the closed piano-top decorated with a bed of roses that never burn but act instead like torches- Hank's mad red piano, the percussive pulse of a generation past its prime.  Scoundrels' fans unanimously exalted, much to the disdain of their younger counterparts who had come to see Hank spin behind his turntables.  This electronically-inspired younger generation had collectively downed a laboratory's worth of chemicals in preparation for their favorite DJ, and it was wrecking their buzz to see Hank at a piano.

Hank's dolled-up escorts sat on his lap, one on each leg.  Kane had never seen this stunt before.  He figured Anika was used to this by now.  Hank never made an effort to hide his extramarital affairs (he always demanded that the floors backstage be bubble-wrapped for sex), but to flaunt his promiscuity before of a crowd the size of a nation was impermissible.  The brunette on his left leg held a bottle of whiskey.  The blonde on his right leg, his lame leg, held a bottle of red wine.  A fresh keg of beer had been built into the piano.  Whiskey, Wine, and Beer- Hank's Holy Triumvirate.  The whiskey was to remind him of how much he hated himself.  The wine was to help him forget.  The beer was for the sport of it.  Hank took a sip from each bottle (hot sauce had already been added), and the audience applauded with sound-shattering energy.  He snorted a line off the girls' breasts as the crowd cheered to heighten the insanity.  Hank's mind was always at war with his body, and the drugs played both sides of the battlefield- but that's Hank, excessive Hank, sniffing cocaine off of perfect-ten tits.  Parthenos, the root word of Parthenon, means virgin, but just look at what Hank Adaline is doing at the forefront of the temple.

Fans held light-up LCD posters, screaming nonsense and setting their clothing on fire.  Years ago, Hank Adaline invented a game for international audiences to play during the concert- international fans were encouraged to tote their native flags, and by the end of the show, whichever flags hadn't been burned by fellow fans would be autographed by the Red Shadow.  The fans didn't need to fight over nationality anymore- there were those who came for the piano and those who came for the turntables.  You were either on one side or you didn't matter.  The piano fans will claim to have gotten there first, while the DJ fans will be too hungry for destruction to really give a shit about the piano fans' existence.  Kane believed that the core of the battle lay in his lyricism- the piano fans identify with Kane Hailand's dead message, while the electronic fans are the ones who killed that message.  Only Hank Adaline could speak to multiple generations so effectively, because Hank was a genius.  Hank never belonged.  He was an outsider, and his music served as a chronicle for the time in which it was composed.  Listeners identified with the time that Hank established because no one can really know who they really are until an outsider tells it to them straight.

Kane watched a particularly energetic fan rush the stage.  The Turkish Wrath Tough Squad quickly assaulted the fan.  Everybody cheered.

Hank rubbed his two fists together and cracked his knuckles, the trademark kickoff to a Scoundrels show.  On a typical piano, the fall is the part of the instrument that covers the keys when folded downward.  On the mad red piano, the fall was made of mirror.  The Red Shadow placed his fingers over the keys, snarling at himself in the mirror.  His two supermodels fed him liquor, kissing his drunken lips between swigs.  Kane Hailand could barely contain his confusion, unsure of whether to kill his brother or kiss him, buried in a sea of people, dressed in full Jester's garb, just waiting to be swept away by the piano.

The brunette slithered down Hank's lap, shocking the crowd as she bent on both knees to service the Red Shadow below the piano.  Hank set his fingers over the keys, staring into the mirrored fall- no matter what the girl did, she could never get between Hank and the music.  Many of the all-time great musical acts have played with a setlist, whether written on paper or tediously ingrained in their heads.  Hank Adaline used no setlist.  A true Rebel acts in the moment and his Art lives in the air.  The faade will crumble when Hank's fingers hit the piano.  The sex, the booze, the drugs, the red-feathered mask- all of it will become invisible, and only gory truth will be spoken.  Pay attention- it's not often we experience genius in our lifetime.

But Hank didn't play.  Instead, he lifted his fingers.  He removed the red microphone from the red mic-stand and he turned to the blonde because the brunette was busy between his legs.

Hank:  Last week, I stopped to play the Trevi Fountain.  The Italian Prime Minister- I forgot his goddamn name already- the guy invited me to some rooftop gala- fuck if I remember anything else.  So I was on that roof, about 9 floors in the atmosphere, and I became really fucking bored, you know?  I mean, shit, I don't speak Italian, and what's a guy like me got to say to any policy-maker?  So I walked over to the wall and leaped up onto the ledge.  And I just sat there, man.  I sat on that ledge, 9 floors high.  And what do you think I did next?

Hank held the microphone to the blonde's mouth, his hand shaking because his hands always shook when they were away from his instrument.  The crowd roared.

Blonde:  You looked down?

Hank:  You're brilliant, baby- A fucking plus.  I looked down.  And what did I think about when I looked down from such a wondrous height?

Blonde (borrowing the mic):  Falling?

Hank:  No, no.  I didn't think about falling.  Do you know what I thought about instead?

Blonde:  What'd you think about?

Hank:  Jumping.  I thought about jumping.  Now, why would that be my first thought?

Blonde (giggling, awkward):  I don't know.

Hank:  Do you mean to say that there's not one imaginable scenario in which you could understand my thinking?

Blonde:  You're the Red Shadow.  People love you.

The blonde raised her hands for the crowd to cheer, trying to save face under Hank's bizarre questioning.  Hundreds of thousands of souls applauded their love for Hank, but he silenced the crowd and turned back to the blonde, forgetting the crowd's existence.  He looked at the blonde and tried to understand her soul.  In melancholia, even the most playful of events are somber.

Hank:  There are two types of people.  There's your type, and there's my type.

Blonde (giggling, feeding Hank more wine):  You're a celebrity?

Hank:  No.  You're escaping the point.  Your type couldn't possibly understand how thrilling I thought it would be to jump.  Do you agree?

Blonde:  I guess so.

Hank:  But your type understands something that I'll never understand.

Blonde (giggling, more wine for Hank):  What's that?

Hank:  You understand why I didn't jump.

Kane Hailand began migrating toward the back of the stage.  His plan was to travel the outskirts of the crowd until he gained access to the rear end of the Parthenon. Once there, he would reveal his identity to the Turkish Wrath Tough Squad and gain access to the stage.  He didn't know what came next.  He was walking into an assuredly formative experience, and he didn't want to go through it without Alma.  He wished that he could speak to her- there were so many unanswered questions.  Squinting with his one uncovered eye, he spotted strange nicks and cuts on Hank's exposed skin- the markings of a stumbling drunk.  Hank used drugs and alcohol to quell the pain, to suppress emotion in a paradoxical attempt to heighten sensation whenever he snorts a line of moonbeams.

Onstage, Hank snagged the wine bottle from the blonde.  He upturned it, closing his eyes to pretend that the wine poured down his throat from the sky.  He corked the bottle, trusting it to never reveal whatever secrets he told it.

Hank looked as if he was going to play, but the blonde straddled him and threw her tongue into his mouth.  You shiver at the prospect of the girl going to the devil, but Hank will win her every time.  Rail some coke, smoke some of this, pop some of that- and wash it down, wash it all down good because what would Hank ever do if any were left behind?

Making his way through the crowd, Kane realized just how badly he needed to kill Hank.  It was no longer about humanity, no longer about Alma or Anika or even Kane himself- he just needed to put his twin out of misery.  It was a pathetic sight- the greatest genius alive on an endless mission to find out how much alcohol it will take to drown himself, drug-addled silly-stupid with synthetics.  Hank couldn't even play his piano.  Hell, Kane would have settled for the turntable at that point.  It had been fifteen minutes since Hank took the stage, and he hadn't done anything except intoxicate himself.

Somehow the crowd was still as rowdy as ever, as if their congregation alone had brought energy beyond the brinks of humanization, and they were now rooting on Hank's slow suicide.  Couldn't they see that Hank's mind and body were at war before their eyes?  His body tried to heal itself, to undo the damage of the mind that tried to kill him, and these people were encouraging war with more gusto than any spectacle has ever been cheered for.  Kane heard gossip among the fans.

Hank pulled a glass from the bench of his red piano and poured himself a beer from the tap that was built into the side of his mad red instrument.  The crowd only intensified.  The men hollered, the women tore their clothes, and everybody raised a beer to the Red Shadow.

Kane was nearing the stage, the mirrored guitar in his close clutches, Apollo strutting sneakily behind him.  This was madness.  This was inhumane.  This must end.  Hank must die.  Kane could almost feel Hank's scrawny neck between his massive hands- the life of a genius, the misguided spirit of crossed cultures, slowly vanishing in his grip.  Anika was near- he could sense her.

The supermodels were now lying in the bed of rose-torches atop the piano.  The piano played.

Music is timeless.  The reaction to music is timeless and will far outlast the grips of humanity.  As demonstrated by the Parthenon itself, it requires a staff of people to preserve history's monuments and temples, its paintings and sculptures, until the original work disappears under an uncanny suggestion of the genius it once held- but music is indestructible, alive in the veins of the listener.  Whatever questions Kane had been asking himself transformed into absolute certainties under the spell of Hank's piano.  Kane's mind drifted back into the pure ecstasy of a live show, when he and Hank explored the shallow depths of human emotion as Anika Handel yowled into the violet microphone, the world itself birthed of her mouth.  Hank was a student of his instrument, the elite, who recognized that you could melt a man's face by segueing Mixolydian into Phrygian with a minor 9.  Kane was the great conductor- the symphony of the world was and always will be the dance of his wrist, ticking the universal heartbeat.  Together, they produced a sound that wrapped not only around the listener, but around all the world, so that the whole world became theirs.

Kane followed the music, lured by the transcendent sounds of the piano.  Hank Adaline's pure improvisation was still genius no matter how many artificial stimulants were in his system.  Thus, Hank guided the crowd.

Hank (singing slowly as his hands moved automatically):  Amass Iconoclasts, I am the rhythm master.

Hank paused, took a breath, and stared into the moon.  Once a man experiences true love and true hatred, true anger and true violence, he can no longer live as he once did.  He can recall these emotions without any prompting, and they will reassume control of his being in an instant, reminding him that the simple days of innocence have long expired.  Hank peered into the moon and he let his thoughts leak through his piano.

Hank:  I cradle sweet America, weak and feeble, gasping her last in my arms.  I wonder, should I nurture her, or quicken her death and end it all?  I close my eyes, cause I don't wanna watch- or do I?  I've met many women in my life, but she is the most evocative.

Hank leaned forth and kissed the red keys of the piano.

Hank:  She always knows what I want and I always know how to give it to her.  Sometimes I love her, but most of all I hate her- now is that love?

The supermodels exited the stage, leaving the genius alone to sing his soul through the piano.  Hank's vocals, although nowhere near Anika's caliber, were strikingly honest.  Bask in the galvanizing aroma of the mad red piano.

Hank:  I dream up schemes in my make-believe world while you amuse and confuse yourself with the naivet of the youth.  But it's not the youth who is nave, it's the youth who is wise- the unheard wailing youth who knows what you've forgotten.  We're all born pure, but we mark ourselves with sin- children, never do as I have done.  Fire incinerates everything but my sins, my clinging pest sins, buzzing like flies in the empty jar of my soul, and I'm so lonely I'd rather be dead because at least the dead have company.  The only home to call home is a hole in the ground.  The mirror screams its loathing to my face.  Go ahead and smash it, a voice inside me says.

Kane waited for Hank to smash the mirror, as Kane once did, but Hank continued, fingers playing automatically.  The blonde came out with a pair of handcuffs and linked them around Hank's wrists.  He never stopped playing.  The cuffs could restrain his hands, but they could never stop his music.  Hank snarled into the mirror above his dancing hands, glaring at himself as he spoke, a prisoner to his genius. He lifted his left leg, his good leg, and began a bass-line with his toes.  The piano intensified, building in sound.  He diverted his gaze back to the endless sea of souls that were fixated on him.  Even the skeptics among them were now entrapped by the flaming red piano.

Hank:  In the night, what's dark is pure- in the day what's pure is light.  No mother to call a mother, no brother to call anything except abandonment.  You think I'm a destroyer and you adore me for it.  But you don't know me.  All you know is the image that was fabricated for me.  I am the last great sinner- a throne of fire burns in the very pits of hell just waiting to scorch me until I'm red as the day I was born.  Satan asked me how I wanna die, to which I replied I wanna melt away, and he retorted but you're already melting, don't you see, you've died without a funeral and your soul belongs to me.  Then he jumped inside my skin and stabbed me in the thigh with a crucifix.  Sinners swim in lakes of lava- lava, lava, lava.  You call me the devil.  You think you know me.  I run through you like an animal and you'll never hear my footsteps unless I decide to jump.  They say the way the devil plays is to astound you 'til you're senseless- music is my weapon and it yields you all defenseless.  You'll learn metaphorically, because that's how I talk- lyrically, I'll kill you and lay out the chalk.  This world is nothing but a glass sphere that fits in the palm of your hand.

Hank blew a miniature fireball from his palm.  He believed himself a sinner, but it was never more clear to Kane that there's no such thing as sin- there's no such thing as pure Good or pure Evil because every individual has a unique motive, and you can't consider any action as it pertains to an individual because you have to consider the individual's actions as they pertain to society as a whole.  And then it all just gets so complicated.  For once Kane understood why Hank was always frustrated.  Somehow, the sorrow that sounded from that mad red piano made it all feel better.

There's an idiomatic expression said of pianists that they tickle the ivories.  Hank doesn't tickle the ivories- he pounds them until they bleed and beg for mercy.  Allow Hank Adaline to demonstrate the power that he once used to snap a key from Queen Elizabeth's $40 million piano.

Hank:  Two lonely souls migrate toward one another, but do they speak?  No, they never speak because they're just too scared.   My only true friends are those with their names on glass bottles, the monosyllabic Americans who never lived long enough to see their selves become a myth- because I've been there, man, and I'm tired of being a myth.  I always told my woman not to smile because she didn't mean it when she smiled.  And besides, she was just too beautiful.  I never deserved that kind of beauty.  So I beat that 9-pound smile off her face and now I wonder where it is.  Whiskey, once bitter, now loses its bite.  Where O where is my despair?  Where O where am I?  Everything Hank Adaline has ever tried was out of line- everything I ever said has been a fucking lie.  Believe it.

Pounding into the keys with the untamed rage of some world beyond, Hank snapped several keys from the mad red piano and sent them soaring into the mosh pit in front of the monument.  This was a frequent occurrence (every key on the mad piano had been replaced multiple times), but the crowd frenzied regardless.  Fans dove and clawed at one another, desperate to snatch the stray artifact from the mad red piano.  Hank continued playing, unconcerned with his missing key.  The blonde unlocked his handcuffs.

Hank Adaline closed his eyes and breathed skyward, communicating silently with some presence that only he could see, lines cut into his cheeks, his jaw denoting the manifestation of pure pain.  The music lightened.  The crowd bowed to that unique hour when the sun and moon guard opposite horizons as if in duel with their own timeless reflection, and Kane Hailand understood his own presence at the Parthenon.

Though he still believed Leon to be idealistic, he couldn't ignore everything his mentor told him.  Much of what Leon had said was filtered through Alma's lips before she died, and Kane hadn't fully understood the meaning of Alma's words until he examined his brother Hank, alone among the masses that love him, the tragically misunderstood icon of sin.  Kane was the one who damned him.  He damned Hank with Train of Power.  The truth was the mirror that Kane couldn't stand to confront, that inescapable mirror.   Kane last stood at a mirror with a fistful of bloody glass and a freshly cut tattoo.  Something happened on the other side of that mirror- Kane Hailand was petrified of himself.  Alma had been telling him all along that the change he needed was to be honest with his self.  Leon said the same thing.  Kane was a broken man.  He was as broken as Hank was.  Together, they created the grandest soundscapes in the annals of time.  The only way Kane could absolve his self of his guilt was not to get rid of Hank, but to save him.  Kane was here to play the song of peace.

The Turkish Wrath Tough Squad patrolled the monument, blocking the fans from the stage.  Kane rounded the Parthenon, the leopard close behind.  He walked with confidence, loosening his fingers over the fretboard of the mirrored guitar.  Upon sight of Kane and his leopard, a guard from the Tough Squad lifted a radio to his mouth and aimed a pistol at Kane's face.  The guard mistook the Jester for a common impersonator.

Kane:  It's me.  It's Kane.

Kane walked forth calmly, the leopard behind him, staring into the muzzle.

Rory:  Do you know what we do to folks who insult the memory of The Jester?

Kane:  Rory?  Rory, it's me- Kane.

Rory (cocking the gun):  You're 9 seconds away from a lifetime of regret.

Audaciously, Kane stared through his one uncovered eye and placed his hands together as if preparing to pray.  He slowly parted his large hands, concentrating a bridged beam of light between his fingers.  Sustaining the beam between his hands, he scrunched it back and forth like an accordion.  The Accordion was one of his most famous tricks.  In Scoundrels shows, Kane would bring out his accordion of light, pretending to pass off Hank's piano as his own music while he mimed a performance to woo Anika.
Rory lowered his gun and hugged Kane.

Rory (choked up):  Where've you been, dude?  We missed you.

Kane:  I'm here now.  How can I get onstage?  I wanna surprise Hank.

Rory pointed to a roped-off passageway, and Kane shot a beam of light to confirm his path through the depleted stone of the Parthenon.

Rory (lifting a radio to his mouth):  Boys, we're in for a hell of a show.

The Parthenon is the foul-preserved birthplace of Western civilization, and for Hank Adaline and Kane Hailand it culminates at this very spot.  Kane and Apollo crept through the dark temple, climbing over ropes meant to block tourists and Scoundrels fans.

The stage crew tuned Kane Hailand's mirrored guitar and plugged it into the amplifiers.  Still backstage, plugged into the dome of sound, Kane listened to Hank's piano, deciphering the tonal language to discern which notes he should play to accentuate the music.  Hank segued into The Bride Wore Violet, a song Kane wrote about standing up at Hank and Anika's wedding.  Hank's playing sounded so sad.  It sounded like betrayal.  Pressing his middle finger into the 9th fret of the bottom string, Kane was immediately in tune with the sound.  The mirrored guitar resonated through the land.  Everyone, most notably Hank Adaline, looked to see where the sound was coming from.  Hank continued playing.  So did Kane.

The people joined in song with the piano and the guitar.  For Kane to hear strangers sing the words that he once wrote brought feelings of pure exoneration from all past failings- all of them united by the words of Kane Hailand.  Kane had fantasized a song of peace, a harmonious duet to filter all bad blood and continue as brothers.  It was fitting that he and Hank were to make peace in front of all their fans, because in so many ways everything he ever said to Hank was said through their fans in the form of song lyrics.  Kane knew, as assuredly as one knows one's self, that he had found his Anima in the guitar.  He gazed into the heavens to find Alma, and he felt her in his soul.  More than an instrument, the guitar is a mode of thought- it is an interpreter, a fundamental purpose, an Anima, and he could feel Alma in his playing.  Sing, great guitar, sing!

The crowd reveled in merriment, but Hank's piano became increasingly frustrated.  He wanted to know who it was that would dare plug a guitar into his show.

Not yet ready to expose himself, Kane sent Apollo forth as a peace offering, guiding the one-fanged leopard by reflecting tactical beams of light against the mirrored guitar toward the stage.  The crowd gasped upon sight of the leopard.  No one applauded.

Random Fan:  Get on the turntable!

Hank continued on the piano, undistracted by the heckler or by the one-fanged leopard on his stage.  Kane had no choice but to continue playing with Hank.  Hank's playing became intense and defensive.  It occurred to Kane that, as far as Hank knew, Kane couldn't play an instrument.  Still, the presence of the leopard should have made it obvious that it was Kane behind the stage.  It was time to expose his identity to his brother, to play the song of peace.  Behold the glory, two Scoundrels are to embrace and shed all former hatred at the base of the Parthenon, freezing the attention of the world.  Nerves tickling, Kane stepped onstage in full Jester's garb, playing the mirrored guitar.

The crowd released a collective gasp.

Hank peered into the mirror above his dancing hands and saw the Jester behind him, a guitar in his clutches, challenging him as he always challenged him.  Kane stood dumb with thoughts of peace.  Hank had thoughts of demolition.  Leaning into the red microphone, Hank snarled at Kane through the mirror above his hands.

Hank:  Eat my shit with a fork and knife.

Hank Adaline beat his fists into the piano, making the melody roar, accepting his challenger as prey.  Fervent fans cawed noise too loud to hear, and Hank Adaline was off in his universe of sound.

Kane wanted to explain that a battle wasn't what he was looking for, that he had come to make peace, but Hank was gone in the impenetrable Combat Sphere, the centered dome of the Rebel's thought in which his annihilation of Kane Hailand could be distracted by nothing.  Kane tried to play along on his guitar, to turn the battle music into a sacred hymn of love, but he couldn't contend with Hank's mastery.  The Red Shadow drove his fingers like a jackhammer into the piano.

All of Athens lay below, not a light lit in the city because the city was at the show.  All were silent and attentive, focused on the warring brothers.  Somehow all humanity had a stake in this battle.

Looking into their instruments, Hank and Kane's reflections bounced back and forth between the mirrored piano and the mirrored guitar, neither of them quite sure of whom was standing where.  Hank looked at Kane, into Kane, through Kane- a look cold enough to frost the sun.  Silence reigned, and the conversation passed through the eyes and not the mouth because everything the mouth could ever say is bullshit, locked in an eternal stare because all that exists is the present moment and it doesn't matter what factors contributed to this passion or the sweet violence of this moment because this. is. NOW.  Kane was everything Hank hated about himself, everything he wished he were.  This was war.  Kane Hailand will be conquered.

The orchestra produced by Hank Adaline's fingers echoed through the city.  A red shadow consumed the visible world to replace all that was tangible, all that was unreal, so that the music of Hank Adaline lay somewhere between the boundaries of what is matter and what is void, absent from your present dimension.  There is no defense against this genius because how do you attack what isn't quite there?  Hank's dexterous fingers do what normal fingers cannot, maneuvering like a well-trained army across the keys.  Thoughts in lingual form ceased to subsist and Hank's red top-hat opened as the militant sounds floated aloft in metaphysical osmosis.  All words lost meaning.  Hank's mind was an open vault, overflowing with the frantic notes of his piano.  Further, further, further Hank flew, linked to the physical world solely by means of the line thrown by his soul as it spat harmonic truths.  All feeling, all thought, and all emotion spewed from his fingers into the keyboard, directing pure hatred at the lowly Jester.  Let Kane Hailand wither and die, for the world thought he was dead once before and they moved on just fine without him.

Kane tried to redirect the music, but he felt the pings of failure in his gut.  He didn't have a prayer of redirecting the mad genius' playing because Hank was just too powerful.  But Kane Hailand came to play the song of peace, and he had traveled too far to leave without an honest attempt.  The luminary Jester dove headlong into the world of his guitar, sending aqueous blue vapor from the neck of his mirrored instrument, slithering and rising to summon the pneuma.  His thoughts surrounded Apollo like a celestial orb, and everyone knew the beast was now one with Kane.  Through the leopard, Kane tried to appeal to Hank, to make peace with his long-estranged twin.  This was to be communication in its most profound form- the sweetest cry and the most heartfelt laughter intertwined in aural climax, a great matrix of music that supported all cosmology and ethical reason.  But Hank took the leopard as a threat.  No matter what Kane tried to play, Hank found the perfect combination of notes to contort Kane's joy into sorrow, his honesty into frivolity, and his love into violence.

Kane wished he were able to use his words that he once used so effectively, but he knew that if he stopped playing for an instant then Hank would do something terrible and irreversible, because all Hank Adaline needed was an instant's weakness to obliterate you.

Hank spit a fireball toward Kane.  Kane's arm surged up in flames.  He dropped the guitar and beat the fire with his sleeve.  Hank cackled, snarling his devilish snarl in the mirror where Kane could see it.  Kane removed the burnt military tunic and resumed his instrument.

Hank stood from his red piano-bench, kicking it backward into Kane, knocking the Jester on his ass and damaging his mirrored guitar.  The crowd was silent.

Kane's music was useless.  He had no Anima- the guitar was just music, noise- sound.  It wasn't life or love or pain or joy, it was a vested simulacrum.   Kane couldn't even be honest with Hank for long enough to say the word peace.  No matter how masterful he ever became on the guitar, he would never stop Hank because Hank was just too strong.

Then Kane remembered what their mother had once told him- if there is to be a battle, Hank will win.  All Kane had to do was give his brother a battle.  He would lose, but he would lose graciously, and then he would explain his peace offering to Hank.

Hank (swigging his liquor, away from the microphone):  She told me.  She told me all about you, brother, and now I've got you where I want you.

Hank began teasing the intro to Train of Power, but even that was too low for the devil.  Police sirens wailed in the distance.  The fans were silent, too shocked to register the gravity of the moment.

Hank (into the red microphone):  You asked for a show and it's all we ever gave you.  So here's an encore, as never promised.  Please drive home safe, and do be sure to tell your friends about how I whooped Kane Hailand's monkey-ass.

Hank produced a large globe of fire and left it hovering above his piano before hurling the firebomb into the crowd.  Panic.  Mayhem.  The leopard moved to pounce, but Kane restrained the beast with the strength of his light.

A riot ensued.  Hank's fire spread through the crowd.  Some men trampled others while trying escape the fire.  Some men trampled others while trying to see the fire.  Some men trampled others while trying to escape the Turkish Wrath Tough Squad.  Some men beat others because they wore security badges.  Some men beat others because they became convinced that it was acceptable.  All men became contentious, fending for themselves.  Eat or be eaten.

The brothers continued their war in front of the temple.  Red as the devil, Hank limped over to his mad red turntables.  Wetting his fingers with liquor, Hank slid his hands over the flames of the record to create a masterful sliding sound.  The younger fans (those who weren't roasting in Hank's fire) roared their support of the mad DJ.  Yes, they rage at the Parthenon, and no, they don't care- for these are the proctors of youth.

Kane rose, charging his lightning in the mirrored guitar, his uncovered eye locked on his brother.  He paced a circle around Hank, the two brothers staring at each other all the while, just as they did in the days of the Violet 9.  All else disappeared.  The crowd, the cops, the riot, the Parthenon- all of it was invisible to the brothers.  All that mattered was destroying the opponent.  They could no longer see the rubble or the violence they inspired among the innocents.  The people fought in the crowd, believing that they were fighting for a worthy cause, although there is no cause worthy enough to violate another's freedom.

The gospel leaked unconscionably from Kane's guitar as though declaimed with honor by a mythopoeic song inside him, dancing his transcendent dance with Hank.  He shot lightning through the neck of his guitar, desperate to incinerate Hank's turntables.

Hank was a red demon clawing transcendent death with rapacious talons, fueling the fire of a thousand deaths, spinning his records with red flashing eyes.

Kane looked into the sky, spotting hints of both the sun and moon.  He was going to do the impossible.  Set the sun- because, despite his former disillusions, the world never really did revolve around Kane Hailand.  In his Scoundrel days, Kane Hailand may have been able to set the sun.  As a Scoundrel, he was significantly more powerful than he was now, recovering from months of absence, injured by Hank's fire.  To set the sun, Kane would need to tap into the knowledge he acquired as a bookish orphan.

Though he was never able to move a body as large as the sun, Kane knew that by turning the earth at a fast enough rate, he can create the illusion that the sun was setting- this is the illusion of day and night that is created naturally through the constant rotation of earth.  Kane also knew that the moon's gravitational energy was causing the earth to slow its rotation so that in millions of years, a day on earth will last 25-26 hours.  If Kane Hailand could steal the energy of the moon, the earth will spin faster and the sun will set.  In the days of The Scoundrels, Kane was the sun and Hank was the moon.  Kane had changed too much since then, but Hank hadn't done much changing- Hank still fed off the moon's fiery glow.  To tap into the energy of the moon, Kane would need to tap into the energy of Hank Adaline, and the only way he could distract the genius enough to tap into his energy was to play the Chord of Creation.

Kane recalled Alma's instructions.  His fingers were loose.  His large hands were limber enough for maximum flexibility.  He began from the beginning, as Alma taught him, placing the third finger of his left hand over the twelfth fret of the top string, letting his other fingers slowly spread over the mirrored guitar.  With his thumb bracing the back of the guitar, the four fingers of Kane's left hand couldn't stretch to stab the notes on the bottom two strings, and so he stopped picking the strings with his right hand and moved both hands to the fretboard.  All six notes locked on the fretboard, Kane didn't have a free hand to strum the strings.  Hank looked up from his turntables, laughing to mock Kane's ridiculousness.

Hands locked to launch into the Chord of Creation, all Kane needed to do was strum the strings and sustain the chord while bending each note a half-step.  But his fingers were so stiff in this contorted position that he couldn't force the strings to budge.  The Chord would require another hand.  Kane looked to Hank Adaline, who was fading back and forth between 9 of the Devil's records to stack his sound in tritones.

Kane:  You know the chord- play it with me!

The cops tried to unplug the stage equipment, but the Turkish Wrath, who traveled with enough artillery to ensure that the show and its surrounding riot will continue, battled them away.

Hank:  You know what your problem is, Kane?  You've always been just two lips short of a twat.

Hank summoned a surge of fire from the top of the red turntables.

Kane summoned Apollo, hands prepped for the Chord of Creation.  He guided the leopard to strum the strings with its one fang, light reflecting off its mirrored spots as the six notes of the guitar sang through the land.  All Kane had to do was bend the strings up a half-step, but he couldn't summon the strength in his hands.  The leopard kept strumming with his one fang.

The flames from Hank's turntables grew higher into the night.  Kane gazed into Hank's face in the mirror below the genius's hands.  Hank flashed his red eyes.  He winked.

Hank was helping Kane.  The Red Shadow was playing half of the Chord of Creation- he just overlapped certain notes that Kane was playing, leaving it to Kane to figure out the rest.  Hands cramped, Kane lifted his fingers from the fretboard to begin again.  He had never played the Chord this way, and he didn't know what notes would complete its sound.  But he did know Hank, so he listened to Hank's spinning as he always listened to Hank's piano because Hank's music gave life to every word Kane ever wrote, and it didn't matter that Hank had converted his gift to a new instrument because it was time to return the favor.  Kane listened to Hank spin that record, and suddenly he understood why the youth had clung to Hank's new sound.  The music needed no message because the message was in the people.  The music needed no content- it needed pulse and drive and power.  This was transcendence, and transcendence has no message.  The old have forgotten, but the youth still remember- Anika and Alma were always so attached to the youth because they realized that the youth was so precious.  The youth know something, and although they'll forget it tomorrow, they remember today.

Kane picked each note of the Chord of Creation, one by one, building the sound like a musical Babel.  Tapping into the energy of the moon, Kane Hailand amassed all light inside his being.  He had complete control, separating particles from waves while guiding all photons.  He hit the crowd with an infrared wave, bending and refracting at will.  Before anyone could realize what happened, the infrared had disappeared into an invisible ultraviolet because Kane Hailand presides over you when you don't even notice him.

The moon, once glowing blood-red through the eclipse in the sky, began to wither.  The energy amassed in Kane's mirrored guitar, flowing through his body and the body of Apollo.  With Kane's two hands occupied, Kane strummed the strings against Apollo's one fang.  The world shook.  All the world and everything inside it- the land, the plants, the animals, the men and all their hopes and products, their fears, and their history of conflict- shook and spasmed as the sun began to rise.

The sky lit red and a beaming disc of light shone on the eastern horizon, affront the Parthenon where the riot had momentarily ceased to observe this most preternatural of phenomena, for the darkness of night had lasted no more than an hour.  The sun continued to rise as Kane played his guitar, channeling all energy into the turning of the earth, defying the nature of physics and time, breaking all laws and all notions of history and aesthetics as only the truest of artists, the Rebel, can do.

The sun hit its zenith, high above the land, beaming down to light all of Athens in the clear blue sky.  But Kane Hailand was not done.  He kept playing, riffing on the Chord of Creation, and the world kept turning as the sun descended rapidly and Hank spun his vinyl, coloring the sky until it faded and disappeared into a small bow behind the temple on the western horizon.  Darkness reigned once again.  The land echoed silence.  The riot paused, all eyes affixed to Kane Hailand, who set the sun.

Hank's eyes flashed red.  He lifted his fingers from the turntables, smothering the fire.  The world reveled in the quiet.  Then Hank traded silence for music.

With a great surge of flames, Hank Adaline set the Parthenon, and all of its surroundings, ablaze.

* * *

Track 9: What Could Kane Hailand Have Tattooed on his Forehead? Reprise


Wildfire scorched the land, spreading flames over all the Acropolis.  Those fortunate souls who survived Hank's initial blast shed all inhibitions and all practiced customs to play part in total chaos.  They ran in every direction because no direction was safe.  They cursed.  They drank.  They beat total strangers.  Trapped in the moment of mayhem, the people hadn't yet considered the amazing possibility presented to them when Hank Adaline burned all of history to mix a cocktail of tumult, uncertainty, and confusion.  Chaos was the possibility of beginning anew- everybody always talks about starting over, and there they were, at the zero-coordinate, the point of creation.  Destruction, you see, can be a beautiful means to creation.  Though the world no longer had the privilege of examining the material ruins of the Parthenon, they were left with the true substance of the Parthenon's existence- the knowledge and wisdom acquired from years of excavation.  Of course, with Hank's fire still rolling over the city, with mobs still stampeding, still fighting for survival, fighting the police who were supposed to be protecting the very laws that were implemented to secure the peoples' survival, the records had yet to show how many casualties resulted from Hank's fire-fueled whims.

In a weary dream-state, Kane thought of Leon.  Leon would have disagreed with Hank's method on a fundamental level because he didn't believe destruction could ever cause reform.  But Hank wasn't looking for reform.  Hank would say that he had no method because he had no objective.  If you asked Hank to justify his actions, he wouldn't be able to- he wouldn't consider justification something to be desired.  Hank did what he did because it was something to do.  The essential difference between Hank and Leon was not the fact that Hank became an immediate agent of change- the difference was that Leon followed a moral code while Hank had no such obligation.  Leon believed in the order of true peace- Hank believed in the chaos of true drink.

Leaning against a cracked marble column, Kane Hailand awoke to the roaring heat of the fire.  He adjusted his eye-patch and rubbed his uncovered eye.  Smoke and fire burned high all around him, heating his skin.  Blown away in the explosion, the Jester's hat was cooking in the crackling flames.  Hank appeared in a cloud of smoke.

Hank:  We shall write?

Kane Hailand stood, confused.

Kane:  What do you mean?

Hank:  You fucked up the R.

Kane (a pause):  I- what?

Hank:  We shall write- on your forehead- you fucked up the R.

Kane put a finger to his tattooed forehead.  Although still dazed from the explosion and the overall absurdity of his current situation, it suddenly occurred to Kane Hailand that WE SHALL WRITE were the mutilated words that he emblazoned on his forehead just lifetimes ago.

Hank:  I've done some stupid shit in my day- hell, you know better than anybody- look, I don't know where you've been and I don't know who you've been partying with, but you've gotta introduce me to these people.  I've never seen anyone tattoo their forehead, man, that' some mythical shit.

Kane attempted to speak, still stunned.  He once believed that if he ever solved the mystery of his own tattoo, he would have discovered his own divine beckon.  Now that the mystery was unlocked and simply stated, there was still no sense of closure because the words we shall write meant absolutely nothing to Kane Hailand.

Hank:  What kind of guy would I be if I didn't complement you on learning guitar?  That was adorable, Kane, thinking you could challenge me.  But hey, at least you made yourself useful onstage.  Oh sweet Satan, it's backwards- double-points for a backwards tattoo!  You've really outdone yourself, you know that?

Kane (rubbing his head, slouching):  Can you just cool it for a moment?

Hank:  You tattooed your fucking forehead and you expect me not to give you shit for it!

Kane:  I'm asking you not to.

Hank silently mimicked his brother.  Kane heard, but for once he suppressed a retort.  He was here to make peace, and now that he had finally earned Hank's attention he had no idea what to say.  In many human relationships, the people involved become more cryptic as time progresses- they learn to code their language because they believe that their partner should know them well enough, and become in tune with their person enough, to perceive their true intentions without ever saying anything aloud.  But Hank and Kane once lived and developed inside the same womb, and they were born cryptic.  In the days of the Violet 9, they carried four-hour discussions in which they only raised one or two ideas.  They had to be cryptic because they had to protect themselves from each other in life's field of war.  If Hank ever learned of Kane's vulnerabilities, or vice-versa, he would find a way to use it against him.  It was time to cut the shit and end the war.  It was time to be honest.  But what words could possibly nullify a lifetime of war?

Kane removed the leopard's fang from his neck.

Hank:  Nice tooth.

Kane:  It was always my dream to learn an instrument.  I wanted to beat you.  I didn't want to need you any longer.  It's not gonna happen, and I've learned to accept that.  I'm done with music, done with the noise.  I don't want to be a Scoundrel anymore.

Kane offered the leopard's fang to Hank.

Hank:  I don't want your gifts.

Kane:  I can't apologize to you.

Hank:  I don't want your apology.

The flames flickered high, surrounding the brothers.  Stones crashed inside the ancient monument.  Hank and Kane fled the fire to speak in the relative safety of the downhill brush.  Once dark and lifeless, the city below was now teeming with squad cars and rioting citizens.

Kane:  Leon would be so ashamed.

Hank:  Who the fuck is Leon?  Look, Mom told me you were the one they gave away.  It was you.

Hank pulled a wrinkled photograph from his red suit-pocket.  He showed the picture to Kane.  Stained with hot sauce and red wine, it was the same picture Kane had always carried, the two of them as infants, wearing white, Kane gripping Hank's leg.

Hank:  She said a mother always recognizes her child.

Kane:  Hmmph.  Some mother.

Hank (chuckling):  Can't argue with you there- the bitch is loony.  After you left she filed a lawsuit against me, claiming public defamation for Satan's Blues.

Kane:  You didn't even write that- I did.

Hank:  She doesn't care.

Hank finally looked at the leopard's fang in his palm, jaw hung low.  After careful examination, he placed the fang around his neck.  He paused to look at his shaking fingers- his fingers always shook when they were removed from an instrument.

Hank:  It doesn't make sense, though- when we met back in college, you were a year ahead of me in school-

Kane:  I skipped third grade.

Hank:  This is too much.  I need a fucking drink.  Why are you here, Kane?  What are you doing?

Kane:  I'm done with that name- Kane.  Call me Jake.

Hank:  Jake?   You're Jake now?

Kane:  I've always been Jake.  That's how Alma knows me.

Hank:  Who the fuck is Alma?  What reality are you living in?

Kane:  I don't wanna hide who I am any longer.

Hank:  I don't suppose you want to be called Jake Israele?  I mean, after all, you were born an Israele.

Kane:  I'm Jake Israele.

Hank:  You're Jake Israele?

Hank removed his red-feathered mask.  There were shadows under his eyes.  There was darkness in his soul.  He found a flask stashed inside his top-hat.  He downed it.

Kane:  Where is she?

Hank's eyes grew big.  Before Kane could say anything else, Hank launched a sprint toward the burning Parthenon.  Kane Hailaind followed his twin, clambering up the hill toward the blazing fire, too focused on following Hank's bare feet to anticipate how he'd react when he saw Anika.  She was dying when he left her.  He replaced her with another woman and she never even had the comfort of knowing that he had a pulse.  Now he was to see her again, after their longest absence, reunited in front of her husband, his newly acknowledged brother.

Hank ducked under collapsed columns, pulling his red suit-collar over his mouth to shield his breathing from the smoke.  Kane followed.  He tripped over a flaming root, regained his footing, and removed his eye-patch for balanced vision.  Moving as fast as his legs would take him, he followed Hank to rescue Anika.

Hank stopped before the mad red piano, his lame leg numb after the short sprint.  Flames soared into the black sky, yet the fireproof piano remained unscathed.  The scorched corpses of Hank's two supermodel companions were roasting in the fire on top of the piano.  He rolled the bodies off and attempted to lift the top of the piano, that famous red piano-top that always held a bed of roses that never burned but acted instead like torches.  It was too heavy.  Kane dashed to help.  Together, they opened the piano.  Kane looked for Anika inside the instrument, never once considering it odd that she would be hiding in a piano because scoundrels are capable of anything.  She wasn't there.  She had escaped.

Hank removed a violet jug from the red-painted brass bottom of the piano.  He hugged the jug to his breast and kissed it with tenderness uncharacteristic of the Red Shadow.  He turned back for another beer and then walked calmly through the fire as Kane followed, dumbstruck.  The flames roared, but Hank and Kane were safe.

Hank (handing the violet jar to Kane):  Hold this for a second.

Hank bit the glass rim of his beer, unzipped his red fly, and pissed over a miniature fire as he tipped his head back to drink.  When alas he had shaken the last drop, and the last of his beer had disappeared down his throat, he dropped the glass in the heated sand.

Hank:  We thought you were dead.  A busted mirror and a sink full of blood- that's taking it a bit far, Kane- Jake- whoever you are.  Anika lost it.  She wanted to fly out to the goddamn Middle East when we found out you bought a one-way ticket- probably sent her to an early grave.

Some part of Kane had known that Anika was dead.  How could he not know?  He was the one who left her for dead.  He felt different now that he could no longer deny it, and he couldn't react to this difference because he couldn't yet gauge what it was.  He tried to think of how Alma would react.  She was always so composed.  It pained him to think that Anika was dead, but then he felt guilty for feeling pain for anyone but Alma.  He couldn't shake the image of Anika from his head.  He thought of her as she was before she was Anika- Lucy Liber, the church girl in the white dress, virginal and pure.  Kane wanted to feel love, as he knew Alma would, but all he could feel was guilt and anger because he and Hank had turned Anika into a scoundrel and then killed her.

Kane:  Why didn't you help her?  Why weren't you there?  You were her husband.

Hank:  Get off your tower, you self-righteous hack.  You knew what you were doing when you left.  You knew she wasn't seeing a doctor!

Kane:  She didn't care if I stayed or went.

Hank:  For someone who used to be so smart, you're a fucking brainless nugget of shit.

Kane:  You vowed to be there for her, in sickness and in health.  But you were never there- not even in the beginning.  She was in the church choir and you took her away.  She wore a white dress!

Hank:  You're still angry over that?  I had to do it.  I had to make her feel.  You weren't there when I gave her joy.  You never saw how I made her feel like the only woman alive.  You only saw the shit.  But I had to do it, and you're just as guilty as I am.  You knew what I was doing and you never stopped me.  We did it for the music.  How could she sing despair if she never felt it?  How could she sing love if she never knew hate?  We needed the complete spectrum, and that's the only way it would've ever worked.  She couldn't feel the music until I broke her heart, until I taught her how to break hearts.  I may be the biggest scoundrel of the three of us, but you've got one thing wrong- I was never in competition with you.  I loved her.  It was never about you.

Kane breathed the taste of soot in his mustache.  The firelight flickered over his face.

Kane:  Alone in Myth- why wouldn't you record it?

Hank:  Because it scared me.

Kane:  What?

Hank:  You were turning into me.  You were letting her do to you what you did to me.

Kane:  What did I ever do to you?

Hank:  You broke my heart.  I used to have one, you know.

Kane:  With Train of Power?

Hank:  What?

Kane hiccuped, trying to mask his verbal blunder.

Kane:  Let's go, the fumes are getting to my head.

Hank's eyes flashed red.  His red suit was tattered and burned and he stood barefoot in the hot gravel.

Hank:  I asked you what you're talking about.

Kane:  What are you talking about, Hank?  How did I break your heart?

Hank:  Tell me right fucking now what you know about Train of Power!

Kane:  What do you think happened?  I rigged it.  I wired the bomb through the holes in the ceiling.

Hank searched his hat for more liquor.  Finding nothing, he checked his suit- there were only empties.  He cursed himself for walking barefoot because shoes and socks could have provided him an opportunity to stash more drugs on his person.

Hank:  Gimme that urn.

Hank grabbed the violet urn.  Anika Handel, the cigarette queen, was now a mound of ashes- it was all so fitting.  Kane tried to remain calm, though the overload of recent information brought his brain to the point of near-explosion.  He felt Alma's presence inside him and it soothed him.  He felt strength, however trying it may be.

Kane:  It was selfish of me.  I did it because I envied you.  I spent so much time hating you, and it was all because of my own insecurities.  I just want to be friends now.  I can be friends now.

Hank:  It was my first time performing for anybody other than you or mom and dad.  I sat at that beautiful red piano and I was so proud, man, I was really proud of something.  I never felt that before.  Everything had always been handed to me, and that song was the first thing I ever earned.  I read your lyrics and I turned them into music, every goddamn note, and I did it by myself.  I think about it every day, man.  She came late (he looked at the urn), but she always knew how to make an entrance.  She sang.  That voice could fluff pillows and knock down walls in the same note.  Just to play the sound behind that voice was the greatest gift a musician could ever strive for.  I played, Annie sang, and what did you do, my dear brother?  You waited until my grand finale, the ending that you told me you wrote specially for me, and you blew up the whole goddamn loft.  We put our hearts into the Violet 9.  That song was supposed to be for them.  All of them- dead!  And you made me believe it was my fault.

Hank wept.  Kane shook.  He had never seen feeling in his brother.

Hank:  I loved that place, man.

Kane was wrong and he knew it, but he couldn't apologize.  He couldn't apologize because he didn't mean it.  It was as Leon said, if a man is content with his current direction, then he cannot regret his past.  Kane was far from content, but he was on a path toward something new, and he wanted to take Hank along with him.  He placed his hand on his brother's shoulder.  The smoke drifted from the burning city.  Hank and Kane smelled searing flesh for the first time since Train of Power.

Hank:  I needed it.  I admit it.  I needed it for the same reason I broke Anika's heart.  Our broken hearts enabled us.  You broke my heart.  I broke hers.  But when she broke your heart, you lost it.

Kane:  What do you mean?

Hank:  You were stuck in your ways.  In order to grow as a man, as an artist, a Rebel, you need to be open to change.

Kane:  I wasn't open to change?

Hank:  You wanted interludes on every album we ever made.

Kane:  So?

Hank:  Nobody listens to interludes anymore.

Kane:  They're an essential part of the album.

Hank:  Your album is dead!

Kane began to speak, but stopped himself.  He had always judged his own success by what others thought of his art.  He relied on others to make him feel good about who he was, but he never stopped to consider how to make others happy.  He never thought about how to please his fans or his band-mates- he only thought about how he could manipulate them into pleasing him.  The logic was cyclical, and it never allowed Kane to believe in his self.  That's why he never accepted Hank- how can a man accept anything without first finding peace in his self?

Kane:  I met a woman when I left.  She helped me understand a lot of things that I always took for granted.  I'm not the genius you are.  I'm not as strong as you or as naturally talented as you.  But I understand you finally.  We have to put our instruments down.

Hank pointed up toward the burning Parthenon, where his mad red piano and his turntables were engulfed in flames.

Hank:  If you think I'm going to live a day without my music then you don't understand the first thing about me.  That music is my only friend.

Kane:  I understand that.  But you can't use it as a weapon.  Just smell the air.  Listen to the streets right now.  There are sirens.  People are screaming, Easton.  All of this is happening because we used the music as a weapon.  We're not ready to handle it responsibly-

Hank:  I have a better idea- why don't you lick the backside of my nut-sack?

Kane:  I get it, Easton.  I understand.  I know how it feels to be deceived.  I know what I put you through, what I'm still putting you through.  I know it, because I finally felt it myself.  I'm a better man for it.  I'm thankful.

Hank:  So am I- I'm thankful.  I'm even thankful for you.  But I just hate you.  You didn't have to be such a dick about everything.

Kane:  Maybe we'll never see eye to eye.  That's okay.  We can still learn to be friends.  I think it's worth us learning to be friends.  It's no one's fault, but we're different.  You're my brother, Easton, and we were separated for a while, but we're together now and we can't ignore our relation any longer.  I thought I could ignore you by moving away, but it was impossible.  People know us everywhere we go- the world has become too small for us to avoid a relationship.  We need to learn to live together.

Kane placed his hand on the violet urn.

Kane:  I've made peace with everything that happened.  With you.  With Anika.  All three of us.  Anika was so amazing.  She was a valuable presence in both of our lives, but she never meant the same thing to me as she did to you.  The way she affected me was special in my own way.  It took me a while to learn that.  I was just too much of a coward to watch her die while knowing that we were the ones who corrupted her.  I was scared.  I felt too guilty to say goodbye.

Hank:  It was pretty, man.  It was a wonderful way that she went.  She wasn't tortured.  She was able to escape the violet, the 9's.  It was just me and her.  It was happy.

Kane smiled, removing his hand from the urn.  The sun appeared on the horizon and the sky was still gray with smoke.  The sun rose at a rapid pace.  Sirens wailed.  People cried in the distance.

Hank:  I think you fucked up the calendar for good with that stunt you pulled on the sun.

Kane:  Let's get out of this heat.

Hank observed the chaos below.  Cop cars blocked every intersection.  The tanks were coming out.  The only sounds were those of screaming and crying.  Nobody remembered what they were fighting for, but the general attitude seemed to suggest that, once fighting, what reason could there ever be to stop?

Hank:  You've caused quite a bit of damage tonight.  I'm actually proud of you for once.

Kane stood in the smoky sun, mustached and tattooed, wearing only pants, boots, and an eye-patch.  He removed the mirrored eye-patch and crushed it beneath his boot.  He had spoken truth, and it was a fantastic relief, because now he could finally begin to confront his own failings.

Kane:  They're gonna come looking for us.

Hank ditched his red suit jacket in the sand.  The brothers walked south, away from the city and the riots, traveling silently, side by side.  Hank's limp had improved.

Hank:  I knew you rigged the bomb.

Kane:  What?  How?

Hank:  I saw you reading about it when I was composing.  You weren't as sneaky as you thought.

Kane:  Why'd you go through with it?

Hank:  Why'd you?

They reached the parking lot pavement.  The lot had been looted and destroyed.  What few cars remained had been piled and burnt.  Kane stopped walking.

Kane:  What made you stick with me?

Hank:  I thought we could be great.

Kane:  Then how come you broke up the band?  Don't say it's because I was turning into you because I know that's not what scared you.

Hank:  You're right.

Kane:  So what was it?  We had such a good thing going.  Why'd you become a DJ?

Hank:  You were fucking my wife, Jake.

Kane put a hand to his mustache, stung with surprise.

Kane:  I thought you knew.

Hank:  Not until she told me.

Kane:  What reason was that to break up the band- you were always cheating.

Hank:  Yeah, but I never cared for any of those girls.  I didn't care if she fucked other people.  I just cared if she fucked you.  You were the one person who was off limits, and she knew that.

Kane:  Why me?

Hank:  Because she cared for you.

Hank was right.  Kane knew it.  Anika always made it a point to be hypersexual with Kane.  She used her sexuality to mask her inner feelings, but there were always those moments.  Sometimes it would gleam through her eyes, sometimes it would be in the sweet rasp of her voice, and there would always be that emotional moment backstage in Paris when she spoke honestly and freely without the heavy burden that Hank and Kane built to imprison her.  No matter what happened between Kane and Anika, there was always spite between them, because on some basic level they were only with each other to get to Hank.  Standing nearly naked in the humid Acropolis parking lot, everything became so clear to Kane, and he wondered how he was ever able to avoid such a simple truth for so long.  She was gone, and he would never be given an opportunity to confess his guilt to her- such is the way of lost lovers.

Hank:  I know what you think of me, but I really loved her.

A squad car turned into the lot.  Hank blew up the car with a quick spray of fire.

Kane:  You can't do that!  Just stop with the violence!  Please.  Stop killing people.

Hank:  I'm going to tell you something.

Kane huffed, frustrated with the chaos and the death, knowing just how dismayed Leon was going to be when he read about Kane's behavior at the Parthenon.

Kane:  What?

Hank:  All that talk about suicide- I never really meant it.  Well, not to that extent.

Kane:  I know.

Hank:  And then she died.  I couldn't take it.  I didn't want to live another second without her.

Hank stopped, visibly emotional.  He pulled a joint from somewhere near the small of his back, lit it with his fingertips, and inhaled deeply.  It was difficult for Kane to actually care about what Hank was saying because Hank's alleged confession lacked gravity when compared to the more recent news of Alma and Anika's deaths.

Hank:  I've never really said this before.  I've tried to not even think about it.

Kane plucked the joint from Hank's lips and squashed it under his heel.

Kane:  I know.

Hank:  I loaded the gun and put it to my head.  I wanted to pull the trigger.  I really did.  I wanted to.  But I couldn't do it, and it wasn't because I wanted to live.  It was because I forgot that I was living.  Do you know what I'm saying?

Kane:  You forgot you were alive.

Hank:  Exactly!  Do you realize how strange it is when you remember something like that?

Kane nodded.

Hank:  I was sitting there with her gun at my temple and all I could think about was when she shot that very gun at me in Carnegie Hall.

Kane (laughing):  You passed out in the middle of a show.

Hank:  So? I was still playing- it hardly warranted a bullet.

Kane:  It was quite a spectacle.

Hank:  Anyways, I had her gun in my ear and what I was thinking was how amazing is that?  Out of all the girls I could've possibly gotten, I got the one who will produce a firearm onstage in a sold-out theatre without giving a semblance of a fuck for any of the rich bastards in the crowd.

Kane:  You're richer than any of those rich bastards that were in that crowd.

Hank:  I'm a bigger bastard too.

Kane:  That's what I'm saying, though.  We have to make some changes.

Hank:  I don't have to do shit.

Kane:  Everyone you hang out with is a junkie.

Hank:  You fail to see their finer qualities.

Kane:  They keep you on drugs, Easton.

Hank:  You say you wanna make amends, but all you're doing is fucking criticizing me.

Hank stooped to examine a beaten sedan in the neighboring aisle.

Hank:  Do you know how to wire a car?

Kane:  Wire a car?

Hank:  How else are we gonna get out of here?

Hank and Kane followed a dirt road because it seemed to lead to the least-riotous direction.  Hank limped slightly, barefoot with a leopard's fang around his neck.  Without his showy suit or his eye-mask, he actually looked human.

The two brothers heard tires screech.  A limousine halted beside them.  Johnny-John lowered his window.

Johnny-John:
Sorry, Sirs, that I am late-
The traffic was a chore.
You must believe me when I say
The streets are streets no more.

Kane:  How'd you know to come here?

Johnny-John handed Kane a note in Leon's handwriting- Just in case you need a getaway car- L.  The note was attached to a small stack of Euro and a falsified passport that contained a picture of Kane Hailand circa the Lightspeed tour.

Johnny-John (wiping sweat from his brow):
I've never been one to voice requests,
I usually roll with the tide.
But would you mind taming your one-fanged pest-
He's followed me all through the ride.

Apollo approached from behind the limo.  Kane rubbed the mirror-spotted leopard between the ears.  Hank gripped the fang at his neck.

Hank:  Can I touch him?

Kane:  Go ahead.

Shielding the urn from the feline, Hank placed a hesitant finger on the crown of the leopard's head.  Kane understood the offer of trust- the DJ had strict rules about whom or what he would expose his fingers to.  Kane opened the limousine door for Apollo.  The leopard climbed in.  Hank and Kane followed.

Kane:  Where are we headed, Johnny?

Johnny-John recited a poem about the airport, speaking for no one because Kane closed the window to allow privacy.

Hank:  Who wrote the note to Johnny?

Kane:  Do you remember Baltasar Kanaan?

Hank:  The dude you obsessed over in Light Shattered- offed himself, didn't he?

Kane:  Not exactly.

They rode in silence.  Both Hank and Kane were deep in thought, too frightened to speak for fear that fresh ideas would be misguided when converted into speech.  Kane thought of Alma.  He thought of Anika's death, of how Hank said it was a happy way to go, and this made Kane feel so much better.  He wanted to share everything he experienced in the wild, but the feelings inside him coagulated into something like stone, and it was too dense to chisel into words.

Kane:  I never really gave your electronic music a chance, but I gotta say- it's real.

Hank:  How immature of you.  I'm flattered.

Kane:  You connect to the audience.  Your music helps them connect to each other when you want it to, but when you want to see a riot you're capable of more ugliness than any man I know.

Hank reached into the mini bar and found a red wine cooler.  He uncorked the bottle and took a sip.  A sip turned into a pull, and soon the bottle was cashed.

Hank:  So I was sitting there with her gun to my head.  She was gone.  It was just me and her gun, and I thought about her firing that very pistol in Carnegie Hall, and it was like, I don't know, it was like I was still talking to her even though she was dead.  I was sober, too, mind you- you don't believe me.

Kane:  Of course I do.

Hank:  Well, I had all these plans.  I was gonna write a will.  I was gonna have our ashes mixed together.  All this shit.  But then I realized that she's better off this way, without me.  I never let her be at peace when she was alive.  She at least deserves it now that she's dead.

Kane:  I think we're gonna find that we have more in common than we ever thought.

Hank:  There you go again, being all cryptic.

Kane:  We both have our problems, Easton.  I know you can help me through mine, and I'm confident that I can help you through yours.

Hank:  Alright.  Just don't get so fucking giddy about it.  If I wanna take drugs, then get off my case.  If I wanna DJ, then let me fucking spin.  Don't get in the way of me and myself.  And don't ever rub it in that you were fucking my wife.

Kane:  Why would I do that?

Hank:  I'm serious.  I'd skin you, motherfucker.

The leopard snarled.  Hank snarled back.  Kane laughed.  The two brothers looked out their respective windows.  The land was still, the city rioting behind them.  If Kane ever looked back, he would have seen cars burning in the streets.  He would have seen the broken glass and the tear gas of the looting mobs- he would have heard the silent screams of those who were faced with the question of capability- what are you capable of as a man?  Who are you capable of besting?  Do you save your belongings or do you save another if you're lucky enough to be given the choice?  How far will you go to protect your children from the terror?  How far will your greed take you?  But Kane didn't look back.  Kane watched the scenery.

Kane:  Johnny, stop the car!

Johnny-John skidded to the shoulder.  Kane nodded to a lone violet placed oddly in the sand to mark what looked to be a freshly dug grave.  Though the sun was high, there was a mystic breeze that surrounded the violet, vivifying the flower on a patch of land where all else seemed dead.  Kane opened the limousine door and let the breeze flow into the car.

Kane:  No one will ever find her here.  She'll finally be free.

Hank lowered his gaze and looked guardedly to his brother, questioning whether Kane was actually suggesting what Hank thought he was suggesting.  Hank hugged the urn close to his red vest.  He was sweating.  For once he looked vulnerable.

Hank:  It's so hot in here.

Hank moved slowly out the door.

Hank:  Are you coming?

Kane:  I'm done standing between you and her.

Hank nodded absently.  He wasn't there.  Kane knew that Hank wasn't there because wherever Hank was, Kane had been there.  Apollo nuzzled in Kane's lap and Kane stroked the one-fanged leopard.  His eyes remained fixated on Apollo's mirrored spots, avoiding a look at Hank because Hank deserved to be alone for this.

Hank approached the flower.  He never felt alone.  The remains of Anika Handel were in his hands.  The world knew her as the greatest contralto in the history of sound, an incessant smoker, a sex-sparked maniac who kept a hot weapon at her waist, the Quaquaversal, but most of all she was the voice that people turned to when they needed to rely on anything, a violet.  To Hank she was the only thing worth staying on earth for.  When he came home at five in the morning, shivering in the rain, she was the one who welcomed him into the warmth.  When he walked into the swimming pool, fully clothed and fully loaded to the point where he no longer remembered where he was, she was the one who placed her hand in his and granted him the marvelous gift of awareness.  She was Hank's love, his life and his flower.  And she lay in an urn, in his trembling hands, where she had always been- her prison.
